## PR descriptions & discussion

### #372 — chore(deps-dev): update mypy requirement from <2,>=1 to >=1,<3 [OPEN]
Updates the requirements on [mypy](https://github.com/python/mypy) to permit the latest version.
<details>
<summary>Changelog</summary>
<p><em>Sourced from <a href="https://github.com/python/mypy/blob/master/CHANGELOG.md">mypy's changelog</a>.</em></p>
<blockquote>
<h1>Mypy Release Notes</h1>
<h2>Next Release</h2>
<h2>Mypy 2.1</h2>
<p>We’ve just uploaded mypy 2.1.0 to the Python Package Index (<a href="https://pypi.org/project/mypy/">PyPI</a>).
Mypy is a static type checker for Python. This release includes new features, performance
improvements and bug fixes. You can install it as follows:</p>
<pre><code>python3 -m pip install -U mypy
</code></pre>
<p>You can read the full documentation for this release on <a href="http://mypy.readthedocs.io">Read the Docs</a>.</p>
<h3>librt.vecs: Fast Growable Array Type for Mypyc</h3>
<p>The new <code>librt.vecs</code> module provides an efficient growable array type <code>vec</code> that is
optimized for mypyc use. It provides fast, packed arrays with integer and floating point
value types, which can be <strong>several times faster</strong> than <code>list</code>, and tens of times faster
than <code>array.array</code> in code compiled using mypyc. It also supports nested <code>vec</code> objects and
non-value-type items, such as <code>vec[vec[str]]</code>.</p>
<p>Refer to the <a href="https://mypyc.readthedocs.io/en/latest/librt_vecs.html">documentation</a> for
the details.</p>
<p>Contributed by Jukka Lehtosalo.</p>
<h3>librt.random: Fast Pseudo-Random Number Generation</h3>
<p>The new <code>librt.random</code> module provides fast pseudo-random number generation that is
optimized for code compiled using mypyc. It can be 3x to 10x faster than the stdlib
<code>random</code> module in compiled code.</p>
<p>Refer to the <a href="https://mypyc.readthedocs.io/en/latest/librt_random.html">documentation</a> for
the details.</p>
<p>Contributed by Jukka Lehtosalo (PR <a href="https://redirect.github.com/python/mypy/pull/21433">21433</a>).</p>
<h3>Mypyc Improvements</h3>
<ul>
<li>Enable incremental self-compilation (Vaggelis Danias, PR <a href="https://redirect.github.com/python/mypy/pull/21369">21369</a>)</li>
<li>Make compilation order with multiple files consistent (Piotr Sawicki, PR <a href="https://redirect.github.com/python/mypy/pull/21419">21419</a>)</li>
<li>Fix crash on accessing <code>StopAsyncIteration</code> (Piotr Sawicki, PR <a href="https://redirect.github.com/python/mypy/pull/21406">21406</a>)</li>
<li>Fix incremental compilation with <code>separate</code> flag (Vaggelis Danias, PR <a href="https://redirect.github.com/python/mypy/pull/21299">21299</a>)</li>
</ul>
<h3>Fixes to Crashes</h3>
<ul>
<li>Fix crash on partial type with <code>--allow-redefinition</code> and <code>global</code> declaration (Jukka Lehtosalo, PR <a href="https://redirect.github.com/python/mypy/pull/21428">21428</a>)</li>
<li>Fix broken awaitable generator patching (Ivan Levkivskyi, PR <a href="https://redirect.github.com/python/mypy/pull/21435">21435</a>)</li>
</ul>
<!-- raw HTML omitted -->
</blockquote>
<p>... (truncated)</p>
</details>

### #371 — chore(deps-dev): update pytest requirement from <9,>=8 to >=8,<10 [OPEN]
Updates the requirements on [pytest](https://github.com/pytest-dev/pytest) to permit the latest version.
<details>
<summary>Release notes</summary>
<p><em>Sourced from <a href="https://github.com/pytest-dev/pytest/releases">pytest's releases</a>.</em></p>
<blockquote>
<h2>9.1.1</h2>
<h1>pytest 9.1.1 (2026-06-19)</h1>
<h2>Bug fixes</h2>
<ul>
<li><a href="https://redirect.github.com/pytest-dev/pytest/issues/14220">#14220</a>: Fixed a logic bug in <code>pytest.RaisesGroup</code> which would might cause it to display incorrect &quot;It matches <!-- raw HTML omitted -->FooError()<!-- raw HTML omitted --> which was paired with <!-- raw HTML omitted -->BarError<!-- raw HTML omitted -->&quot; messages.</li>
<li><a href="https://redirect.github.com/pytest-dev/pytest/issues/14591">#14591</a>: Fixed a regression in pytest 9.1.0 which caused overriding a parametrized fixture with an indirect <!-- raw HTML omitted --><a href="https://github.com/pytest"><code>@​pytest</code></a>.mark.parametrize<!-- raw HTML omitted --> to fail with &quot;duplicate parametrization of '&lt;fixture name&gt;'&quot;.</li>
<li><a href="https://redirect.github.com/pytest-dev/pytest/issues/14606">#14606</a>: Fixed <code>list-item</code> typing errors from mypy in <code>@pytest.mark.parametrize &lt;pytest.mark.parametrize ref&gt;</code> <code>argvalues</code> parameter.</li>
<li><a href="https://redirect.github.com/pytest-dev/pytest/issues/14608">#14608</a>: Fixed a regression in pytest 9.1.0 where <code>conftest.py</code> files located in <code>&lt;invocation dir&gt;/test*</code> were no longer loaded as initial conftests when invoked without arguments.
This could cause certain hooks (like <code>pytest_addoption</code>) in these files to not fire.</li>
</ul>
</blockquote>
</details>

### #356 — fix(configurator): OPPO dev console — wake + signin before :436 HTTP commands [MERGED]
## Problem
The Developer Options → OPPO → **HTTP (:436)** tab fired app-API commands with **no session**, so a real player refuses them. The :436 app API needs a **wake → `/signin`** handshake first; the dev console's `oppo_http_get` skipped it entirely.

Worse, the one place that *did* attempt the handshake — `oppo_http_play` (the Pure-HTTP launch) — used the **wrong wake** (a 6-byte `0x55` broadcast to :436) and the **wrong signin body** (`{"user":"","password":""}`). Both were software-verified only, never validated on hardware.

## Fix — match the working bridge
Corrected to mirror the operator's **emby-chinoppo-bridge** (`lib/oppo.py`), which works against real clones:
- **Wake:** UDP `NOTIFY OREMOTE LOGIN` → `<player>:7624`  *(was `0x55`×6 broadcast → :436)*
- **Signin:** `GET /signin?{"appIconType":1,"appIpAddress":<lan-ip>}`  *(was `{"user","password"}`)* — session is keyed to the caller's source IP.
- New `oppo_http_signin` Tauri command (wake + signin).
- The OPPO HTTP tab gets a **Sign in** button + auto-signin before the first command + re-signin on a refusal.
- `oppo_http_play`'s wake/signin corrected too (shared the broken helpers).

**The TCP (:23) path is untouched** — it works and was out of scope.

## Verification
- ✅ Software: `tsc --noEmit` · vitest **361/361** · `cargo test` **57/57** · `vite build`.
- ⏳ **Hardware-pending (Phase-C):** the live :436 wake+signin against a real M9205/OPPO — confirm the dev console now reaches the player and read/control commands stop refusing.

## Source
Corrected flow derived from `siberian-git/Xnoppo` and the operator's `skull-01/emby-chinoppo-bridge` (`lib/oppo.py`, `lib/playback.py`).

🤖 Generated with [Claude Code](https://claude.com/claude-code)

### #352 — fix(release): configurator release title emits v-prefix; warn against 2>&1 [MERGED]
## What

The local configurator release script titled the GitHub release `…Configurator <version>` (no `v`), so every release needed a manual `gh release edit` to match the v0.9.x branding the (now-disabled) cloud CI job already emitted (per `release-evidence/v0.9.7/BUILD_NOTES.md`). This realigns the local script.

- `scripts/release-configurator-local.ps1` — title `…Configurator v$Version` (matches the add-on script's `v$Version Final`).
- Add a `.NOTES` warning: do **not** invoke via `2>&1` — under the script's `$ErrorActionPreference='Stop'`, Windows PowerShell 5.1 wraps native npm/tauri stderr as a terminating `NativeCommandError` and aborts the build *before* publish (this broke the v0.9.9 first attempt; the bundle built but nothing shipped).
- `tests/test_release_scripts.py` — pin the `v`-form.

## Verified (software only)

- `pytest tests/test_release_scripts.py` → **3 passed**; `ruff check` clean.
- `-DryRun -SkipBuild` prints `--title Kodi Oppo External Player Configurator v0.9.9`.

No change to the build/publish code path — only the release title text + script docs.

### #347 — ci: local release scripts (add-on + configurator) [MERGED]
Part of #345 (go-local CI/release).

Adds the two local release scripts that replace the cloud release jobs.

**`scripts/release-addon-local.ps1`** (replaces `package.yml`'s release job) — reads the add-on version, builds the runtime installable ZIP + `.sha256` via `tools/package_installable_zip.py` under WSL, then `gh release create "v<version>" --title "v<version> Final" --latest=false` with those assets. `--latest=false` because the **configurator** holds the repo Latest badge (a bare add-on ZIP as Latest would misdirect Windows users). It calls the Python packager directly rather than `package_release.sh` so it builds **only** the runtime ZIP — `package_release.sh` also writes a dev-source ZIP that would walk `configurator/node_modules` + `src-tauri/target` in a live checkout.

**`scripts/release-configurator-local.ps1`** (replaces `configurator-ci.yml`'s release job) — `npm run dist` (native; Tauri needs MSVC + WebView2), collects the current-version MSI + NSIS + `SHA256SUMS`, then `gh release create "configurator-v<version>" --latest --title "Kodi Oppo External Player Configurator <version>" --generate-notes`. Filters to `*_<version>_*` because a local `bundle/` dir accumulates installers across builds (the cloud runner is always fresh).

Both take `-DryRun`; the configurator one also takes `-SkipBuild` for logic checks.

`tests/test_release_scripts.py` pins the publish conventions (Final title + `--latest=false` for the add-on; `--latest` + the branded title + `SHA256SUMS` for the configurator; `-DryRun` on both).

### Verification (software, in-session)
- **Add-on `-DryRun` (full):** built `script.oppo203.iso.external-2.9.17.zip` (76 files) + sha; emitted `gh release create v2.9.17 --target main --title "v2.9.17 Final" --latest=false --notes-file ...RELEASE_NOTES_v2.9.17.md <zip> <sha>`.
- **Configurator `-DryRun -SkipBuild`:** read version 0.9.7; the version filter was checked against real Tauri output (`*_0.9.6_*` matched the 2 existing 0.9.6 installers; `*_0.9.7_*` = 0). The actual MSI/NSIS build (`npm run dist`, ~8 min) is exercised at the next real release, **not** this session.
- **Add-on gate:** `ruff check` clean · `mypy --gate` 51/0 · full `pytest` **1223 passed, 3 skipped** · **coverage 99.17%**.

No hardware surface (dev tooling).

Local gate: `cd D:\Git\script.oppo203.iso.external; .venv\Scripts\python.exe -m pytest -q tests\test_release_scripts.py`

---

### #346 — ci: clean-room local gate scripts/ci-local.sh (supersedes cloud ci.yml) [MERGED]
Part of #345 (go-local CI/release).

Adds `scripts/ci-local.sh` — the local-first clean-room gate that supersedes the cloud `.github/workflows/ci.yml`. It does a fresh `git clone` of HEAD into a throwaway dir (gates the **committed** state, not the dirty worktree), provisions uv-managed throwaway venvs, and runs:

- **Stage A (3.12, once):** `ruff check` / `ruff format --check`, `mypy --gate`, `render_docs` / `sync_version` / `test_layout` / `i18n_extract` `--check`
- **Stage B (3.12, full):** `py_compile` / `compileall`, full `pytest`, `unittest discover`, serial 99% coverage gate (matches `ci.yml` — not `-n auto`)
- **Stage C (compat smoke, 3.9 + 3.10):** `py_compile` + `sync_version --check` + the targeted `test_v2910_final_release` + g5–g8 readiness tests (mirrors `ci.yml`'s compatibility-smoke job)
- **Stage D (3.12, once):** runtime ZIP + forbidden-prefix audit + dev-source unpack smoke + `audit_release`

`tests/test_ci_local_gate.py` pins ci-local.sh to LF and to the same gate commands `test_github_readiness_g6_ci_hardening.py` pins for `ci.yml`, so the local gate can't silently drift from the (frozen) cloud spec.

One-time prereq (already done on this machine): `curl -LsSf https://astral.sh/uv/install.sh | sh && uv python install 3.9 3.10 3.12`.

### Verification (software, in-session)
Ran `wsl bash scripts/ci-local.sh` clean-room on this branch — **all green**:
- Full gate (3.12): pytest **1213 passed**, unittest **606 OK**, **coverage 99% (5922 stmts)**, audit_release PASS (`fail_under=99`)
- Compat smoke (3.9 + 3.10): **24 passed** each
- Packaging: runtime zip `...-2.9.17-cilocal.zip` **76 files, forbidden=0**; dev-source unpack smoke 24 passed

No hardware surface (dev tooling). Cloud `ci.yml` stays active until it is disabled in the norms-flip PR.

Local gate: `cd D:\Git\script.oppo203.iso.external; wsl bash scripts/ci-local.sh`

### #338 — cfg: rebrand configurator to "Kodi Oppo External Player Configurator" [MERGED]
Renames the Windows configurator app from **OppoKodiAddon Configurator** to **Kodi Oppo External Player Configurator** across the user-facing surfaces, and makes the in-app title bar show the live version.

## Changes
| Surface | After |
|---|---|
| In-app title bar (`App.tsx`) | `Kodi Oppo External Player Configurator-v0.9.5` *(live)* |
| `productName` (`tauri.conf.json`) — drives installer/exe/Start-Menu | `Kodi Oppo External Player Configurator` |
| OS window title (`tauri.conf.json`) | `Kodi Oppo External Player Configurator` |
| Browser/tab title (`index.html`) | `Kodi Oppo External Player Configurator` |
| i18n `app.title` | `Kodi Oppo External Player Configurator` |
| NSIS preinstall-hook header comment | renamed |

**Live version:** injected from `package.json` at build time via a Vite `define` → `__APP_VERSION__`, composed through the existing `app.versionLine` i18n key (`{name}-v{version}`). Tracks each release with no manual edits. Version stays out of `productName` so exe / Start-Menu / uninstall-entry names don't churn per release. Bundle **identifier is unchanged** (preserves NSIS upgrade detection and `app_data_dir`, so existing user state isn't orphaned).

## Verification
- `tsc -b` clean; **359/359 vitest pass** (incl. updated `i18n.test.ts`, `settings_xml.test.ts`).
- Dev-server DOM check: title bar = `Kodi Oppo External Player Configurator-v0.9.5`, document title = brand name, `__APP_VERSION__` = `0.9.5`, no console/server errors.

## Operator note (release-time)
The configurator CI gate (tsc/vitest/cargo) covers this, but the **installer-side** rename can only be confirmed when the NSIS/MSI bundle is built on a `configurator-v*` tag. At next release, verify on a real Windows host: installer display name, Start-Menu shortcut, uninstall-entry name, exe filename, and the desktop window title all read the new brand. Minor edge: the preinstall hook's parallel-MSI detection matches `DisplayName == ${PRODUCTNAME}`, so the first post-rename installer won't auto-detect an *old-named MSI* install.

Out of scope (left intentionally; happy to follow up): old-name provenance strings in generated XML (`generate.ts`), diagnostics export header, settings.xml "Managed by…" comment, and `README.md`/`BUILD.md`.

🤖 Generated with [Claude Code](https://claude.com/claude-code)

### #336 — cfg(installer): single old-version prompt - drop NSIS reinstall page (PR2/3) [MERGED]
**PR 2 of 3** — installer single old-version prompt (ENH #334). Builds on PR #335 (merged).

Removes the stock Tauri NSIS **reinstall page** from the vendored `installer.nsi` (`PageReinstall` / `PageReinstallUpdateSelection` / `PageLeaveReinstall` + the `Page custom` insertion — 202 lines) and broadens `installer-hooks.nsh` `NSIS_HOOK_PREINSTALL` to absorb its job:

- Detects a prior **NSIS** install via `SHCTX ${UNINSTKEY} "UninstallString"` and removes it silently in place (`/S _?=<dir>`, app settings preserved).
- Keeps detecting a parallel **MSI** install (now disambiguated from our own NSIS key, which is named `${PRODUCTNAME}`) and removes it via `msiexec /x /qn`.
- One `MB_YESNO` confirmation covers both → an upgrade shows **one** prompt, not two.

The hook runs at the top of `Section Install` — before files are copied and before the new uninstall key is written — so it still sees the prior install's registry state; `$INSTDIR` is already restored by `RestorePreviousInstallLocation`.

### Verification (software-verified only)
- **`tauri build --bundles nsis` locally → makensis compiled the edited template + hook into a working installer** (528 B smaller than the verbatim PR1 build). This is the real check — the configurator PR gate does **not** run `tauri build` (only the `configurator-v*` release job does).
- `tsc -b` ✓ · `vitest` 359 ✓ · drift guard still green.
- **Phase C (real Windows host):** install v0.9.4, then upgrade to the v0.9.5 build → confirm exactly **one** remove-previous-version prompt and that settings survive.

### Known change
The silent-install (`/S`) downgrade auto-abort (EarlyChecks) relied on the removed page's version comparison and is now inert. GUI installs are unaffected. Documented for Phase C.

Refs #334.

---

### #335 — cfg(installer): vendor Tauri 2.11.2 NSIS template + drift guard (PR1/3) [MERGED]
**PR 1 of 3** — installer single old-version prompt (ENH #334).

Vendors the exact `@tauri-apps/cli` **2.11.2** NSIS template into `configurator/src-tauri/installer.nsi` (verbatim, only a version-stamp header added) and points `bundle.windows.nsis.template` at it. This makes the template editable in-repo — the prerequisite for PR 2, which removes the built-in reinstall page so an upgrade shows **one** prompt.

**Behavior-neutral.** The template body is unchanged, so the generated installer is equivalent to the stock Tauri one. The behavioral change lands in PR 2.

**Drift guard.** `src/installer-template.test.ts` pins the template's `oppo-nsis-template-version` stamp to the resolved `@tauri-apps/cli` in `package-lock.json` — a silent CLI bump fails the build until the template is consciously re-vendored.

### Verification (software-verified only)
- `tsc -b` ✓ · `vitest` **359 passed** (+2 drift guard) ✓ · `vite build` ✓ (local)
- `cargo test` + the windows-CI `tauri build` (compiles the vendored NSIS) gate this PR.
- No runtime/app-logic change; seven-preset matrix untouched. Hardware validation not claimed.

Refs #334. Provenance: `tauri-apps/tauri` ref `@tauri-apps/cli-v2.11.2`, `crates/tauri-bundler/src/bundle/windows/nsis/installer.nsi`.

### #333 — Release v2.9.16 Final: AVR/Pure-HTTP correctness + hardening + coercion fixes [MERGED]
## Release v2.9.16 Final — add-on maintenance & hardening

Cuts the standalone add-on release that folds in the correctness/robustness fixes merged since **v2.9.15** (the configurator already bundles `main`'s add-on; this stamps the add-on release track and ships the runtime ZIP).

### What's folded in (already on `main` since v2.9.15)
- **AVR / Pure-HTTP correctness** (#221–#224) — `http_handoff` is now AVR-eligible under the Pure-HTTP default; OPPO HTTP path translation before BDMV; AVR power-on settle; URL-encoded backslash.
- **Monitor / transport hardening** (#226–#233) — SVM3 startup timeout gated on confirmed playback; single-`recv` + CR/LF reassembly in `oppo_control`/eISCP; clone-wake import; `LOADING` ≠ confirmed.
- **Settings schema guards** (#235–#237) — six configurator-owned settings declared + emitted-vs-read guard; AVR backend-id guard.
- **Honest Pure-HTTP launch** (#254) — failed `activate→signin→play` recorded as `failed` (rc=1).
- **Distinct Samsung HDMI defaults** (#256).
- **Coercion-crash fixes** (#275, #329) — `OverflowError` on `int(inf)`; four `int()` port/option crashes.

### New in this PR (surfaced during release verification)
- **AutoScript CR/LF hardening (cross-area).** `autoscript_helper.generate()` now strips CR/LF from embedded path/credential fields via `_safe_text`; the configurator's byte-exact mirror `autoscript-gen.ts` gets the identical `safeText`, a new `crlf_paths` fixture pins it on both sides, and the cross-language consistency guards stay green. Surfaced by the #330 property test; same class as #275/#329.
- **`discovery._safe_port` mypy `--strict` fix** — `int()` on an `object` argument failed the strict gate (latent from #329); behavior-preserving `cast(Any, …)` restores **51/0**.

### Verification (software-verified only)
- Add-on: `py_compile` · `render_docs --check` · `sync_version --check --expected-version 2.9.16` · `test_layout --check` · `i18n_extract --check` · **`audit_release` PASS (607/607)** · ruff check + format clean · **mypy --strict 51/0** · full **pytest 1187 passed / 3 skipped** · **serial coverage 99%** (5899 stmts / 16 missed).
- Configurator (AutoScript mirror touched): **`tsc -b` clean · vitest 357 passed · `vite build` OK**.

**Hardware validation is not performed or claimed.** Real OPPO/Kodi/NAS/AVR/TV behavior is Phase-C pending.

Evidence: `docs/release-history/*_v2.9.16*` + `release-evidence/v2.9.16-final/MANIFEST.txt`.

### #332 — AVR raw-command console (send arbitrary receiver commands) [MERGED]
﻿## AVR raw-command console ? implements #331

The Developer Options ? AV receiver tab previously only did **input-select**. This adds a true **raw-command console** per backend so you can send arbitrary receiver commands (power / volume / mute / query), fired through a new thin Rust `avr_raw_send`:

| Backend | Transport | Example |
|---|---|---|
| Denon / Marantz | line-ASCII over telnet `:23` (CR-appended) | `PWON`, `MV505`, `PW?` |
| Onkyo / Pioneer | eISCP payload framed over `:60128` | `!1PWR01`, `!1MVLUP` |
| Yamaha | MusicCast API path over HTTP `:80` | `/YamahaExtendedControl/v1/main/setPower?power=on` |
| Sony audio | JSON-RPC (no line protocol) | unchanged ? `setPlayContent` URI box is its raw surface |

Each backend gets a preset palette (Power On/Off, Vol ?, Mute On/Off, Query) plus a free-form box, logged to the shared command/response transcript. The existing input-select palettes stay; the old "raw input" boxes are relabelled "Other input" to disambiguate from the new raw-command box.

### Safety
`avr_raw_send` routes through pure, unit-tested builders **before any socket opens**:
- `denon_raw_command` / `eiscp_raw_payload`: reject control characters and over-length input; eISCP requires the leading `!`.
- `yamaha_raw_path`: requires an absolute `/?` path; rejects `..`, spaces, and CR/LF (header-splitting).
- `host` goes through the existing `validate_ssh_component`. Reuses `socket_exchange` / `eiscp_frame` / `http_get_request` / `device_response_ok` / `first_line_or_sent`. Best-effort + hardware-pending.

### Verification
- **cargo test 57** (+3 new builder tests), no warnings ? `tsc -b` clean ? **vitest 356** ? `vite build` ok.
- Render verified in the preview: Denon + eISCP backends show both subheads, the input + raw preset palettes, the raw box (placeholders `PWON` / `!1PWR01`), and the per-backend framing hint.
- Rides **configurator v0.9.4**.

---

### #330 — Add-on property-test pass: fix int() coercion crashes (discovery + autoscript) [MERGED]
﻿## Add-on property-test pass ? int() coercion crash fixes

Implements #329. A property/fuzz sweep over the add-on's pure helpers surfaced a cluster of `int()`-coercion crashes (same root cause the earlier play-status pass fixed in `oppo_control`/`i18n`): a device-cache JSON file / mDNS record / JSON-loaded AutoScript preset can carry a port or option that is textual (`"8060/tcp"`) or a non-finite float (`inf`), and `int(value or 23)` raised `ValueError`/`OverflowError` instead of degrading.

### Fixes
- **`oppo/discovery.py`** ? new `_safe_port()` (falsy ? default, matching the old `or 23`; unparseable ? default) routed through `parse_mdns_record()`, `DeviceCache.add()`, and `DeviceCache.load()`. The `load()` site previously sat outside the JSON try/except, so a bad cached port made the recovery path itself raise.
- **`oppo/autoscript_helper.py`** ? `_safe_int()` adds `OverflowError` so `int(float("inf"))` degrades to the default.
- No happy-path behavior change; all four are defensive coercions.

### Regression guard ? `tests/test_property_addon_robustness.py`
Mirrors `test_property_http_hdmi.py`: **Hypothesis when installed, curated deterministic fallback otherwise** so the gate never silently weakens (and Python 3.9 compat-smoke + minimal CI stay green without a new dep). Pins the four fixes plus the eISCP frame round-trip (`parse(build(p)) == p[:160]`) and the Kodi/player path-normalize idempotence as invariants. Locally fuzzed with Hypothesis 6.155 ? no counterexamples.

### Audited & already-robust (no change)
`hardware_capabilities`, `preset_manager` version parsing, `settings_reader`/`settings_schema`, `hdmi_sequencing`, `oppo_control` play-status, `path_mapper`, the TV/AVR drivers, `reconnect_backoff`.

### Gate (software-verified only)
- `pytest -n auto`: **1187 passed, 3 skipped** (skips are POSIX-only release scripts).
- Serial coverage: **99%**, `coverage report` exit 0. `autoscript_helper.py` 100%; `discovery.py` 99% (sole partial is the pre-existing `_RealFS.write` dir branch).
- `ruff check` + `ruff format --check` clean.

---

### #328 — Harden dev-console commands (session review fixes) [MERGED]
﻿## Hardening ? session code review fixes

An independent adversarial review of this session's ~21 PRs found **no high/blocking issues** (ship-worthy). This PR applies its 1 medium + 3 low hardening findings plus a labelling honesty fix:

- **MED** ? `nas_test_smb`: reject `net use` user/password that net.exe would re-tokenize (quotes/newlines, or a `/`-leading or `*` password it reads as an option / interactive prompt). Not RCE (no shell is spawned), but prevents a misparsed or hung login.
- **LOW** ? `autoscript_push_telnet`: reject a script containing a line equal to the heredoc terminator (`OPPOEOF`) so a crafted script cannot close the heredoc early.
- **LOW** ? `validate_addon_zip`: cap each zip entry decompressed read at 16 MB so a crafted zip cannot balloon memory; an over-cap entry truncates -> hash mismatch -> never reported as a verified build.
- **LOW** ? `install_addon_zip`: reject quotes/newlines in `addons_path` (consistent with the other SSH path guards).
- **Honesty** ? relabel the Kodi panel `signed build` -> **`build tag verified`** (it is a content-integrity tag, not a cryptographic signature).

### Verification
- `tsc -b` clean, `vite build` ok, **vitest 356/356**, **cargo test 54/0**.
- All five are defensive early-returns plus a label change; no change to the happy path. These ride the next configurator release (v0.9.4).

### #326 — Configurator: verify the add-on build tag (PR 2) [MERGED]
﻿## PR 2 ? Configurator verifies the build tag

Completes the embedded build-tag initiative (#322). Implements **#324**. Builds on PR 1 (#325).

`validate_addon_zip` now reads `resources/oppokodiaddon.sig` and recomputes the SHA-256 content manifest over the zip's members:
- **Rust `addon_manifest_sig`** is a byte-exact mirror of the add-on packaging's `compute_manifest_sig` (new dep `sha2`).
- **signed** (tag matches) ? **unsigned** (no tag ? older build, still uploadable + labeled) ? **mismatch** (tag present but content differs ? **`valid:false`, blocked** with a reason).
- `AddonZipInfo` gains `signature_state`; the Kodi panel shows it on the validation line (`? Valid add-on v2.9.15 ? signed build ?` / `? unsigned (older build)`).

**Cross-language guard:** a cargo test pins `addon_manifest_sig` to the **same fixture hash** as `tests/test_addon_signature.py` (`bbcc6382?`), so the Python (packaging) ? Rust (validation) manifest can't silently drift.

### Verification (software-only)
- `tsc -b` clean ? `vite build` ok ? **vitest 356/356** ? **cargo test 54/0** ? including `addon_manifest_sig_matches_the_python_fixture` (the Rust hash reproduces the Python hash, so a Python-packed tag verifies in the configurator).
- Browser-verified (vite dev): the Kodi panel renders cleanly (Browse + Upload-disabled gate intact), no console errors.
- **Phase-C / operator:** the signed/unsigned/mismatch display against a real signed add-on zip on the built app.

### #325 — Add-on: stamp a build-integrity tag into the installable zip (PR 1) [MERGED]
﻿## PR 1 ? Add-on packaging stamps a build-integrity tag

First of the embedded build-tag initiative (#322). Implements **#323**. **Add-on tooling only ? no runtime/behavior change.**

`tools/package_installable_zip.py` now stamps `script.oppo203.iso.external/resources/oppokodiaddon.sig` into the installable zip: a small JSON carrying the add-on id, version, file count, and a **SHA-256 content manifest** (`compute_manifest_sig` ? sorted `arcname\n<sha256(bytes)>\n` ? SHA-256) over every runtime file **except the tag itself**.

- It lives under the allowlisted `resources/` dir and is **inert to Kodi** (Kodi never reads it). The allowlist invariant `set(namelist) == names` still holds (the tag is in both).
- `compute_manifest_sig` is the **cross-language contract** the configurator's Rust `addon_manifest_sig` will mirror (PR 2); `tests/test_addon_signature.py` pins it to a shared fixture hash so the two can't drift.
- It's an **integrity/build tag, not a cryptographic signature** (the project ships unsigned).

### Verification
- `pytest -n auto` **1162/3** ? **serial coverage 99%** (exit 0) ? `ruff check` + `ruff format --check` clean.
- The new test asserts the produced zip carries a verifying tag, the manifest is order-independent + matches the fixture hash, and the allowlist invariant holds. No runtime change ? nothing Phase-C here.

### #303 — Developer Options: NAS panel (PR D-NAS) [MERGED]

Sixth slice of the Developer Options console (#290, `docs/BUILD_PLAN.md` ?2). Implements **#295**.

### #301 — Developer Options: TV command console (PR D-TV) [MERGED]
﻿## PR D-TV ? TV command console

Fourth slice of the Developer Options console (#290, `docs/BUILD_PLAN.md` ?2). Implements **#293**.

Every TV backend is available for experimentation regardless of the configured one, each with a preset palette + a free-text raw box, fired via the existing commands:
- **Roku ECP** ? any keypress via `tv_switch_roku` (already takes a `key`).
- **ADB** ? any `input keyevent` / `am start` via `tv_switch_adb` (runs on the Kodi box over SSH).
- **Sony Bravia** ? HDMI-port REST switch via `tv_switch_sony_bravia` **plus** generic IRCC remote keys via a new **`tv_sony_bravia_ircc`** (POST /sony/IRCC, SOAP body, X-Auth-PSK) ? the one input-only gap.
- **LG / Samsung / custom** ? any `{tv_ip}`-templated command via `tv_switch_external` (runs on the box over SSH).
- **SmartThings** ? `setInputSource` request built for display via `smartthings_switch_request` (the add-on fires it over HTTPS; no TLS client here).

Everything streams to a shared **live transcript** ? new `devTranscript.tsx` (`useTranscript` + `Transcript` + `runAndLog`), reused by the AVR and NAS panels next. TVs expose no telemetry feed, so it's a command/response log + reachability ? stated honestly in the UI.

### #276 — test(addon): property-based robustness tests for HTTP/SVM3 predicates (+ OverflowError fix) [MERGED]
Adds tests/test_property_http_hdmi.py: property-based robustness tests (Hypothesis-or-fallback, no new hard dep) asserting the Xnoppo V3 status/info predicates (tcp_qpl_is_idle, http_status_is_idle, http_info_is_definitive_stop, http_info_indicates_playing, global_info_is_playing) never raise and always return a bool across arbitrary inputs, plus the HDMI timing helpers (compute_play_delay/switch_mode/av_stagger) clamp junk. The test immediately caught a real latent crash (#275): http_info_indicates_playing did int(float('inf')) guarded only by except (TypeError, ValueError) -> OverflowError; broadened to include OverflowError (same class as the v1.1.9 i18n.L(inf) fix). Gate: pytest -n auto 1158/3, ruff clean, mypy --strict 51/0, serial coverage 99% (exit 0). Refs #275.

### #274 — fix(installer): single old-version prompt on upgrade [MERGED]
Collapses the two upgrade prompts to one. Tauri's built-in NSIS reinstall page already offers to remove a previous NSIS install; the PREINSTALL hook (installer-hooks.nsh) was additionally prompting for the same thing. The hook is now scoped to the gap Tauri misses -- a parallel MSI install of the product -- and stays silent on a normal NSIS upgrade, so the user sees one prompt, not two. (A full custom-template override to drop Tauri's page outright needs Tauri's versioned handlebars template and isn't safely authorable offline; this achieves the single-prompt UX without that fragility.) makensis-validated via npm run dist locally; detect/remove runtime is Phase-C.

Rust diagnostics_env() (os/arch/version, no secrets) + write_diagnostics() (writes the redacted JSON to app-data, returns the path). DiagnosticsCard on the dashboard: Export diagnostics (save file) + Copy to clipboard. Gate: cargo test 43, vitest 314 (+3), tsc -b + vite build green. On a configurator-v* tag it builds the MSI/NSIS via npm run dist, computes SHA-256, and publishes the GitHub release as Latest. tags are deliberately not combined with paths under one push trigger (GitHub filters tag pushes when paths is present).

### #267 — Fix Reset-all hang on an unreachable device + stream live progress [MERGED]
Fixes the operator-reported hang where **Reset all configurations** froze the PC when it couldn't connect to the Kodi box (or other devices) and gave no indication of what it was doing. Refs #266.

## Root cause
- **Tier A** `reset_box_ssh` fired **5 sequential `ssh` subprocesses** (4 deletes + restart), each `ConnectTimeout=8` → ~40s blocking on a powered-off box, UI frozen on "Resetting…". No reachability pre-probe.
- **Tier B** `reset_box_userdata` → `remove_existing_paths` ran `is_dir()`/`exists()`/`remove_dir_all` against a dead SMB UNC, which blocks on Windows SMB timeouts.
- **No UI feedback** — a single `await` toggling only `busy`.
- **Latent bug** — the box `invoke` was awaited before `reset_app_data`; a box failure aborted the whole reset, so an unreachable box blocked even the purely-local reset-to-first-run.

## Fix
- **Rust** (`lib.rs`): `reset_box_ssh` does a fast SSH-port-22 pre-probe (`connect_timeout` 2.5s) and fails in seconds instead of grinding through five timeouts; `reset_box_userdata` probes the SMB share (port 445) for a UNC target first; both emit a `reset-progress` event per step. New pure `unc_host()` helper + `ResetProgress` struct.
- **TS** (`reset.ts`): pure `resetStepPlan(state)`; `resetEverything(state, onProgress?)` runs the box and local resets as **separate stages** so a box failure no longer aborts the local reset (start-over always works), reporting `boxFailed` for partial success.
- **React** (`ResetAllCard.tsx`): renders a **live step list** (pending/running/done/failed) driven by the orchestrator + the granular `reset-progress` line — shown on both entry points (header + Step 0 → ResetAll screen, and the dashboard) since they share the card.

## Verification (software only)
- `cargo test` **43 passed** (+1 `unc_host`).
- `vitest` **311 passed** (+7 in `reset.test.ts`: `resetStepPlan` ×3, `resetEverything` stage-separation ×4).
- `tsc -b` clean · `vite build` OK.
- **Browser-verified** (vite dev): both entry points reach the ResetAll screen; clicking through renders the live "Reset progress" step list and (because vite dev has no Tauri runtime) the local step shows `failed` with its detail and the summary message — proving the step list + failure rendering + that it **does not freeze**; no console errors.

## Not verified here (Phase-C / operator, on real hardware)
The destructive on-box deletion itself is unchanged from v0.8.2 and remains hardware-pending: the actual SSH/SMB delete + Kodi restart, and the real fast-fail timing against a powered-off box. The **set of deleted paths is unchanged** (the four configurator-owned paths, pinned by `box_reset_targets`).

---

### #264 — Make Reset-all reachable from app header and Step 0 [MERGED]
## What & why

The **Reset-all-configurations** action (shipped in configurator v0.8.2/v0.8.3) renders
**only** on the Live dashboard (`ResetAllCard` in `screens/dashboard.tsx`), and the
dashboard is reachable **only** via `go("dashboard")` from the final playback-test screen
(`screens/test.tsx:1232`) — i.e. after completing the whole wizard. So on a fresh install
or a broken/partial setup — exactly when you'd want to reset and start over — it cannot be
reached, and the feature looks missing. (#263)

## Change

- New `reset_all` utility screen (`screens/ResetAll.tsx`) that **reuses the existing
  `ResetAllCard` unchanged**, wrapped with a title and a "← Back" (returns to `step0_gate`).
- Two persistent entry points routing to it via `go("reset_all")`:
  - a small **"Reset all…"** button in the app header (`App.tsx`) — visible on **every**
    screen, hidden only on the reset screen itself;
  - a **"Reset all configurations…"** link on the **Step 0** gate (`Step0Gate.tsx`).
- `steps.ts`: `reset_all` added to the `ScreenId` union and both exhaustive maps
  (`SCREEN_TO_STEP` → `step0`, `SCREEN_TO_CHAIN` → `media`).
- The **dashboard card and the reset action itself are untouched** (`reset.ts`, the Rust
  `reset_box_*`/`reset_app_data` commands, and `ResetAllCard` are unchanged).

## Verification (software-verified only)

- `npx tsc --noEmit` → 0 errors.
- `npm test` → **304 vitest passed** (301 prior + 3 new in `steps.test.ts` pinning the
  `reset_all` map wiring).
- `npm run build` → clean.
- **Browser-verified** (vite dev): the header entry appears on Step 0 **and** a mid-wizard
  step (Step 1) and is hidden on the reset screen; both entry points navigate to the reset
  screen; the reused danger card reveals its confirm gate ("Yes — delete everything…" /
  "Cancel"); "← Back" returns to Step 0; **no console errors**. (The screenshot tool timed
  out, so evidence is the accessibility snapshot + DOM eval, not an image.)

## Not verified here

This change only makes the existing action **reachable**. The actual on-box deletion
(Tauri/Rust path, shipped in v0.8.2) is **unchanged and remains hardware-pending** —
Phase-C, operator. Ships in the next configurator release (**v0.8.4**, bundling the add-on).

### #205 — Release v2.9.14 Final: six-option playback architecture & hardening [MERGED]
Bumps the Kodi add-on to **v2.9.14 / build 23**, capturing all runtime work merged since the last stable `v2.9.13`.

## What's in this release
- **Six-option playback architecture** — 3 routing modes (`playercorefactory`, `service_interception`, `http_handoff`) × 2 monitor modes (`legacy`, `svm3`), six presets sharing one dispatch in `run_playback_session`.
- **SVM3 verbose-mode monitor** — confirms real playback/progress from `@UPL`/`@UTC`, legacy fallback on connect failure.
- **Richer session status** — `oppo203iso-status.json` carries `session_id`, `started_at`/`updated_at`, and a `launching`→`monitoring`→`ended` phase + heartbeat (additive).
- **Robustness hardening** — default `hold_mode` `tcp_qpl_poll`, bounded hold modes with timeouts, stale-sentinel self-heal.
- Supporting: `tv_*` rename, ENH-#51 `mypy --strict` rollout, ENH-#42 in-add-on menus, `resources/lib` sub-package split.

## Release mechanics
- Version sources bumped (`version.py`, `addon.xml`, `pyproject.toml`, `sources.yaml`, `ci.yml`, `verify.sh`); managed docs regenerated; version-pinned tests bumped; new `v2.9.14` evidence set + `release-evidence/v2.9.14-final/MANIFEST.txt`.
- `runtime_behavior_changed: true` (defaults changed) — protected core behaviors preserved.

## Gate (software-verified only)

**Hardware validation not performed / not claimed.**

### #203 — Shared playback-preset source + cross-language parity guard [MERGED]
## Shared playback-preset source — automate the six-preset cross-language contract

PR-only hardening (the optional item flagged in `docs/BUILD_PLAN.md` §6). No tracked issue.

### Problem
The six-option playback-architecture matrix (3 routing × 2 monitor) was encoded **independently** on each side:
- **Add-on:** `PLAYBACK_ARCHITECTURE_PRESETS` + `_PRESET_BY_AXES` + `_ROUTING_ALIASES` (`settings_reader.py`).
- **Configurator:** the `${routing}_${monitorMode}` emission + a **hardcoded `CANONICAL_SIX`** in `mapping.test.ts` whose own comment admitted it mirrors the add-on's `PLAYBACK_ARCHITECTURE_PRESETS`.

The only cross-language link was that manual mirror + the AGENTS.md "maintained matrix" norm + reviewer discipline — nothing *failed* if one side changed and the other did not.

### Change (no runtime change)
- New `configurator/src/presets-db/playback-presets.json` — the single cross-language source of truth: `routing_modes`, `monitor_modes`, `presets` (the 6, in add-on order), `preset_by_axes`, `routing_aliases`.
- **Add-on** `tests/test_playback_presets_consistency.py` pins the JSON ↔ `settings_reader`'s tuples/dicts (the players-DB-guard pattern). The tuples stay; the test asserts they equal the JSON.
- **Configurator** `presetsdb.ts` loader + `presetsdb.test.ts` pin the TS side; `mapping.test.ts`'s `CANONICAL_SIX` now derives from the DB (manual mirror deleted).

Cross-language preset drift is now a **test failure** instead of a review check. `settings_reader` keeps its tuples and `mapping.ts` keeps its emission — the JSON is the asserted-equal source, not a new runtime dependency.

### Gate (software-verified only)
- Add-on `pytest -n auto` **1053 passed / 3 skipped** (+7 parity guard) · `ruff check .` clean (new guard `ruff format`-clean)
- Configurator `tsc --noEmit` 0 · `vitest` **266** (+5 `presetsdb`) · `vite build` exit 0
- mypy / serial-coverage unaffected — no `resources/` production code changed.

No hardware step (pure data + tests, no Phase C). Single copy by design — presets are not remotely refreshed like the model DBs, so no docs mirror. Checklist row under Phase A.

🤖 Generated with [Claude Code](https://claude.com/claude-code)

### #202 — Dashboard memory (3/3): session-history card + exact session_id dedup (#168) [MERGED]
## Dashboard memory (3/3): session-history card + exact session_id dedup (#168)

Stacked on #201 (snapshot diff) → #200 (appdata store). Rebuilds the superseded draft #166 on the current dashboard.

### What the card does
Adds a **Session history** card to the Live dashboard. The add-on overwrites its single `oppo203iso-status.json` per run, so each 6s poll folds the freshly-read status into a local history (`foldObservation`), persisted under appdata (via #200''s store), so past sessions survive reopening the dashboard. An entry updates in place as a session advances `starting → stopped` (and on a heartbeat that only refreshes `updatedAt`/`phase`), a signature change opens a new entry, history caps to the newest 50, and an unchanged poll returns the **same array reference** so idle polls never churn the appdata file.

### The 5.1 unlock -- exact dedup
This is the deferred piece from #166: `sessionSignature` now prefers the add-on''s **`session_id`** (shipped in add-on PR #183 / Phase 5.1, surfaced by `parseOppoStatus`) for an **exact** identity match -- so two identical back-to-back sessions are told apart, which the old descriptor heuristic could not do. Older records that carry no id fall back to the descriptor heuristic (the documented limitation #168 noted).

### Files
New: `session_log.ts` (+test, 10 cases). Modified: `screens/dashboard.tsx` (the card + the in-poll fold/persist).

### Gate (software-verified only)
- `tsc --noEmit` 0 / `vitest` **283** (+10: session_log) / `vite build` exit 0
- Dev-server boot smoke test: app mounts, **zero console errors**.
- The live render with real sessions needs the built Tauri app + a tier A/B box -- **Phase C**.

No add-on (`resources/`) change; no Rust change; no new dependency. Checklist row under Phase A.

**Merge order (stacked):** #200 → #201 → this. Retarget each child to `main` before merging bottom-up -- this repo does not auto-retarget.

🤖 Generated with [Claude Code](https://claude.com/claude-code)

### #201 — Dashboard memory (2/3): settings-snapshot diff card (#167) [MERGED]
## Dashboard memory (2/3): settings-snapshot diff card (#167)

Stacked on #200 (appdata store). Rebuilds the superseded draft #165 on the current (Phase 5.2/5.3) dashboard, which had diverged.

### What the card does
Adds a **Configuration changes** card to the Live dashboard. A **Snapshot now** button (on-demand -- a diff is only meaningful on demand) reads the box''s `settings.xml` over the existing tier-aware routing, masks secret-bearing ids, persists the sanitized snapshot under appdata (via #200''s store), and diffs it against the previous snapshot (added / removed / changed; the first capture is a baseline).

### Secrets never reach disk or screen
`sanitizeSettings` replaces the values of secret-bearing ids (Sony PSK, SmartThings token, `sony_avr_psk`) with a fixed `[secret]` sentinel **before** the snapshot is persisted **and** before it is diffed. Because the mask is constant, a changed secret reads as no-change by design (its key add/remove still shows). Unit-tested: a `psk` value never appears in the snapshot or the diff.

### Behaviour-preserving factor-outs (frozen guards held)
- `parseSettingsXml` is factored out of `mergeSettingsXml` via a shared `readSettingsDoc` -- the merge output and the malformed `/refusing to overwrite/` guard are unchanged (pinned by `settings_xml.test.ts`).
- `fileReadPlan(state, rel)` is factored out of `statusReadPlan` -- tier A/B/C routing unchanged (pinned by `dashboard_status.test.ts`); `statusReadPlan` is now a one-line wrapper.
- `isSensitiveKey` is the single sensitivity policy in `debug/log.ts`, shared with the debug redactor.

### Gate (software-verified only)
- `tsc --noEmit` 0 / `vitest` **273** (+12: settings_diff 5, parseSettingsXml 4, fileReadPlan 3) / `vite build` exit 0
- Dev-server boot smoke test: app mounts, **zero console errors**.
- The live card render (a real `settings.xml` diff) needs the built Tauri app connected tier A/B to a real Kodi box -- **Phase C**.

No add-on (`resources/`) change; no new crate dependency. Checklist row added under Phase A.

**Merge order:** retarget to `main` after #200 merges, then merge bottom-up.

🤖 Generated with [Claude Code](https://claude.com/claude-code)

### #198 — Persist every TV backend's runtime config from the configurator [MERGED]
## The gap
`configurator/src/mapping.ts` `wizardStateToAddonSettings` persisted only Roku keys and Sony Bravia HDMI **ports**, so after setup the add-on could not actually drive the other TV backends (ADB, LG/Samsung/custom command, SmartThings) — their runtime config was never written. This completes the configurator→add-on TV-config wiring. Configurator-only; `resources/` is untouched (the add-on already reads every key below — verified in `tv_control.py`, `tv_adb_control.py`, `tv_smartthings_control.py`).

## What changed

  - Stale comment on `hdmiInputSettings` (the "wired in the TV-input slice, not here" note) refreshed — this PR is that slice. Routing/monitor/preset logic, the six presets, and the AVR side are untouched.
- **`state.ts`** — additive `WizardState` + `INITIAL_STATE` fields: `tvOppoCommand`, `tvKodiCommand`, `tvSmartThingsToken`, `tvSmartThingsDeviceId`, `tvSmartThingsOppoInputId`, `tvSmartThingsKodiInputId`. (`tvSonyPsk` already existed.)

### #190 — Phase 4.4 — OPPO self-test orchestration [MERGED]
## Phase 4.4 — OPPO self-test orchestration

Sequences the full headline self-test end-to-end, each step with an honest fallback:

1. **Power-cycle** — `oppo_power` off (`#POF`) then on (`#PON`). Failure is non-fatal; the run continues.
2. **Reach the share** — no mount command for `http_handoff` (the player mounts the share itself on play), so this is marked **skipped** with the honest "mount it in the player's browser once if it can't see the share" note.
3. **Play** — computes the OPPO-visible path by rewriting the captured Kodi path via `oppoPathFrom → oppoPathTo` (`applyRewrite`, mirroring the add-on's `_translate_media_path` first-occurrence replace), then fires `oppo_http_play`. Skipped honestly when no path/mapping exists.
4. **Confirm (SVM3)** — starts the live monitor, folds `oppo-live` frames (reusing the Phase 4.3 `foldSvm3Frame`), and gates on `@UPL PLAY` within a watch window; falls back to "confirm manually below" on timeout. Stops the monitor when done.
5. **Control forwarding** — stays operator-confirmed (can't be auto-verified); hands off to the existing `test_confirm` screen.

> **Stacked on Phase 4.3 (#187) → 4.2 (#185).** Base is `main` per the branch policy, so the diff also contains 4.2 + 4.3; the commit unique to this PR is `458cb08`. Review/merge 4.2 → 4.3 → 4.4 in order.

### New pure helper (`self_test.ts` + tests)
- `applyRewrite(path, from, to)`, `canFireHttpPlay`, the fixed `SELF_TEST_STEPS` model, and `selfTestComplete` / `selfTestPlaybackConfirmed` predicates — framework-free, unit-tested (12 tests).

### UI (`test.tsx`)
- A `SelfTestOrchestrator` card (a "Capture from Kodi" path field reusing `kodi_now_playing`, a per-step status list, a live frame tail, and a "Confirm control forwarding" hand-off). Reuses `oppo_power`, `oppo_http_play`, `kodi_now_playing`, and the live monitor already on `main`.

### Gate (software-verified only)
- `npx tsc --noEmit` clean · `npx vitest run` **214 passing** (+12) · `npm run build` OK. Cumulative Rust (from 4.2): `cargo fmt --check` clean · `cargo test` **37** · `cargo build` **0 warnings**.

### Honest signature
The power-cycle, http_handoff play, and SVM3 confirm all depend on a real OPPO + reachable share — **none verifiable in-session**. Software-verified only; hardware validation not claimed.

### #189 — Phase 5.3 — full-chain dashboard view (Kodi/OPPO/TV/AVR) [MERGED]
## Phase 5.3 — unified full-chain live view

A single "Playback chain" card on the Live dashboard showing **every node on the playback chain** (Kodi / OPPO / TV / AVR) in signal order, each with its liveness and current activity, respecting the chain topology (`state.topology`: TV-only vs AVR chain).

> **Stacked on #186 (Phase 5.2).** Base is the 5.2 branch; review/merge 5.2 first. Retarget this PR to `main` before merging (this repo does not auto-retarget).

### What changed
- **New `dashboard_chain.ts` — pure `chainNodeViews(state, probes, status)`.** Builds the ordered node list from `chainNodeIds(topology)` (minus the `media` source): TV chain = kodi → player → tv; AVR chain inserts the receiver (kodi → avr → player → tv). For each node it reconciles:
  - **Liveness** from the dashboard's existing probe map — `up` / `down` / `checking`, plus `unprobed` (addressed but the backend has no plain-TCP check, e.g. a SmartThings TV — so a missing probe is never shown as "down") and `no-address` (no IP captured).
  - **Activity** derived from the add-on session — the player shows the OPPO playback state + media (or a confirmed-playback fallback), Kodi shows what it launched while a session is live; the TV/AVR switch state is not observable, so they stay blank.
- **`dashboard.tsx` — render the chain card.** New `ChainCard` / `ChainNodeRow` between the Current-session and Live-stream cards, fed the `statuses` map + parsed session the dashboard already polls (no new probes or commands). `LiveStatus` structurally satisfies the probe shape, so it is passed directly.

### Gate (software-verified only — hardware NOT validated)
- `npx tsc --noEmit` — clean
- `npx vitest run` — **206 passed** (+9 new: topology ordering for both chains, the null-topology soft default, probe→liveness mapping, unprobed vs no-address, and the player/Kodi activity derivation)
- `npm run build` — clean (82 modules)

### #188 — Phase 3.3 — Step 5 auto-find inputs (stacked on #184) [MERGED]
## Phase 3.3 — Step 5 auto-find inputs

Replaces the `step5.tsx` "find it for me" fallback (which only stored fabricated values — a bare number, `"cec"`, `"cycle:2"` — without driving anything) with real auto-detection where the backend allows, and an honest manual fallback otherwise.

> **Stacked on Phase 3.2 (PR #184).** This branch is built on top of `claude/cfg-step5-switch-verify-9f3a2c1d`, so it contains both commits. Merge #184 first; the auto-find commit (`d3b939a`) is the only one unique to this PR.

### What changed
- **New pure helper `configurator/src/step5_autofind.ts`**:
  - `autoFindMethod(state)` → `"sweep"` only for the TV chain on a backend that can drive discrete HDMI inputs (Roku ECP / ADB) with a TV IP; `"manual"` for SmartThings / LG / Samsung / custom / Sony, the AVR chain, or no TV IP.
  - `sweepCommandFor(state, hdmi)` reuses `planSwitch` so the sweep fires exactly the per-backend command the Test-switch action does.
  - `autoFindProbePorts(state)` → the control port to knock on before a sweep.
- **`step5.tsx` `Step5Fallback`** now:
  - **Scan reachability** — `tv_port_probe` (TV control port open?) + `oppo_query #QPW` (`parseOppoPowerReply` → OPPO powered?), to fail fast on an unreachable TV and confirm there's something to look for.
  - **Driven sweep** (Roku/ADB) — switches to each HDMI in turn; the user confirms when the OPPO appears; the confirmed number is stored as `playerInput` (and a different default for `kodiInput`).
  - **Honest manual entry** + a manual-switching exit for everything else.
- Removed the now-dead `FallbackRung`/cosmetic CEC/blind-cycle stub rungs.

### Why no passive read
No TV/AVR control protocol reports the active HDMI input number (consistent with the documented OPPO-IP limitation), so the driven sweep + user confirmation is the strongest honest automation; there is no silent inference.

### Verification (software-only)
- `npx tsc --noEmit` — pass
- `npx vitest run` — **207 passed** (6 new in `step5_autofind.test.ts`)
- `npm run build` — pass

**Software-verified only — hardware NOT validated.** No real TV/AVR was reachable; the sweep, probe interpretation, and arg mapping are unit/type-checked only, not exercised against a device.

### #185 — Phase 4.2 — test-ISO copy_to_share + progress UI (D-2) [MERGED]
## Phase 4.2 — test-ISO copy (D-2: user supplies the ISO)

Placeholder wiring for the OPPO self-test's "copy a test file to the shared library" step. **D-2 (locked): the operator supplies the master disc/ISO** — nothing is bundled or downloaded; this copies a user-chosen source file to a user-chosen destination.

### Rust (`lib.rs`)
- New `#[tauri::command] copy_to_share(source_path, dest_path)` — streams the source to the destination (local path **or** SMB UNC, the same transport `deploy_to_userdata` uses on Windows) in 1 MiB chunks, emitting a `copy-progress` event (`bytesCopied`/`total`/`percent`) per chunk. Writes to a sibling temp file then renames into place, so an interrupted copy can't leave a half-written target in the library.
- Registered in the `generate_handler!` list (after `smb_test_write`).
- Pure helpers with unit tests: `copy_progress_percent` (saturating 0..=100, zero-total-safe, no overflow on multi-GB totals) and `validate_copy_paths` (both paths non-empty; destination must include a file name).

### UI (`test.tsx`)
- The "disc" test mode becomes an honest **copy** flow: a user-supplied **source ISO path** field, a **destination** field (local or `\server\share` UNC), a **Copy** button invoking `copy_to_share`, and a **progress bar** that listens to `copy-progress`. Picker/callout copy updated to reflect D-2 ("you supply the disc") instead of a bundled master.

### #184 — Phase 3.2 — Step 5 switch-and-verify [MERGED]
## Phase 3.2 — Step 5 switch-and-verify

Replaces the simulated HDMI switch in `step5.tsx` (the "configurator can't drive the switch yet" copy + cosmetic manual confirm) with a real **Test switch** action that dispatches the matching backend command and shows the device reply, keeping an honest manual fallback where a switch can't be confirmed.

### What changed
- **New pure helper `configurator/src/step5_switch.ts`** — `planSwitch(state, target, hdmi, extras)` returns a `SwitchPlan`:

  - `manual` (honest fallback): no backend / missing IP / missing per-backend value / `custom_command` AVR — switch with the remote and confirm visually.
- **`step5.tsx` `Step5Ask`** now builds the plan, fires it via `invoke` (from `src/ipc.ts`), and surfaces the reply. Inline capture appears only for the active backend: Sony TV PSK, the external command template, or the SmartThings device/input ids. A device reply is labelled **command-accepted, not a visual confirmation** — the user still confirms they see the OPPO/Kodi.
- **`state.ts`** — additive field `tvSonyPsk` (Sony Bravia TV Pre-Shared Key; the only place the TV PSK is needed today, handled as a secret like `avrSonyPsk`). Appended, no reorder/rename.

### #179 — Phase 3.1: configurator TV input-switch commands (#178) [MERGED]
Per-backend TV input-switch commands mirroring `resources/lib/tv/`: Sony Bravia (direct HTTP setPlayContent + X-Auth-PSK), adb + LG/Samsung/custom (run on the Kodi box over SSH like the add-on), SmartThings (cloud request builder; HTTPS firing out of scope -- no TLS crate). <details><summary>2 inline review comment(s)</summary>

**`chatgpt-codex-connector[bot]`** · 2026-06-01:

**<sub><sub>![P2 Badge](https://img.shields.io/badge/P2-yellow?style=flat)</sub></sub>  Preserve escaped braces in external commands**

For LG/Samsung/custom command templates that include literal JSON or other brace syntax, this no longer mirrors the add-on's `command.format(tv_ip=...)` behavior. Templates that work on-device must escape literal braces as `{{`/`}}`; this replacement only substitutes `{tv_ip}` and leaves the doubled braces in the command, so a common command like `curl -d '{{"input":"HDMI1"}}' http://{tv_ip}/...` is sent with invalid doubled braces during the configurator switch test.

Useful? React with 👍 / 👎.

**`chatgpt-codex-connector[bot]`** · 2026-06-01:

**<sub><sub>![P2 Badge](https://img.shields.io/badge/P2-yellow?style=flat)</sub></sub>  Quote ADB shell commands before sending over SSH**

When the user-configured ADB command contains shell metacharacters needed by Android shell commands, this string is interpreted first by the Kodi box's remote shell instead of being passed to `adb shell` like the add-on's `subprocess.run([...]+shlex.split(command))` path. For example, a compound command such as `input keyevent 3; input keyevent 22` runs the second half on Kodi rather than the TV, so the configurator test can fail or execute unintended commands for valid editable ADB presets.

Useful? React with 👍 / 👎.

</details>

<details><summary>1 inline review comment(s)</summary>

**`chatgpt-codex-connector[bot]`** · 2026-06-01:

**<sub><sub>![P2 Badge](https://img.shields.io/badge/P2-yellow?style=flat)</sub></sub>  Parse AVR API bodies before reporting success**

When a Yamaha or Sony receiver returns HTTP 200 with an application-level failure, this helper reports success because it only checks the status line. The add-on paths this mirrors do parse those bodies (`resources/lib/avr/avr_yamaha.py` treats nonzero `response_code` as failure, and `resources/lib/avr/avr_sony_audio.py` treats JSON `error`/unexpected bodies as failure), so a real unsupported Yamaha input or Sony API error would be shown as a successful switch in the configurator. Please inspect the response body for the Yamaha/Sony commands before returning `Ok`.

Useful? React with 👍 / 👎.

</details>

### #174 — Phase 1b: NAS-path capture (observe-and-verify) + OPPO HTTP-play (#173) [MERGED]
Builds the **observe-and-verify NAS-path capture** (D-4 / Phase 1b) so the `http_handoff_svm3` default stops being inert. Tracks #173.

## What this does
The default preset writes `http_handoff_svm3`, but the add-on can't play until it knows the OPPO-visible media path (`oppo_http_path_from/to`). This adds the UI + plumbing to *learn* that path:

- **`kodi_now_playing`** (Rust) — read the path Kodi is playing over the existing SSH channel (JSON-RPC `Player.GetActivePlayers` then `Player.GetItem{file}`; `kodi.log` fallback).
- **`oppo_playback_info`** (Rust) — best-effort read of the OPPO's `/getmovieplayinfo` (undocumented; payload shape unverified).
- **`deriveRewrite` / `parseOppoPlayingPath`** (TS, pure) — turn the two observed paths into `oppo_http_path_from/to`.
- **`oppo_http_play`** (Rust) — fire a network-file play over the OPPO HTTP app API (activate then signin then `/playnormalfile`), pulled forward from Phase 4 PR-4.1, for the verify step.
- **Capture card** on the Player step (`step2.tsx`) — observe-both-ends capture + a manual **SMB/NFS** prefix fallback (WebDAV/FTP out of scope; the OPPO can't necessarily mount them).

## Verification
- Gate: **cargo 18**, **vitest 190**, `tsc --noEmit`, `vite build` — all green.
- Browser-verified (vite dev server): the capture card renders on the Player step, the `deriveRewrite` preview computes (`smb://10.0.1.10/` to `MyNAS/`), "Use this mapping" persists, no console errors.
- **Hardware-pending (per "test later"):** the SSH/UDP/TCP I/O, the OPPO activate+signin+play handshake, whether `/getmovieplayinfo` carries the path, and real end-to-end capture+play. None verifiable in-session.

## Not in this PR
- The verify-by-playing **UI loop** (a "test by playing" button wired to `oppo_http_play` + a live SVM3 `@UPL PLAY` watch) — the primitive is here; the thin UI wrapper + the full Phase-4 OPPO self-test are follow-ups.

Software-verified only; hardware validation not claimed.

### #169 — Guard: configurator emits exactly the six playback presets [MERGED]
## What

Adds a **completeness guard** to `configurator/src/mapping.test.ts`: it iterates the full routing × monitor matrix and asserts `wizardStateToAddonSettings` emits **exactly the six** canonical `playback_architecture_preset` values, pinning `size == 6` on the configurator side.

## Why

The suite already tested each preset individually, but had **no closure assertion** — a 7th routing or a dropped combo would still pass. This mirrors the add-on's `PLAYBACK_ARCHITECTURE_PRESETS` `len == 6` guard (`tests/test_architecture_presets.py::PresetConsistencyGuard`) and backs the new **"six playback-architecture presets are a maintained matrix"** norm in `AGENTS.md` (+ handoff §4).

`CANONICAL_SIX` is kept in lock-step with the add-on list per that norm — adding or removing a routing/monitor combo must change both sides at once.

## Scope

- **Test-only.** No runtime / behavior change; `resources/` untouched.
- Software-verified: `vitest run` → **176 passing** (mapping.test.ts 39); `npm run build` (`tsc -b` + `vite build`) green.

🤖 Generated with [Claude Code](https://claude.com/claude-code)

### #166 — Dashboard follow-on (2/2): historical session log [CLOSED]
## Dashboard follow-on (2/2) — historical session log

**Stacked on #165** (base = `claude/cfg-dashboard-snapshot-91ea2784`). Reuses the
`read_app_json` / `write_app_json` appdata store introduced there. ⚠️ Per this
repo's merge mechanics, retarget this PR to `main` **before** merging #165 (it
does not auto-retarget; merging the base with `--delete-branch` would close this).

### What it does
The add-on overwrites its single `oppo203iso-status.json` each run, so the
**Current session** card only ever shows the latest session. This adds a
**Session history** card: each 6s poll folds the freshly-read status into a local
history (newest first), persisted under appdata, so past sessions survive closing
the dashboard and reopening it.

### How it's built
- New pure `session_log.ts` — `foldObservation(log, status, nowIso, cap)`
  (timestamp injected): updates the newest entry **in place** as a session
  advances `starting → stopped`, opens a **new** entry when the signature changes
  or the same media replays after the prior run ended, caps to the newest N, and
  **returns the same array reference when nothing changed** so the idle polls that
  re-read an unchanged file don't churn the appdata write.
- `screens/dashboard.tsx` — loads the log once on mount, folds on each poll
  (persist only on change), renders the Session history card (state badge, media,
  confirmed flags, stop reason, observed-at) reusing the existing card helpers.

### Caveat (documented)
Dedup is **heuristic**: the add-on's `_status` schema carries no session id or
start timestamp, so two identical back-to-back sessions cannot be told apart.
Making it exact would need an add-on schema field (`session_id` / `started_at`) —
a separate addon-area change, out of scope here.

### Verification (software-only)
- `tsc --noEmit` 0 · **vitest 194** (＋7 `session_log`) · `vite build` ok.
- No Rust change (cargo unchanged from #165); add-on `resources/` untouched.
- **Not hardware-validated:** the real status reads need a Kodi box (Phase C);
  in-session gated by the pure-fold unit tests + render path.

Tracks #168; second of the 2-PR dashboard-memory stack.

<details><summary>1 conversation comment(s)</summary>

Superseded by #202 (session-history card rebuilt on the current Phase 5.2/5.3 dashboard, with exact session_id dedup), now merged to main. Closing the stale draft.

</details>

### #165 — Dashboard follow-on (1/2): settings-snapshot diff [CLOSED]
## Dashboard follow-on (1/2) — settings-snapshot diff

Extends the post-setup **Live dashboard** (`screens/dashboard.tsx`), which was
entirely ephemeral, with a persisted **"Configuration changes"** card.

### What it does
- A **"Snapshot now"** button reads the box's `settings.xml` over the existing
  tier-aware routing (SSH tier A / SMB tier B; manual tier C shows a note),
  sanitizes it, persists it, and shows a **diff vs. the previous snapshot**
  (added / removed / changed). First capture is a baseline.
- **Secrets never leak.** Values for secret-bearing ids (Sony PSK, SmartThings
  token, `sony_avr_psk`) are masked with a fixed sentinel **before** the snapshot
  is written to disk **and** before it is diffed — so a secret value never
  reaches the screen or appdata. The sensitivity policy lives in one place
  (`debug/log.ts` `isSensitiveKey`, shared with the debug redactor).

### How it's built
- **Rust:** `read_app_json` / `write_app_json` — a guarded (`safe_app_rel`,
  no `..`/absolute) appdata JSON store modelled on `save_wizard_state`. Reused by
  PR 2 (session log).
- **TS:** exported `parseSettingsXml` (factored out of `mergeSettingsXml`),
  `settings_diff.ts` (`sanitizeSettings` + `diffSettings`), a shared
  `fileReadPlan(state, rel)` (factored out of `statusReadPlan`),
  `dashboard_store.ts` (persistence wrapper), `dashboard_snapshot.ts` (orchestrator).

### Frozen behaviour (guarded)
- `mergeSettingsXml` and `statusReadPlan` keep **identical** behaviour after the
  extractions — pinned by `settings_xml.test.ts` and `dashboard_status.test.ts`.
- The existing three dashboard cards are unchanged (additive card only).

### Verification (software-only)
- `tsc --noEmit` 0 · **vitest 187** (＋12: settings_diff 5, parseSettingsXml 4,
  fileReadPlan 3) · `vite build` ok · `cargo test` **8** (＋3 `safe_app_rel`).
- Add-on `resources/` untouched.
- **Not hardware-validated:** the actual device `settings.xml` read needs a real
  Kodi box (Phase C). In-session this is gated by pure-function unit tests, the
  cargo path-guard test, and the render path — matching the dashboard's existing
  software-verified-only posture.

Tracks #167; first of a 2-PR stack — PR 2 adds the historical session log on the
same persistence primitive.

### #164 — Configurator: Live Session Dashboard - current-session panel (Theme 2 / D2) [MERGED]
> **Recovery note:** this PR replaces #159, which GitHub auto-closed when its stacked base branch `claude/cfg-live-dashboard-shell-7c1a9f2e` (D1 / #158) was deleted on merge — this repo does not auto-retarget closed-base PRs. The code is byte-identical to #159; it is re-targeted directly onto `main`. See #159 for the original review thread.

---

**Theme 2 - Live Session Dashboard (PR D2 of 3, was #159, stacked on D1 #158 now on `main`).** PR-only.

Adds a **Current session** card to the dashboard that reads the add-on's `oppo203iso-status.json` and surfaces what the last/current playback session reported:

- session state (in progress / ended / failed), media file, and the resolved preset / routing / monitor;
- the `confirmed_playback` / `confirmed_progress` honesty flags;
- once stopped: OPPO playback state, UTC tick count, stop reason.

### Scope
- New pure `oppo_status.ts`: the `OppoSessionStatus` type + a tolerant `parseOppoStatus()` that mirrors `resources/lib/kodi/playback_session.py` `_status` (8 base keys + 3 snapshot keys), plus `ADDON_DATA_STATUS_REL` (sibling of `ADDON_DATA_SETTINGS_REL`).
- New `dashboard_status.ts`: a pure `statusReadPlan(state)` (tier A -> `read_ssh_file`, tier B -> `read_userdata_file`, manual -> unsupported) + a thin `readOppoStatus()` executor that **reuses the same file-read commands as `applyToKodi`**.
- `screens/dashboard.tsx`: the `SessionCard`, folded into the existing 6s poll.
- **No Rust change, no new dependency, no add-on change.** Read-only.

### Honesty
The add-on writes the status file only at session **start and end**, so the card is a last/current-session summary, not a sub-second live feed (that is D3). In manual mode (tier C) there is no remote link, and the card says so rather than erroring.

### Verification (software-only signature)
`npx tsc --noEmit` clean, **171 vitest** pass (163 + 5 `oppo_status` + 3 `dashboard_status`), `npm run build` ok. The thin async executor is not unit-tested (matches `applyToKodi`); the pure parser + planner are. Phase C on a real box. See `docs/MANUAL_VERIFICATION_CHECKLIST.md`.

Stacked: D1 #158 -> **D2** (this) -> D3 #160 (gated live verbose stream).

<details><summary>1 inline review comment(s)</summary>

**`chatgpt-codex-connector[bot]`** · 2026-06-01:

**<sub><sub>![P2 Badge](https://img.shields.io/badge/P2-yellow?style=flat)</sub></sub>  Correct the SVM3 fallback expectation**

In the Chinoppo / unsupported-`#SVM 3` scenario described here, the code does not fall back just because the command is rejected: `_run_svm3_monitor` only returns `None` for the legacy fallback when `monitor.connect()` raises `OSError`, while `OppoSvm3PlaybackMonitor.enable()` ignores the `#SVM 3` acknowledgement and proceeds to the listen loop. This Phase-C runbook would therefore tell the operator to expect a fallback that will not occur when TCP connects but verbose mode 3 is unsupported, which can misclassify hardware validation results.

### #160 — Configurator: Live Session Dashboard - gated live verbose stream (Theme 2 / D3) [MERGED]
**Theme 2 - Live Session Dashboard (PR D3 of 3, stacked on D2 #159).** PR-only. The capstone PR.

Adds a **Live stream** card that opens the configurator's *own* verbose-mode-3 connection to the player and shows the raw `@UPL` / `@UTC` / status push frames live.

### Rust (`configurator/src-tauri/src/lib.rs`)
- A managed `LiveMonitor` + two commands: `start_oppo_live_monitor(host, port)` / `stop_oppo_live_monitor()`.
- Start connects, remembers the prior verbose mode (`#QVM`), switches to `#SVM 3`, and spawns a background `std::thread` that streams each CR/LF-terminated frame to the webview as an **`oppo-live`** event. Stop signals the thread, which **restores the prior verbose mode** and closes. Unmounting the dashboard also stops it.
- Mirrors `resources/lib/oppo/playback_monitor_svm3.py`. Uses `std::thread` + `AtomicBool` - **no tokio, no new crate dependency** (`Cargo.toml` unchanged). 2 `cargo test` units (`classify_frame`, `parse_verbose_mode`).
- Its own `oppo-live` channel - **independent of the open wire-transcripts draft #153** (which uses `debug-wire`). The only overlap is the imports block + the handler list in `lib.rs`.

### Dual-subscriber gate (the safety crux)
The OPPO treats verbose mode as a **device-global** setting, so two `#SVM` drivers conflict. A pure `canStartLiveStream(status)` **refuses** to start while the add-on reports an active (`starting`) session, and the 6s poll **auto-stops** the stream if a session starts mid-stream. This *reduces* but cannot *eliminate* a race in the poll window - and the non-conflict can only be confirmed on real hardware.

### Verification (software-only signature)
`npx tsc --noEmit` clean, **173 vitest** (171 + 2 gate tests), `cargo check` clean, `cargo test` 2/2, `npm run build` ok. **Not** exercised against a real OPPO or a live Tauri runtime. **The dual-subscriber non-conflict is NOT hardware-validated** - Phase C must confirm the configurator stream never disrupts an add-on playback session. See `docs/MANUAL_VERIFICATION_CHECKLIST.md`.

Stacked: D1 #158 -> D2 #159 -> **D3** (this).

<details><summary>2 inline review comment(s)</summary>

**`chatgpt-codex-connector[bot]`** · 2026-06-01:

**<sub><sub>![P2 Badge](https://img.shields.io/badge/P2-yellow?style=flat)</sub></sub>  Block live stream when session status is unreadable**

In manual mode, or whenever the SSH/SMB status read fails, `readOppoStatus` returns `status: null`; passing only `session?.status ?? null` into the gate makes that indistinguishable from a genuinely idle/no-record state, so the Start button remains enabled even though the dashboard cannot know whether the add-on is mid-session. That defeats the dual-subscriber safety gate in exactly those contexts and can let the configurator send `#SVM 3` while the add-on's SVM monitor is active; include `supported`/read-error state in the gate and fail closed when the status source is unavailable.

Useful? React with 👍 / 👎.

**`chatgpt-codex-connector[bot]`** · 2026-06-01:

**<sub><sub>![P2 Badge](https://img.shields.io/badge/P2-yellow?style=flat)</sub></sub>  Disable Start while a start request is pending**

If the user double-clicks Start, both handlers can pass the `streaming === false` render state and issue `start_oppo_live_monitor`; the Rust side accepts one and rejects the other as already running, and the rejected call can run last and set `streaming` back to false while the monitor thread is still active. The UI then shows Start instead of Stop, and subsequent starts only report “already running” until the screen is unmounted; track a pending state or set the UI to streaming before awaiting the command.

Useful? React with 👍 / 👎.

</details>

### #153 — Configurator: OPPO wire-level transcripts in the developer debug panel [MERGED]
## Wire-level OPPO transcripts in the developer debug panel

Completes the deferred **PR-3** of the developer debug view ([#142](https://github.com/skull-01/script.oppo203.iso.external/pull/142)). The panel previously captured each `invoke` round-trip's structured args/result (via the `ipc.ts` wrapper) but never the **raw bytes on the wire** — so an OPPO that misbehaves at the protocol level was invisible.

### What changed
- **Rust (`src-tauri/src/lib.rs`):** `oppo_query` takes a Tauri-injected `AppHandle` and emits a `debug-wire` event for the bytes it **sends** (the CR-terminated command) and **receives** (the reply) over TCP:23. Payload: `{ direction, label, host, port, hex, text, len }`. The returned reply string is **byte-for-byte unchanged** — emission is a pure observational side-effect (best-effort; a failed emit never breaks the command). New pure `to_hex` helper with 3 unit tests.
- **Frontend:**
  - `debug/log.ts` — `DebugEntry` is now an `ipc | wire` discriminated union; new `recordWire()` appends wire frames to the same bounded ring buffer (shared seq/step).
  - `debug/wireListener.ts` (new) — subscribes to `debug-wire` via `@tauri-apps/api/event` and records each frame; started once from `App.tsx` (no-op in a non-Tauri context).
  - `shell/DebugPanel.tsx` — renders wire rows (`→ sent` / `← recv`, byte count; hex + lossy text on expand). `statusOf` no longer miscounts wire frames as errors.

### Security boundary (deliberate scope)
Emission is **scoped to the OPPO IP-control path only**. `deploy_ssh` / `read_ssh_file` / `deploy_to_userdata` are **not** instrumented: their payloads are the generated `settings.xml` (Sony PSK / SmartThings token), and the panel's key-based `redact()` cannot sanitize a raw byte stream. OPPO control frames (`#QVM`, `@UPL`, …) carry no secrets. The panel stays gated behind **Ctrl+Shift+D**, off by default.

### Verification (software-only)
- **Frontend:** `tsc -b` clean · **157 vitest** pass (incl. new `recordWire` cases) · `vite build` OK.
- **Rust:** `cargo check` clean · `cargo test` 3/3 (`to_hex`).
- **No add-on change** (zero Python touched).

### Not verified here
The `emit → listen` pipeline can't run in vitest (no Tauri runtime) or a plain vite preview, and **CI does not build Rust** (the configurator gate is frontend-only). The `lib.rs` change is verified by local `cargo check`/`cargo test` only. The actual bytes need a real OPPO — **not hardware-validated**. Phase A/C steps are in `docs/MANUAL_VERIFICATION_CHECKLIST.md`.

Draft — software-verified only; only the operator promotes/closes.

🤖 Generated with [Claude Code](https://claude.com/claude-code)

### #148 — Session B / PR B3: SVM3 capability probe in the player test [CLOSED]
**Session B · PR B3 of the configurator four-option work.** Stacked on #147 (PR B2). Pairs with addon PRs #144/#145.

## What
After the **Step 2** player test confirms two-way control (`#QPW` → ON), it now runs an **SVM3 capability probe**, reusing the existing `oppo_query` command — **no Rust change**:
1. `#QVM` — read the player's current verbose mode;
2. `#SVM 3` — does the player accept verbose mode 3?
3. `#SVM <prev>` — restore the previous mode (the probe leaves the player exactly as it found it).

- New pure parsers `parseOppoVerboseMode` / `parseSvm3Accepted` (`probes.ts`).

- A callout reports *supported* / *not-detected*; the Step 3 SVM3 tile shows the per-player outcome.
- **Never gates the power test** — if SVM3 isn't accepted, two-way control still passed and Legacy is used.
