### #145 — Session A / PR A3: shared run_playback_session engine + four-option rewire [CLOSED]
**Session A · PR A3 (final) of the SVM3 / four-option playback build.** Stacked on #144 (PR A2) — review/merge A1 → A2 → A3 in order.

## What
New `resources/lib/kodi/playback_session.py` — `run_playback_session(settings, media_file, launch_source)`, the **single sequence** both routings now share:
`mark_session_active` → `fast_start` (TV + AVR pre + OPPO start) → **monitor** → `fast_return` (stop + AVR/TV restore) → `clear_session_active`.

The monitor branch is chosen by `playback_monitor_mode` (resolved via `normalize_architecture`):
- **legacy** → the existing `hold_playback` dispatcher, unchanged;
- **svm3** → `OppoSvm3PlaybackMonitor` (PR A2), **falling back to the legacy hold if it cannot connect**.

A split-truth **status JSON** (`oppo203iso-status.json`) is written next to the session sentinel — `launch_source`, `architecture_preset`, `routing_mode`, `monitor_mode`, `confirmed_playback`, `confirmed_progress`, `oppo_playback_state`, `stop_reason` — so confirmation is reported honestly, never as a single success flag.

## Rewire (the duplicate sequences are gone)
- `external_player.main()` → delegates to `run_playback_session(..., launch_source="playercorefactory")`.
- `service._run_interception()` → delegates to `run_playback_session(..., launch_source="service_interception")` (still stops Kodi playback + keeps the daemon thread + duplicate-session guard + safe 4K classifier — all pre-existing).
- `fast_start` / `hold_playback` / `fast_return` / `mark_session_active` / `clear_session_active` stay **public and unchanged**; the legacy paths keep the exact same call sequence.

`main()` passes its own module (`sys.modules[__name__]`) into the engine so the helpers resolve to the same instance when `external_player` runs directly as `__main__` (preserves the runpy entrypoint coverage test).

## Scope notes
- **No new persistent settings** here (monitor_mode/preset came from A1; SVM3 tuning is code constants from A2).
- Much of the plan's "Build 4 service revision" was **already implemented** — service already runs interception off the main loop (daemon thread), already dup-guards, already uses the safe classifier — so that build collapses into this one call-swap.

## Tests
`tests/test_playback_session_modes.py` (10 tests): legacy runs `hold_playback`; svm3 runs the monitor and skips the hold; svm3-connect-failure falls back to legacy; `fast_start` failure returns 1 and still clears the sentinel; `fast_return` failure is non-fatal; status JSON carries split-truth confirmation; status-writer edge cases. `playback_session.py` is at **100%** coverage.

## Gate (software-verified only — no hardware)
- pytest **1036 passed / 3 skipped**
- coverage **99%** — `playback_session.py` 100%, and the missing-statement count is unchanged at 16 (no new gaps)
- `ruff check` + `ruff format --check` clean
- mypy `--strict` gate **51 / 0**
- layout / docs / version / i18n checks green

## Notes
- ENH issue to be filed by the operator (`area:addon`): *"Shared playback-session engine (four-option) + status JSON"*.
- The paused teaching-commentary wip branch on `external_player.py` will need a rebase (this PR changed `main()` logic).
- Phase A/C rows added to `docs/MANUAL_VERIFICATION_CHECKLIST.md`.

Software-verified; hardware validation not performed / not claimed.

### #144 — Session A / PR A2: SVM3 verbose-mode-3 playback monitor [CLOSED]
**Session A · PR A2 of the SVM3 / four-option playback build.** Stacked on #143 (PR A1) — review/merge A1 first. New module only; not wired into the runtime yet.

## What
New `resources/lib/oppo/playback_monitor_svm3.py` — `OppoSvm3PlaybackMonitor`, a persistent verbose-mode-3 (`#SVM 3`) client that confirms OPPO playback from the device's own push events:
- `#QVM` → remember the current verbose mode; `#SVM 3` → enable; `#SVM <prev>` → restore on exit (even after the socket drops).
- `@UPL PLAY` → `confirmed_playback`; an **advancing** `@UTC` time code → `confirmed_progress`. A play command being *sent* is never treated as proof.
- `@UPL STOP/HOME/MCTR/NO DISC` end the session; `PAUSE`/`MENU`/`DISC` keep it active.
- Bounded ring buffer of recent raw events; logs **state changes + periodic summaries**, not per-second `@UTC` spam, unless `full_event_log` is on.

## Design
Built on the same CR/LF line reader and stop/keep-alive vocabulary as `oppo_tcp_client.py` (the existing `#SVM 2` verbose-push client), and **fully injectable** (socket factory + monotonic clock) so it runs hermetically — no real device, socket, or wall-clock. Tuning (summary interval, ring size, startup/session timeouts, require-progress) ships as **code constants** — no new persistent settings (per the build-plan decision). The legacy `hold_mode` monitors are untouched.

## Not wired yet
Nothing imports the monitor at runtime in this PR. **PR A3** adds the shared `run_playback_session()` that selects it when `playback_monitor_mode=svm3`, with a fallback to the legacy monitor if SVM3 can't connect.

## Tests
`tests/test_svm3_playback_monitor.py` — 32 hermetic tests covering QVM/SVM3/restore, `@UPL` states, advancing-vs-repeated `@UTC`, production-vs-full logging, ring-buffer cap, and the startup-timeout / session-timeout / connection-closed / stop_event exits. **Module at 100% coverage.**

## Gate (software-verified only — no hardware)
- pytest **1026 passed / 3 skipped**
- coverage **99%** (the new module at 100%)
- `ruff check` + `ruff format --check` clean
- mypy `--strict` gate **50 / 0** (module added to the allowlist)

- Phase A row added to `docs/MANUAL_VERIFICATION_CHECKLIST.md`.

### #143 — Session A / PR A1: playback_monitor_mode + four-option preset mapping [MERGED]
**Session A · PR A1 of the SVM3 / four-option playback build.** Settings-only; no runtime playback change.

## What
Adds the **monitor axis** `playback_monitor_mode` (`legacy` | `svm3`, default `legacy`) to `settings_reader` alongside the existing `playback_architecture` **routing axis**, plus two pure helpers:
- `architecture_preset(routing, monitor)` → one of the four preset ids (`playercorefactory_legacy`, `service_interception_legacy`, `playercorefactory_svm3`, `service_interception_svm3`); treats the stored `external_player` spelling as `playercorefactory`.
- `normalize_architecture(settings)` → resolves `{preset, routing, monitor_mode}`. The combined **`playback_architecture_preset` is the source of truth when present** (configurator-written); when absent it is **derived** from the legacy fields.

## Why no settings.xml / strings.po
This mirrors the existing **reader-only `playback_architecture`** precedent: those keys live in `DEFAULTS`/`ENUM_VALUES`, are written by the configurator, and have no add-on settings UI. Keeping the add-on **read-mostly** is the project's config-ownership rule (`AGENTS.md`). The configurator seeds these keys in **Session B**.

## Why the preset has no DEFAULTS entry
`Settings` always merges `DEFAULTS`, so a default preset would be indistinguishable from a configured one and would **mask a pre-existing `service_interception` install**. Leaving it out makes "absent" mean "derive from the legacy fields", preserving existing behavior exactly. `playback_monitor_mode` *does* default (`legacy`) — correct for every existing install.

## Migration (test-verified)
- `external_player` install → `playercorefactory_legacy`
- `service_interception` install → `service_interception_legacy`
- fresh / unconfigured → `playercorefactory_legacy`
- an explicit preset wins over stale / disagreeing legacy fields (drift resolution)

## Tests
`tests/test_architecture_presets.py` — 18 tests: mapping (all four combos + the `external_player` alias + unknown-value fallbacks), migration back-fill, drift resolution, and a **preset↔normalized round-trip consistency guard**.

## Gate (software-verified only — no hardware)
- pytest **994 passed / 3 skipped** (the 3 are POSIX-only release scripts, skipped on Windows)
- coverage **99%** (serial gate)
- `ruff check` + `ruff format --check` clean
- mypy `--strict` gate **49 / 0**

## Notes
- ENH issue to be filed by the operator (`area:addon`): *"playback_monitor_mode + four-option preset mapping"*. The new reader key was authorized in-session (SVM3 four-option build plan).
- Phase A row added to `docs/MANUAL_VERIFICATION_CHECKLIST.md`.
- First of the stacked Session-A PRs: **A1 → A2 (SVM3 monitor) → A3 (shared session engine + rewire)**.

Software-verified; hardware validation not performed / not claimed.

### #142 — Developer debug view: per-step IPC command panel [MERGED]
A developer-only **debug view**: a global docked panel that shows every IPC command (sent args, received result/error, timing) for the current setup step. Built per the approved plan (global docked panel; PR-3 wire-level transcripts deferred).

## How it works
- **Capture** (`src/debug/log.ts`) — a 500-entry ring buffer of `{seq, ts, step, command, args, durationMs, ok, result/error}`, with `redact()` (blanks `psk`/`token`/`password`/`secret`/`credential` keys, truncates long blobs) and a current-step tag.
- **Wrapper** (`src/ipc.ts`) — a drop-in `invoke()` over `@tauri-apps/api/core` that records every call (redacted, timed) as a **pure pass-through**. Every wizard call site now imports `invoke` from here; **only `ipc.ts`** still imports it from the Tauri package, so the panel sees all 13 commands.
- **Panel** (`src/shell/DebugPanel.tsx`) — a global docked window mounted once in `App.tsx`, filtered to the active step (toggle to all steps), expand a row for redacted args + result/error, with copy + clear.

## Gating
**Off by default**, toggled with **Ctrl+Shift+D** (persisted in localStorage). Renders nothing otherwise — production UX is unchanged, and the internal/secret surface is never shown to ordinary users.

## Security (redaction)
`invoke` args/results can carry the Sony PSK, a SmartThings token, and deploy file blobs (a generated `settings.xml` can embed the PSK). `redact()` blanks secret-named keys and truncates large blobs **before** anything reaches the panel or a copy/paste; pinned by tests.

## Verification (software-only; hardware validation not claimed)
- `tsc --noEmit` clean · `vitest` **136 passed** (+13: `debug/log.test.ts` covers redaction / ring-buffer cap / step tagging / `entriesForView`; `ipc.test.ts` covers pass-through-with-capture incl. a PSK-redaction pin) · `vite build` ✓.
- **Not** browser-preview tested — the panel needs the Tauri runtime (`invoke` doesn't resolve in a plain vite preview). The rendered panel + hotkey are a **Phase-C** manual step in the built app.

## Scope / notes
- **No add-on change**; configurator-only, not loaded by the add-on at runtime.
- **Deferred (optional, separate session):** wire-level raw-byte transcripts emitted from the Rust commands (`oppo_query` / `tcp_probe` / ssh) via a `debug-log` event channel. The IPC layer already surfaces the OPPO command string + raw reply + port results + deploy reports, so this is a depth upgrade rather than a gap.
- Independent of #139 / #140 / #141 except `MANUAL_VERIFICATION_CHECKLIST.md` (all prepend a Phase-A row — expect a trivial union-merge).

Delivered as two commits: (1) the capture layer + call-site migration, (2) the panel UI.

### #139 — Capture the receiver Kodi input as a dedicated Step-5 field [MERGED]
Follow-up to #138. The AVR chain wrote `avr_restore_input` by reusing the TV-side `kodiInput` (the Step-4 TV HDMI port). But the add-on reads `avr_restore_input` as a **free-text receiver input** (`resources/settings.xml` → `type="string"`; consumed at `resources/lib/avr/avr_sequence.py` as a stripped string, symmetric with `avr_player_input`), so a TV HDMI number was a semantic mismatch.

## What changed
- **`state.ts`** — new `avrKodiInput: string` field (defaults `""`).
- **`screens/step5.tsx`** — a dedicated **"Kodi input on the receiver"** field in the Receiver-control card, shown only in the AVR chain for native (non-Sony) backends. The success callout now also notes the on-exit restore.
- **`mapping.ts`** — `avr_restore_input` / `avr_restore_enabled` now sourced from `avrKodiInput`; a blank value emits no restore input (the add-on treats that as a non-fatal skip). Removed the now-unused `describeReceiverInput` helper.
- **`screens/test.tsx`** — the end-of-wizard summary shows the receiver inputs (e.g. `Receiver BD` / `Receiver CBL/SAT`) instead of `HDMI N` in the AVR chain.

## Scope / non-goals
- **No add-on change** — every setting already exists in `settings.xml` and is read by `avr_control.py` / `avr_sequence.py`. Stays within config-ownership.
- **TV chain unchanged**, regression-pinned.
- **Sony out of scope** — `sony_audio_api` still emits no `avr_restore_*` (it has its own `sony_avr_restore_input_uri`); the new field is hidden for Sony. `custom_command` (Anthem/Arcam/NAD) unchanged.

## Behavior change
AVR-chain users previously got `avr_restore_input` = the TV's Kodi HDMI number as a string (e.g. `1`). Now it is the receiver input name from the new field; **blank ⇒ no restore written** (power-on still fires). An existing AVR-chain config relying on the old reuse should re-open Step 5 and set this field.

## Verification (software-only; hardware validation not claimed)
- `npx tsc --noEmit` → clean
- `npm run build` (`tsc -b && vite build`) → built
- `npx vitest run` → **125 passed** (adds a pin that restore comes from `avrKodiInput`, not `kodiInput`; a blank-input case; and an `INITIAL_STATE` default)

Not browser-preview tested — the Tauri `invoke` paths don't resolve in a plain vite preview. The real "receiver returns to the Kodi input on exit" is a **Phase-C** hardware row in `docs/MANUAL_VERIFICATION_CHECKLIST.md`.

<details><summary>1 inline review comment(s)</summary>

**`chatgpt-codex-connector[bot]`** · 2026-05-31:

**<sub><sub>![P2 Badge](https://img.shields.io/badge/P2-yellow?style=flat)</sub></sub>  Clear stale AVR restore settings when input is blank**

When an AVR-chain user leaves the new receiver Kodi input blank to skip restore, this branch simply omits `avr_restore_enabled` and `avr_restore_input`. However `buildApplyFileSet` merges through `mergeSettingsXml`, which preserves existing setting IDs that are not present in `ours`, so a previously-applied restore value (including the old reused TV HDMI number) remains active instead of being cleared. In the blank-input scenario, emit `avr_restore_enabled: "false"` and/or an empty `avr_restore_input` so re-applying actually disables the stale restore target.

Useful? React with 👍 / 👎.

### #138 — Write receiver-as-switcher AVR settings for the AVR chain [MERGED]
## What

Wires the **AVR chain** through to the add-on settings the configurator writes. When `state.topology` is `kodi_avr_tv_player` and AVR control is enabled, `mapping.ts` now additionally emits:

- `avr_power_on_enabled = "true"` — the receiver powers on at handoff;
- `avr_restore_enabled` / `avr_restore_input` — restore the **Kodi** input on the receiver on exit, reusing the Step‑4 Kodi return target;
- `tv_switching_enabled = "false"` — in the AVR chain the **receiver** is the switcher and the TV is fixed, so the add-on must not also drive the TV (even if a TV backend was configured for reference).

The TV chain (and a null/legacy topology) is **unchanged** — regression-pinned by new tests.

## Why

Part 3 of the two-chains theme. The add-on already reads `avr_restore_*` / `avr_power_on_enabled` (`resources/lib/avr/avr_control.py`, `resources/settings.xml`) but the configurator never wrote them — so the "receiver switches between player and Kodi inputs" behavior the AVR chain promises wasn't actually configured. This closes that gap. No add-on change (config-ownership respected — every setting already exists).

## Decision / caveat

The receiver **restore** input reuses the already-captured `state.kodiInput` (the Kodi return target from Step 4, which the AVR chain now frames as a receiver input). A non-numeric capture (CEC / blind-cycle) has no receiver meaning, so no restore input is written in that case. A dedicated Step‑5 "Kodi input on the receiver" field could be added later if a distinct value is wanted — flagged for follow-up rather than expanding the UI here.

## Verification

Software-verified only: `npm run build` (tsc -b + vite) + `vitest` green, with new `mapping.test.ts` cases pinning the AVR-chain switcher settings and the TV-chain regression. Real receiver switching is Phase-C on hardware (checklist row added). Draft; only the operator merges.

🤖 Generated with [Claude Code](https://claude.com/claude-code)

### #136 — Add a Step 0 playback-chain picker (topology state) [MERGED]
## What

Adds an explicit up-front choice between the two supported playback chains, captured as `state.topology`:
- **Kodi · TV · OPPO** (`kodi_tv_player`) — player → TV; the TV switches inputs.
- **Kodi · AVR · TV · OPPO** (`kodi_avr_tv_player`) — player → AV receiver → TV; the receiver switches inputs, TV fixed.

A new **Step 0** screen ("How is your home theater wired?") sets it; the gate routes into it. This is the state + picker foundation; the flow-copy / chain-viz / settings wiring that *consumes* the choice lands in follow-up PRs.

## Why

The wizard previously implied receiver-presence only from `avrModel != null` with a late optional ask. An explicit topology lets the steps differ by what the user actually has.

## Notes

- **Soft default:** a null/legacy `topology` behaves exactly as the TV chain, so persisted sessions are unaffected (they spread over INITIAL_STATE and land on the picker).
- Config-ownership respected — no add-on change.

## Verification

Software-verified only: `npm run build` (tsc -b + vite) + `vitest` green. Picker render/route is Phase-C (checklist row added). Draft; only the operator merges.

🤖 Generated with [Claude Code](https://claude.com/claude-code)

### #135 — Add a Step 5 receiver reachability probe (reusing tv_port_probe) [MERGED]
## What

Step 5 (AV Receiver) captured the receiver IP but had no way to confirm the box is reachable before relying on AVR control. This adds a **Test reachability** button to the receiver-control card that TCP-probes the receiver's control port and reports whether it answered — mirroring the Step 3 TV port-probe UX (loading state, pass/fail line). No state-changing commands are sent.

Port per resolved add-on backend (from `resources/lib/avr/avr_presets.py`):
- Denon/Marantz -> 23, Yamaha -> 80, Onkyo/Pioneer -> 60128.
- Sony (`sony_audio_api`, authenticated HTTP API) and `custom_command` brands have no simple TCP check, so no probe button is shown for them.

## How

Frontend-only. Reuses the existing `tv_port_probe` Tauri command (`configurator/src-tauri/src/lib.rs`), which is a generic multi-port TCP probe despite its `tv_` name — so **no Rust change**. Adds a `controlProbePort()` backend->port map plus a small probe handler/state to `AvrControlCard` in `configurator/src/screens/step5.tsx`.

> Naming caveat: `tv_port_probe` is reused here for the AVR probe. It is genuinely generic; a future cleanup could rename it `tcp_port_probe`. Left as-is to keep this diff frontend-only.

## Verification

Software-verified only: `npm run build` (tsc -b + vite build) and `npx vitest run` green in `configurator/`. The actual TCP reachability against a real receiver is on-hardware (Phase C) and not verified in-session. No add-on change.

PR-only theme (no tracked issue). Draft for operator review; only the operator merges.

🤖 Generated with [Claude Code](https://claude.com/claude-code)

<details><summary>1 inline review comment(s)</summary>

**`chatgpt-codex-connector[bot]`** · 2026-05-31:

**<sub><sub>![P2 Badge](https://img.shields.io/badge/P2-yellow?style=flat)</sub></sub>  Clear stale probe results when the target changes**

When the user successfully probes one receiver, then edits the Receiver IP or selects another AVR backend/model in the same Step 5 screen, this `reach` result is still rendered even though it belongs to the old host/port. Because the message interpolates the current `probePort`, a prior success on Denon `:23` can be shown as “Port 80 answered” after switching to Yamaha before any new probe runs, which can mislead the operator into enabling control for an unverified receiver. Clear the result on `avrIp`/`probePort` changes or store and compare the probed target before displaying it.

Useful? React with 👍 / 👎.

</details>

### #134 — Pin the two avr-models.json copies with a consistency vitest [MERGED]
## What

Adds `configurator/src/avr_db_consistency.test.ts`, a vitest guard that pins the AVR control DB's two copies together:

- **byte-for-byte identical** -- `configurator/src/avr-db/avr-models.json` (the bundled copy `avrdb.ts` imports) and `docs/configurator/avr-db/avr-models.json` (the canonical, remotely-refreshable copy);
- **schema invariants** -- `schema_version === 2`, non-empty `db_version`, non-empty `lineups`/`models`, unique lineup ids, unique model ids, and every `model.lineup` resolves to a real lineup.

## Why

`build/gen_avr_db.py` writes both copies, but nothing enforced they stay in step -- and the loader only ever imports the bundled copy, so a hand-edit to one could ship undetected drift. Closes the AVR twin of the players/TV DB no-consistency-guard gap.

### #132 — Probe oppo_http_port (default 436) in the diagnostics HTTP check (#111) [MERGED]
## Summary

The diagnostics-dashboard HTTP reachability probe (`_http` inside `default.run_diagnostics_dashboard`) connected to TCP port **80**, but the OPPO HTTP control API runs on `oppo_http_port` (default **436**). The HTTP capability line therefore reported reachability against a port the device never serves. **Low severity — diagnostics-only**, no playback routing or control path involved.

### Change (refs #111)

- `default.py` — `run_diagnostics_dashboard` gains an `http_port: int = 436` parameter; the nested `_http` probe now connects to (and reports) `http_port` instead of the hardcoded `80`.

`run_diagnostics_dashboard` has no live menu caller today (it is a tested/symbol-level entry point), so the **436 default** governs; a future caller can thread the configured `oppo_http_port` through the new parameter.

## Tests

`tests/test_diag_probe_port.py` (2): with `socket.socket` faked, the probe connects to **436** by default and to an explicit override, **never 80**.

## Gates (software-verified only; hardware validation not claimed)

- `ruff check` + `ruff format --check` clean; mypy strict gate **49 files, 0 errors**

### #131 — Self-heal a stale oppo203iso-active session sentinel (#117) [MERGED]
## Summary

The `oppo203iso-active` session sentinel is written at playback start (`mark_session_active`) and removed in a `finally` (`fast_return` → `clear_session_active`). If the Kodi process is killed during a hold — power loss, crash, or Kodi force-terminating the external player — the `finally` does not run and the sentinel persists on disk.

A stale sentinel then:
- makes Service Interception skip **all** further interceptions (`service.py` `_session_is_active` → `_handle_started`), and
- makes the remote bridge forward keys to the OPPO with no active session (`oppo_remote.py`, `remote_bridge_only_when_active` default true).

### Change (refs #117)

- `resources/lib/kodi/settings_reader.py` — new dependency-free `session_is_active(addon_data_dir)` + `SESSION_MAX_AGE_SECONDS` (21600 = 6h, comfortably beyond the longest legitimate hold). A sentinel whose file is older than that is treated as **inactive**, so the next session self-heals. The file mtime is the session-start clock (the sentinel is written exactly once), used directly so the check is robust to unreadable contents.
- `service.py` + `resources/lib/oppo/oppo_remote.py` — the two **duplicated** `_session_is_active` readers now delegate to the shared helper, resolving the duplication the issue noted.

## Tests

`tests/test_session_sentinel_staleness.py` (5): missing / fresh / stale via the helper, plus the service and remote readers honoring staleness (sentinel aged with `os.utime`).

## Independence

No file overlap with the other robustness PRs — mergeable in any order. The checklist row is prepended to avoid a docs conflict.

## Gates (software-verified only; hardware validation not claimed)

- `pytest` **970 passed / 3 skipped**; serial coverage **99%** (`oppo_remote.py` 100%, helper fully covered)
- `ruff check` + `ruff format --check` clean; mypy strict gate **49 files, 0 errors**

On-device verification (kill Kodi mid-hold; confirm interception self-heals) is queued in `docs/MANUAL_VERIFICATION_CHECKLIST.md` (Phase A). Only the operator closes the issue.

### #130 — Default hold_mode to tcp_qpl_poll so playback stop is detected (#114) [MERGED]
## Summary

The shipped default `hold_mode` was `fixed_timeout` — a blind 180-minute `time.sleep` with **no stop detection**. Out of the box, Kodi's playback slot (External Player mode) and the `oppo203iso-active` session sentinel (Service Interception mode) stayed busy for three hours regardless of when the disc actually ended. The configurator does **not** write `hold_mode`, so this default governs every unconfigured install.

This switches the default to `tcp_qpl_poll`, which polls `#QPL` over TCP and ends the hold when the player reports idle/stopped.

### Change (refs #114)

- `resources/lib/kodi/settings_reader.py` — `DEFAULTS[hold_mode]` `fixed_timeout` → `tcp_qpl_poll`.
- `resources/settings.xml` — `hold_mode` enum `default=0` → `default=3` (the index of `tcp_qpl_poll`).

Both sides are changed together; `tests/test_hold_default.py` pins them consistent with `ENUM_VALUES` so the reader default and the settings.xml enum index cannot drift apart.

## Merge order

**Merge after #129** (the #112/#115/#116 hold-robustness PR). That PR adds the unreachable-OPPO abort to `tcp_qpl_poll`, so the new default inherits it and a dropped-off player no longer holds to the 240-minute timeout. The checklist row is prepended (not appended) specifically to avoid a docs merge conflict with #129.

## Gates (software-verified only; hardware validation not claimed)

- `pytest` **965 passed / 3 skipped**; serial coverage **99%**
- `ruff check` + `ruff format --check` clean; mypy strict gate **49 files, 0 errors**
- `render_docs` / `test_layout` / `i18n_extract` / `sync_version` `--check` all OK (settings.xml in sync)

On-device verification (fresh-install hold behavior) is queued in `docs/MANUAL_VERIFICATION_CHECKLIST.md` (Phase A). Only the operator closes the issue.

---

### #129 — Bound hold_playback modes and fix the verbose_push QPL fallback (#112/#115/#116) [MERGED]
## Summary

`hold_playback` could pin Kodi's playback slot (and the `oppo203iso-active` session sentinel) far past the end of playback. This PR bounds every hold mode and repairs the broken `verbose_push` fallback. **No change** to playback routing, OPPO payloads, TV/AVR sequencing, or the idle-confirmation / definitive-stop / trick-play-suppress logic.

### Fixes (refs #112, #115, #116)

- **#112** — `verbose_push` on a connect failure set `mode='tcp_qpl_poll'` and fell through, but the QPL handler sits *above* that point, so control reached the blind `fixed_timeout` sleep. The `tcp_qpl_poll` loop is now extracted into `_hold_tcp_qpl_poll(settings)` and called directly from the `verbose_push` `except`.
- **#115** — `manual_file` waited forever for a stop file. It is now bounded by the `fixed_timeout_minutes` ceiling (default 180).
- **#116** — `http_poll` / `tcp_qpl_poll` ran to the 240-minute timeout when the OPPO became unreachable. They now end the hold after `MAX_CONSECUTIVE_POLL_FAILURES` (5) connection failures. A graceful no-response (recv timeout) still does **not** count as a failure.

## Tests

`tests/test_hold_robustness.py` (4): verbose_push fallback polls `#QPL` (not the blind sleep); manual_file returns at the ceiling; http_poll + tcp_qpl_poll abort after 5 failures.

## Gates (software-verified only; hardware validation not claimed)

- `pytest` **967 passed / 3 skipped**
- serial coverage **99%** (≥ 99% floor; new branches covered)
- `ruff check` + `ruff format --check` (changed files) clean
- mypy strict gate **49 files, 0 errors**

On-device verification steps are queued in `docs/MANUAL_VERIFICATION_CHECKLIST.md` (Phase A). Only the operator closes the issues.

### #122 — feat(configurator): Step 5 auto-enables a Sony AV receiver (PSK + ack) [MERGED]
## What

Step 5 mapped a Sony receiver to the add-on's `sony_audio_api` backend but always wrote `avr_control_enabled=false` — Sony was the one native backend the configurator couldn't turn on. Its Audio Control API path is gated (in the add-on) on an experimental **acknowledgement** + a **PSK** that the wizard never captured. This wires those in, giving Sony the same auto-enable as Denon/Yamaha/Onkyo/Pioneer.

This is AVR follow-up #1 from handoff §3b item 6. **No add-on change** — `sony_avr_experimental_acknowledged` / `sony_avr_psk` / `sony_avr_player_input_uri` already exist in `resources/settings.xml:135–138`.

## Changes

- **`state.ts`** — new `WizardState` fields `avrSonyAcknowledged` / `avrSonyPsk` / `avrSonyPlayerInputUri` (+ `INITIAL_STATE` defaults).
- **`screens/step5.tsx`** — the Sony branch of the Receiver-control card now shows a **Sony API input URI** field, a **password-masked PSK** field, and an experimental-acknowledgement toggle; the callout flips to "we'll enable" only when the gate is satisfied.
- **`mapping.ts`** — `avrSettings()` emits the three `sony_avr_*` settings and sets `avr_control_enabled=true` for `sony_audio_api` **only** when acknowledgement + PSK + input URI + host + player input are all present — mirroring the add-on's own Sony gate (`avr_presets.py` `requires_experimental_acknowledgement` + sensitive fields; `avr_control.py` Sony validation). Non-Sony and custom_command paths unchanged (frozen by `mapping.test.ts`).
- **`MANUAL_VERIFICATION_CHECKLIST.md`** — Phase-A/C entry.

## Verification (software-only)

- `npm test` → **103 vitest passed** (mapping **24**, incl. Sony enable + ack/PSK/URI partial-gate cases); `npm run build` (`tsc -b` + `vite build`) clean.
- **Rendered in Vite preview**: Step 5 → Sony → model → the URI + PSK (`type=password`) fields + acknowledgement toggle render; filling IP + input + URI + PSK and ticking ack flips the callout from the warn "stays off" state to the green *"We'll enable Sony control with sony_audio_api: … switch to extInput:hdmi?port=2"*.
- **Not hardware-validated.** The Sony Audio Control API driver is experimental and all AVR mappings are `validated:false` candidates — confirm against a real Sony receiver (Phase C).

### #120 — fix(configurator): Sony brand badge visible (dark chip for light marks) [MERGED]
## What

The configurator's real brand marks (`BrandIcon`) are drawn in each brand's own color on `.brand-logo-mark`, whose chip background is hard-coded white. Sony's Simple Icons brand color is `#FFFFFF`, so the **Sony badge rendered white-on-white (invisible)** on the TV brand picker (Step 3) and the AV Receiver picker (Step 5). Flagged in PR #99 + the v0.2.0/v0.5.0 build notes (`styles.css:769`).

## Fix

- `BrandIcon.tsx`: detect a near-white mark by perceived luminance (`0.299R+0.587G+0.114B > 200`) and tag it with `brand-logo-mark-dark`.
- `styles.css`: `.brand-logo-mark-dark` (and its `.brand-pill.selected` variant) gets a fixed warm-dark chip `#1A1612` — theme-independent, so the white mark stays visible in both light and dark themes.
- Colored marks (Samsung/LG/Roku/Panasonic/OPPO) are untouched — they keep the white chip they need.

Smallest viable change: only marks that would be invisible get the dark chip; no change to the colored-mark path.

## Verification (software-only)

- `npm test` → **101 vitest passed**; `npm run build` (`tsc -b` + `vite build`) clean.
- **Rendered in Vite preview** and inspected the live DOM on Step 3 (TV):
  - Sony pill → `class="… brand-logo-mark brand-logo-mark-dark"`, computed `background-color: rgb(26,22,18)` (`#1A1612`), svg `fill="#FFFFFF"` → **visible**.
  - Samsung/LG/Roku/Panasonic → plain `brand-logo-mark` (white chip), unchanged.
- Not installed from a packaged binary; no hardware involved. Cosmetic-only.

### #118 — feat(addon): read-only OPPO player-status probe (#Q.. queries) [MERGED]
## What

A **read-only OPPO player-status probe** plus a protocol reference — the documented basis for #113 (verify the OPPO actually played the requested file).

- `oppo_control.probe_player_status(settings, *, send=None, http=None)` — sends the documented OPPO UDP-20X `#Q..` query battery (`QPW/QPL/QFN/QFT/QTK/QCH/QTE/QTR/QEL/QRE/QDT/QAT/QST/QIS/QHD/QVR`) over one TCP:23 connection, classifies each reply (`OK`/`ER`/no-response, **preserving #QFN file-name case**), and best-effort attaches the raw HTTP `/getmovieplayinfo` payload. Plus `format_player_status_probe()` and a non-raising `_classify_probe_response()`.
- `installer.py` — new menu action **"Probe OPPO player status (diagnostic)"** (appended at index 13 before Cancel; existing menu indices unchanged) → shows the parsed replies in a textviewer and saves `addon_data/oppo-status-probe.txt`.
- `docs/OPPO_PROTOCOL_REFERENCE.md` — transcribes the query/verbose tables from OPPO's RS-232 & IP Control Protocol (Dec 2017).
- `tests/test_oppo_status_probe.py` — 13 tests.

## Why

The add-on hands a file/disc to the OPPO and then holds Kodi's slot, but never confirms the OPPO actually started playing (see #114–#117). The documented `#QFN` (Query media file name) reads the **current media file name** over the control channel — so #113's "did it play the requested file?" can be answered against the **documented** protocol rather than the undocumented HTTP app API. This PR delivers the read-only probe that empirically confirms what a given firmware reports; the #113 verify wiring is a follow-up built on its findings.

## Scope / safety

- **No change** to playback routing, OPPO command payloads, or the 5 hold modes — read-only queries only.
- `#QFN`/`#QFT` apply to media files (NAS/USB); a physical disc returns `ER INVALID`, so fall back to `#QDT`/`#QTK`. Replies are <=25 bytes, so long names truncate with `*` -> match by prefix.

## Verification (software-only)

- `pytest` **963 passed / 3 skipped** (pre-existing POSIX-only skips)
- coverage **99%** (>=99 gate, exit 0); probe code fully covered
- `ruff check` + `ruff format` clean; `mypy` strict clean on both gated files
- **Hardware validation not performed.** Phase C steps (run the probe on the real Kodi box + OPPO during a NAS-ISO and a tray-disc playback; record what `#QFN`/`#QDT` return) are in `docs/MANUAL_VERIFICATION_CHECKLIST.md`.

Relates to #113. Draft — promote when verified.

🤖 Generated with [Claude Code](https://claude.com/claude-code)

### #110 — Wire AVR Step 5 into add-on settings; release configurator v0.5.0 [MERGED]
## Summary

Follow-up to the AVR database (v0.4.0): the **Step 5 (AV Receiver) selection now flows into the
add-on's `settings.xml`**, giving the receiver step true parity with the TV and Player steps
(which already write `tv_backend` / `oppo_hardware_model` etc.). Previously Step 5 was
display-only. Then cuts **configurator v0.5.0**.

### What's new
- **Step 5 captures receiver IP + player input** (`avrIp`, `avrPlayerInput` in `WizardState`),
  shown in a "Receiver control" card once a model is picked.
- **`mapping.ts` emits AVR settings** — new `avrAddonBackend()` maps the DB's backend vocabulary
  onto the add-on's `avr_backend` enum, with two deliberate fix-ups verified against
  `resources/lib/avr/avr_presets.py`:
  - **Pioneer** (the DB folds it into `onkyo_eiscp`) → the add-on's distinct `pioneer_eiscp` driver, by brand.
  - **Sony** (`sony_audio` in the DB) → `sony_audio_api`.
- **Conservative enable.** `avr_control_enabled=true` only for a native, non-gated driver
  (Denon/Marantz, Yamaha, Onkyo/Integra, Pioneer) **with host + player input present**. Sony is
  configured but left **disabled** (the add-on gates it on an experimental acknowledgement + PSK
  the wizard doesn't capture). `custom_command` brands (Anthem/Arcam/NAD) write **no**
  `avr_backend` — the add-on has no native driver and its own validator would reject the value.
- **Skipping Step 5 writes nothing AVR-related**, so it never disturbs an existing add-on AVR
  config (the merge in `settings_xml.ts` preserves un-owned settings).

### Verification
- `tsc -b` ✓ · `npm run build` ✓ · `npm run test` — **105 passed** (13 new mapping tests) ✓
- Browser-preview pass: Pioneer → `pioneer_eiscp` with the enable callout after filling the
  input; Sony → `sony_audio_api` with the "needs ack + PSK, left off" callout; no console errors.
- `npm run dist` → MSI + NSIS; sizes + SHA-256 in `release-evidence/v0.5.0/BUILD_NOTES.md`.

### Honesty
**Software-verified only** — unsigned; not installed on a clean machine; no hardware validation.
Enabling AVR control means the add-on will actually try to power on + switch the receiver on
handoff; all backend/input mappings are `validated:false` candidates to confirm against real
hardware.

**`chatgpt-codex-connector[bot]`** · 2026-05-30:

**<sub><sub>![P2 Badge](https://img.shields.io/badge/P2-yellow?style=flat)</sub></sub>  Stop routing QLED models through the ADB warning**

For this newly added Samsung QLED row (and the other new non-ADB rows whose ids contain `q`), selecting it stores `tvBackend: "samsung_command"`, but `Step3AdbWarn` still treats any `tvModel` containing `q` as ADB via `state.tvBackend === "adb" || (state.tvModel || "").includes("q")`. Users with these Samsung/LG/Sony/Hisense Q models are shown USB debugging instructions even though their resolved backend is not ADB, which sends them down the wrong setup path; base the warning only on the resolved backend or stop using `q` in non-ADB ids.

Useful? React with 👍 / 👎.

## 3. Real brand icons

New `src/shell/BrandIcon.tsx` renders the real brand mark from **`simple-icons`** (CC0 SVGs, bundled at build → stays offline-clean); brands the library doesn't carry fall back to a device glyph on the brand color. Adds `simple-icons@^16.21.0`.

> **Trademark note** (repo's conservative posture): the marks are CC0 SVGs used only to identify the user's *actual* device — trademarks remain with their owners, no endorsement implied.

## 4. AGENTS.md norm

Adds "Names must match what the user sees — people read the files": file names / ids / components / comments / labels must track the UI; rename in the same change; `steps.ts` is the source of truth.

## Integration notes

- `simple-icons@16.21.0` does **not** ship `siTcl`, `siHisense`, or `siVizio` (removed upstream). Per the changeset's instructions those three were dropped from `BrandIcon.tsx`'s import + `BRAND_ICONS`, so TCL / Hisense / Vizio render the generic TV-glyph fallback. The other six (Sony, Samsung, LG, Roku, Panasonic, OPPO) render real marks.
- **Heads-up, left as-authored:** `siSony`'s brand color is white (`#FFFFFF`) and `.brand-logo-mark` has a white background (`styles.css:769`), so the Sony mark renders white-on-white (effectively invisible). Flagging for a possible follow-up — not changed here to keep this PR scope-clean.

### #94 — Add a repeatable Windows build recipe for the configurator [MERGED]
## What

First half of "ship the first Windows binary" — make the build **repeatable and
version-guarded** before producing the artifact (follow-up C.2).

## Changes (configurator-only, no app behavior change)

- **`npm run dist`** — alias for `tauri build` (`package.json`).
- **`src/version.test.ts`** — pins the three version sites (`package.json`,
  `src-tauri/Cargo.toml`, `src-tauri/tauri.conf.json`) to the same value, so a build
  can't ship mismatched crate / installer / artifact versions. The configurator-scale
  analogue of the add-on's `sync_version` guard.
- **`src-tauri/.gitattributes`** — keeps `Cargo.toml` LF so the Tauri bundler's CRLF
  rewrite on a Windows build no longer leaves the file showing as modified (observed
  during the de-risk build).
- **`BUILD.md`** — prereqs (→ handoff §2a), the build command, outputs, the versioning +
  `configurator-v*` tag convention, and the unsigned / SmartScreen caveat.

## Verification

### #91 — Split Chinoppo M9205 V1 into a distinct hardware model [MERGED]
## What & why

`M9205 V1` and the plain `M9205` were collapsed onto a single `oppo_hardware_model`
enum value (`chinoppo_m9205`) — a comment in `players.ts` flagged it as pending
maintainer confirmation that they were the same device. **The operator confirmed they
are distinct devices** that share the M9205 eject-to-wake clone control protocol, so
this gives `M9205 V1` its own identity end-to-end.

This is a deliberate cross-area change (one cohesive split, operator-approved) so the
add-on contract and the configurator land together and the configurator never writes an
enum value the add-on does not recognize.

## Add-on (`area:addon`)

- New `oppo_hardware_model` enum value **`chinoppo_m9205_v1`**, **appended** to
  `resources/settings.xml` so existing users' stored enum **indices are unchanged**
  (Kodi `type="enum"` stores by index).
- Wired through the taxonomy as an **exact mirror of `M9205`** (canonical key
  **`M9205-V1`**): `settings_reader.py` (`ENUM_VALUES`, `_HARDWARE_ALIASES`,
  `HARDWARE_COMPAT`, `CHINOPPO_NAS_PLAYBACK_MODELS`), `hardware_profiles.py`
  (`PLAYER_PROFILE_KEYS`, `PROFILE_ALIASES`, `HARDWARE_PROFILES`),
  `hardware_capabilities.py` (`CHINOPPO_STYLE_MODELS`, `CHINOPPO_NAS_PLAYBACK_MODELS`).
- The `M9205-V1` profile = `#EJT` eject-to-wake, clone-safe, `http_api_436=False` —
  identical to `M9205`. **No OPPO command payloads change.** `hardware_presets.py` is
  untouched (plain `M9205` has no preset and falls through to `generic_oppo_clone`; the
  V1 mirrors that).

## Configurator (`area:configurator`)

- `players.ts`: the **M9205 V1** picker label now maps to `chinoppo_m9205_v1`; plain
  **M9205** still maps to `chinoppo_m9205`. The "Other / clone" eject-to-wake default is
  unchanged. Removed the now-resolved "pending confirmation" comment.
- `CONFIGURATOR_HANDOFF.md` §4 enum order updated to match `settings.xml`.

## Tests

- New `tests/test_chinoppo_m9205_v1_split.py` (5 tests): enum membership, alias
  normalization to `M9205-V1`, profile mirrors `M9205`, registry class, capability gates,
  and `#PON`/`#POW` to `#EJT` resolution.
- Updated taxonomy guards: `test_all.py` (17 to 18), `test_v2910_build2` (17 to 18),
  `test_v2910_build3` (set + `M9205-V1`); configurator `players.test.ts` /
  `mapping.test.ts` now assert M9205 V1 and M9205 are distinct.

## Verification (software only — no hardware validation claimed)

- Add-on: `pytest -n auto` **943 passed / 3 skipped**; coverage **99.06%** (>= 99 gate);
  `ruff check` + `ruff format` clean; `mypy --gate` **49/0**.
- Configurator: `tsc --noEmit` clean; `vitest` **63/63**; `npm run build` exit 0.

On-device (Phase C) steps are queued in `docs/MANUAL_VERIFICATION_CHECKLIST.md`. No
tracked issue — PR-only delivery of the configurator §3b "M9205 V1 vs M9205" follow-up.
Draft until the operator verifies.

### #88 — configurator: cleanup (xmlEscape, db_version, TV-switch gate, player catalog) + ENH-#41 Part C [MERGED]
## Configurator cleanup + ENH-#41 Part C

Follow-up to the PR #68 review (the high / medium fixes landed in #68). This clears the lower-severity findings plus the configurator side of ENH-#41 Part C.

- **#85** - extract a single shared XML escaper (`src/xml.ts`) used by both `settings.xml` and `playercorefactory.xml` generation; removes two diverged copies.
- **#77** - `tvdb.isNewer` parses `db_version` (YYYY.MM.DD) to a sortable integer instead of comparing raw strings, so an unpadded/reformatted version is not mis-ordered, and an unparseable version is never treated as newer.
- **#86** - `tv_switching_enabled` is written `true` only when a TV backend is configured and the user did not drop to manual, so a no-TV setup does not switch against the add-on default backend.
- **#87** - single source of truth for the player brand/model catalog (`src/players.ts`): `mapping.ts` and the Step 3 picker both derive from it, so a model added in one place cannot silently fail to map. Folds in the `isClone` posture dedup; the M9205 V1 / M9205 collapse now lives in one place (still pending maintainer confirmation that they are the same device).
- **ENH-#41 Part C (configurator side)** - write a static provenance marker into the generated `settings.xml`, pairing with the add-on's "managed by the configurator" overwrite warning.

## Verification (software only)
- `tsc -b` + `vite build` clean; **63 vitest tests**; no Rust changes (cargo unaffected); the add-on 99% coverage gate ran green on push (938 passed, 3 skipped).
- On-device verification steps added to `docs/MANUAL_VERIFICATION_CHECKLIST.md` (Phase C).

Implementing SHAs are commented on each issue. Issues left open for the operator to verify and close (only the operator closes issues).

### #68 — configurator: wire the wizard to the add-on contract (slices 1-7) [MERGED]
Wires the existing 23-screen configurator UI to the add-on, per configurator/CONFIGURATOR_HANDOFF.md. Delivered as 7 commits (one per slice) on this branch; the add-on (resources/, service.py) is unchanged.

## Slices
1. State to setting-ID mapper (mapping.ts) + screen-resume persistence + Step-1 architecture chooser + brand-to-model fix.
2. Data-driven TV model DB (docs/configurator/tv-db/tv-models.json, hybrid lineup + per-model schema) + tvdb.ts loader/resolver + on-demand GitHub refresh.
3. File generation (generate.ts: playercorefactory.xml + keymap reimplemented from installer.py) + Rust generate_files/reveal_path + Tier C Generate-and-save.
4. settings.xml serializer + DOM playercorefactory merge (mirrors playercorefactory_merge.py) + Rust SMB deploy/read/write-test commands + Tier B real write probe.
5. Real connectivity probes (probes.ts + Rust tcp_probe / tv_port_probe / oppo_query) wired into Step 2 (TV port probe + backend inference) and Step 3 (OPPO #QPW wake-and-confirm).
6. Tier A SSH deploy + Kodi restart via the system OpenSSH client (ssh_test / deploy_ssh, key auth) + Step-1 Tier A test wiring.
7. End-of-wizard Apply to Kodi (apply.ts): composes settings.xml + merged playercorefactory + keymap and deploys via the chosen tier.

## Decisions captured (handoff Q and A)
- A: file templates reimplemented in the configurator (add-on generators are Kodi-bound Python).
- B: settings written as direct files over SFTP/SMB (no add-on endpoint); written before the Tier A restart / while Kodi is stopped.
- C: the playback-architecture choice is surfaced on the Step-1 Kodi-box screen.
- D: TV DB schema = hybrid lineup + per-model rows, hosted under docs/configurator/tv-db/.
- E: test ISO uses a placeholder until the real asset is provided.

## Verification
- tsc -b + vite build clean; cargo check clean (std-only Rust, no new crates).
- 46 vitest unit tests (mapping, tvdb, generate, settings_xml, merge, probes, apply).
- The add-on coverage gate ran green on every push (938 passed, 99.07%); this branch touches only configurator/ and docs/.
- NOT exercised against real hardware (Kodi box / OPPO / TV) and NOT run in the live app this session. Software-verified only; hardware validation not claimed.

## Notes for review
- Tier A SSH is non-interactive (BatchMode): key auth only; password auth via the bundled path is unsupported on Windows (use a key, or Tier B / C). The system OpenSSH client must be present.
- Tier A apply writes a fresh playercorefactory with a remote .bak (no remote read-back); Tier B reads + merges the existing one. Both back up before writing.
- The Chinoppo "M9205 V1" vs "M9205" collapse to chinoppo_m9205 still needs confirmation.
- The TV DB model seed is small and all validated:false; lineup rules carry the platform-to-backend mapping. Brands without seeded models fall through to the not-found probe path.
- The design archive (attached zip) was reviewed from a temp dir; it is not committed here (already on main as the configurator zip).

### #64 — ENH-#51: gate the settings_reader + oppo_control hubs (mypy --strict PR 5) [MERGED]
Part of #51 (mypy `--strict` rollout). **PR 5 — the two hubs.** Annotates the
two heaviest un-migrated modules to zero strict errors and gates them
(**33 -> 35**): `kodi/settings_reader` (72 errors) and `oppo/oppo_control`
(111 errors). These are the hubs the cascade group depends on, so this unblocks
the remaining oppo/kodi dependents in PR 6+.

> **Stacked on #63 (PR 4).** Base is the PR 4 branch; **merge #63 first.** Per the
> rollout's stacking note, the test/types/coverage CI jobs only run on PRs
> targeting `main`, so they will appear once #63 merges and GitHub retargets this
> PR. Verified locally instead (below).

### Key decisions
- **`Settings.get` / `Settings.__getitem__` now return `Any`**, not a concrete
  type. `get` is the raw accessor; the typed accessors (`get_str` / `get_int` /
  `get_bool` / `get_float` / `get_path`) carry concrete return types. This matches
  how callers use them (immediate coercion) and avoids a cascade of false errors
  at every `settings.get(...)` site in oppo_control. settings_reader's own
  internal use still type-checks.
- oppo_control imports `Settings` under `if TYPE_CHECKING:` — annotation-only, no
  runtime import or import cycle.
- `HARDWARE_COMPAT` annotated `dict[str, dict[str, object]]` so indexing returns a
  dict (mypy infers `object` from its heterogeneous inner dicts otherwise).
- A `dict[str, Any]` pin on the firmware-status result clears a var-annotated +
  union-attr + assignment cluster in one place.
- `cast` on `urlopen().read()` bytes and object-typed settings-metadata values;
  one loop variable renamed to avoid a reuse type clash.

`get_lines` now coerces via `get_str` (equivalent for string settings).
**Annotations / casts only — no behavior change.**

### Verification (software-only)
- `mypy --gate`: **35 modules / 0 errors**
- `pytest -n auto`: **938 passed, 3 skipped**
- coverage: **99.04%** (>= 99% floor)
- `ruff check` + `ruff format --check`: clean

Opened as **draft** for operator review. Does not close #51 (multi-PR rollout).

### #63 — ENH-#51: extend mypy --strict gate to 5 import-fallback modules (PR 4) [MERGED]
Part of #51 (mypy `--strict` rollout). **PR 4** — resolves the `no-redef`
import-fallback idiom blocker called out in handoff §3a and gates the 5 leaf
modules whose only remaining errors were that idiom plus co-located fixes.
Gate allowlist **28 -> 33** modules, all at zero strict errors.

### The import-fallback strategy (the decision §3a flagged)
The ENH-#43 lib split left modules with a `try:` (canonical dotted import) /
`except ImportError:` (bare top-level import) fallback. Under `--strict` the
except branch redefines each name -> `no-redef`.

**Decision:** suppress *only* the except-branch (runtime-fallback) import with a
targeted `# type: ignore[no-redef]`. The canonical dotted import stays fully
type-checked; the bare fallback (used by sys.path-based importers / the test
suite) is the line annotated as intentionally redefining. Zero runtime change,
smallest diff, consistent with the pre-existing ignore on the disc_classification
fallback.

### Modules added
- `resources/lib/__init__.py` — annotated the lazy alias finder/loader; `cast`
  the loader to `importlib.abc.Loader` at the `ModuleSpec` call.
- `resources/lib/avr/avr_control.py`
- `resources/lib/kodi/intercept.py` — `_FsLike` Protocol for the duck-typed `fs`
  param; `# type: ignore[attr-defined]` for constants re-exported through the
  disc_classification shared-constants hub (names exist at runtime).
- `resources/lib/oppo/oppo_tcp_client.py`
- `resources/lib/tv/tv_diagnostics.py` — `dict`->`dict` `@overload` on
  `sanitize_payload` (the avr_diagnostics precedent).

Common fixes: `cast` object-typed settings-metadata dict values before iterating;
removed stale `# type: ignore` comments `--strict` now flags unused.
**Annotations / ignores only - no behavior change.**

### Verification (software-only)
- `mypy --gate`: **33 modules / 0 errors**
- `pytest -n auto`: **938 passed, 3 skipped**
- coverage: **99.04%** (>= 99% floor)
- `ruff check .` + `ruff format --check`: clean

Opened as **draft** for operator review. Does not close #51 (multi-PR rollout).

**`chatgpt-codex-connector[bot]`** · 2026-05-29:

**<sub><sub>![P2 Badge](https://img.shields.io/badge/P2-yellow?style=flat)</sub></sub>  Load testmon when plugin autoload is disabled**

In shells that follow the repo's documented coverage/pre-push workflow, `PYTEST_DISABLE_PLUGIN_AUTOLOAD=1` is left in the environment (`scripts/hooks/pre-push` exports it, and `pytest --help` documents that it disables plugin auto-loading). Copying `os.environ` through here means pytest never auto-loads pytest-testmon, so the wrapper's `--testmon` option is rejected as an unrecognized argument until the user manually unsets the variable. Clear that variable for this subprocess or explicitly load the testmon plugin.

### #56 — Expand mypy --strict allowlist to 28 modules (ENH-#51 PR 3) [MERGED]
## ENH-#51 PR 3 — the `avr_*` strict type-fix backends (allowlist 23 → 28)

Third PR of the source-only `mypy --strict` rollout (PR 1 = #53; PR 2 = #54, now merged).
Annotates the five remaining AVR backends to **zero strict errors** and adds them to the
gate `files=` allowlist. No gate/tooling/CI changes — those landed in PR 1.

> Recreated from #55, which GitHub auto-closed when its base branch (the PR 2 branch) was
> deleted on merge. Same branch (`claude/enh51-mypy-pr3-avr-x7m2k9q4`), same commits
> (`d36e76f` + checklist `6062712`), now targeting `main`.

### What's in this batch — 5 modules, 34 strict errors cleared (type-only)

- **`avr_denon_marantz` / `avr_onkyo_eiscp`** (`attr-defined` ×4): the per-command socket
  was typed `object`, so `sendall`/`recv` didn't resolve. Annotated as the module's existing
  `SocketLike` Protocol and `cast()` the socket-factory result.
- **`avr_yamaha`** / **`avr_sony_audio`**: pinned `urlopen().read()` to `bytes`; `cast()` the
  `int()` / `list()` / `map()` inputs and the `meta.get()` warning/missing tuples that type
  as `object`.
- **`avr_diagnostics`** (13× `no-any-return`): `dict -> dict` `@overload` on `sanitize_payload`
  so the dict-returning helpers stop leaking `Any`; one local pinned; 2 stale `# type: ignore`
  removed. Coverage unaffected (0 missed).

Both `mypy.ini` (authoritative) and the `pyproject.toml` mirror updated in lockstep.

### Latent Python 3.9 import bug fixed along the way

The `HttpGet` / `SonyPost` aliases used PEP 604 `bytes | str`. These are **module-level
assignments** (eagerly evaluated — not lazied by `from __future__ import annotations`), so on
the project's **3.9 floor** they raise `TypeError` at import. The full suite runs on 3.11 and
the 3.9 compat-smoke job doesn't import these modules, so it was latent. Switched to
`typing.Union`.

### Verification (software-only; hardware validation not claimed)

- `tools/type_check.py --gate` → **28 source files clean, 0 errors**.
- `pytest -n auto` → **933 passed, 3 skipped** (unchanged count).
- `coverage report` → **TOTAL 99%** (floor held; `avr_diagnostics` 0 missed).
- `ruff check .` + `ruff format --check .` → clean.
- `unittest discover` → **551 OK**.
- `py_compile` + `sync_version` / `test_layout` / `i18n_extract` / `render_docs --check` → all OK.

Implementing SHA `d36e76f` (operator checklist entry `6062712`). Part of ENH-#51 (#51).

assignments** (eagerly evaluated — *not* lazied by `from __future__ import annotations`,

### #53 — Enable incremental mypy --strict gate (ENH-#51 PR 1) [MERGED]
﻿PR 1 of the source-only `mypy --strict` rollout tracked by ENH-#51. It stands up the strict **gate + tooling** and annotates the first **leaf-module batch**; the remaining ~28 modules follow in later PRs.

## Why incremental
`mypy --strict --python-version 3.9` on `resources/lib` reports a **788-error / 35-module** baseline (274 `no-untyped-def` driving 390 `no-untyped-call`, plus 34 `no-redef` from the ENH-#43 lazy-import idiom). A wholesale flip is not reviewable, so this PR enforces strict only on a curated allowlist and grows it module-by-module.

## Mechanism
- **`mypy.ini`** (authoritative) + **`pyproject.toml [tool.mypy]`** mirror:
  - `python_version` **3.10 -> 3.9** — the mypy config was the lone holdout; everything else targets 3.9 (`ruff target-version = py39`, `requires-python = ">=3.9"`, the compat-smoke matrix).
  - `strict = True`, **`follow_imports = silent`** (the key piece: allowlisted modules type-check fully and get correct types from imports, but not-yet-annotated modules do not block), and a `files = [...]` **allowlist** of the 7 modules below.
  - Dropped the now-unused `[mypy-tests.*]` / `tests.*` override (no invocation type-checks tests; `warn_unused_configs` flagged it).
- **`tools/type_check.py`** gains a blocking **`--gate`** mode: runs mypy with no explicit targets (so the config `files` apply) and returns mypy''s real exit code. The **default invocation stays non-blocking** for release safety, and `build_mypy_command` still targets `resources/lib`, so the build-13 baseline guard tests keep passing.
- **CI**: new **`types`** job runs `python tools/type_check.py --gate` (3.11 runner; mypy targets 3.9). Suitable as a required check.

## First leaf batch (zero strict errors)
All four buckets represented; changes are signatures + removing stale `# type: ignore` + two pinned locals (`raw: float`, `body: str`) -- **no logic changes**:
`avr/avr_sequence`, `kodi/keymap_skin`, `tv/smartthings_control`, `tv/roku_ecp_control`, `oppo/reconnect_backoff`, `oppo/autoscript_helper`, `tv/adb_control`.

`nas_playback_adapter` was deliberately **deferred** -- its calls cascade into `settings_reader` + `oppo_control` (the two heaviest modules).

## Guard tests (updated in lockstep)
- `test_v291_build13_type_hint_baseline.py`: `python_version` assertion 3.10 -> 3.9; adds strict / `follow_imports` / `files` + gate-command-shape assertions.
- `test_github_readiness_g6_ci_hardening.py`: expects the `types` job and the gate command in CI.

## Verification (software-verified only; hardware validation not performed / not claimed)
- `pytest -n auto`: **933 passed, 3 skipped**
- serial coverage: **99%** (floor held)
- `ruff check .` + `ruff format --check .`: clean
- `mypy --gate`: clean (7 modules, 0 errors); default non-blocking run still exits 0
- `unittest discover`: **551 OK**
- `audit_release`: **580/580**; py_compile + render_docs/sync_version/test_layout/i18n `--check`: green

No runtime code paths, settings, or hardware behavior change -- typing config / dev tooling / CI only.

Draft for Phase A review (`docs/MANUAL_VERIFICATION_CHECKLIST.md` updated). Implementing SHA commented on the issue.

### #52 — configurator: real app icon + first MSI/NSIS bundle [MERGED]
## Summary

Replaces the placeholder configurator icon with a real icon set and verifies the
app bundles end-to-end on Windows for the first time.

`configurator/src-tauri/tauri.conf.json` `bundle.icon` referenced four files
(`32x32.png`, `128x128.png`, `icon.icns`, `icon.ico`), but only a 766-byte
placeholder `icon.ico` (PR #35) existed on disk — so a release `tauri build`
would have failed on the three missing files.

## What changed

- **Real icon set** generated from the repo-root add-on artwork (`icon.png`,
  256x256) via `cd configurator; npm run tauri -- icon ..\icon.png`. The
  operator chose to reuse the add-on art for this first pass.
- Committed the **standard Tauri desktop set only** — icon PNG sizes +
  `Square*Logo.png` / `StoreLogo.png` (Windows Store) + `icon.icns`. The `ios/`
  and `android/` folders `tauri icon` also emits were pruned (Windows desktop
  app). `tauri.conf.json` itself is unchanged.
- Refreshed the stale placeholder `src-tauri/icons/README.md`.
- Added a Phase A/C entry to `docs/MANUAL_VERIFICATION_CHECKLIST.md`.

## Build verification (software-verified only)

`cd configurator; npm run tauri -- build` -> **exit 0**, release compile ~1m13s,
**2 bundles produced** (under `configurator/src-tauri/target/release/`):

| Artifact | Path | Size |
|---|---|---|
| MSI (WiX) | `bundle\msi\OppoKodiAddon Configurator_0.1.0_x64_en-US.msi` | 3.0 MB |
| NSIS setup | `bundle\nsis\OppoKodiAddon Configurator_0.1.0_x64-setup.exe` | 1.9 MB |
| raw exe | `oppokodiaddon-configurator.exe` | 8.4 MB |

(`target/` is gitignored — artifacts are not committed.)

## Caveats

- The add-on art is a busy, text-heavy promo image, so the 32x32 taskbar icon is
  cluttered. Swap in a purpose-built 1024x1024 PNG and re-run `tauri icon` to
  improve.
- 256x256 source means the macOS `icon.icns` and larger Store logos are
  upscaled; the Windows MSI/NSIS bundle only uses sizes <=256, so its icons are
  not upscaled.
- **Software-verified only**: build + bundle succeeded; installed-app behaviour
  and on-screen icon appearance are not yet verified (see Phase C in the
  checklist).

### #50 — Enforce ruff across the whole codebase (ENH-#38) [MERGED]
Phase 1 of the ruff + mypy enforcement rollout (resolves ENH-#38). Makes `ruff check .` + `ruff format --check .` clean across the **whole** Python codebase and enforces both in CI on every PR.

## What

Ruff previously covered only source (CI ran `ruff check resources default.py service.py`); `ruff check .` reported **246 findings** confined to `tests/` (235), `tools/` (22), and `conftest.py`. This PR clears them and widens enforcement.

- **Config consolidation** — `ruff.toml` stays the authoritative standalone config (kept per the `test_github_readiness_g5` "legacy config files remain" test, matching the project's `.coveragerc` pattern); the `pyproject [tool.ruff]` mirror is brought in sync so the two can't drift. Added rule family **C4**; `tests/**` get per-file-ignores `F401, F811, B011` (import-for-side-effect, fixture redefinition, assert-False).
- **Findings cleared** — `ruff check --fix` (+ unsafe fixes for `UP022` / statement-splits) and `ruff format`. The compound one-liners (`E701`/`E702`, ~70) were resolved by `ruff format` splitting them. **80 files reformatted** (tests/tools/conftest only — source was already format-clean, so there is no source diff).
- **CI** — the lint job now runs `ruff check .` and `ruff format --check .` (was scoped to `resources default.py service.py`).

## Verification (software-verified only)

- `ruff check .` → **All checks passed**; `ruff format --check .` → clean.
- `pytest -n auto` **932 passed, 3 skipped** (unchanged); serial coverage **99%** (unchanged — no source touched); `unittest discover` green; config-guard tests (`test_ruff_config_present`, g5 legacy-remain + pyproject-carries) green.
- **No source files changed** → no runtime/behavioral impact.

The mypy `--strict` rollout follows as a separate series of PRs (source-only, curated allowlist).

### #49 — Add in-add-on add-on-language switcher (ENH-#42, language) [2/2] [MERGED]
Part 2 of 2 for ENH-#42 (#42). **Stacked on #48** (base = the network-editor branch) because both touch `installer.main()` and the menu-shape test — **merge #48 first**, then GitHub retargets this PR to `main`.

## What

A new **"Add-on language"** entry in `installer.main()` that pins the add-on language to a bundled locale or the **"Follow Kodi system language"** sentinel (the default), persisted in a hidden `addon_language` setting (driven from the add-on menu, not Kodi's settings panel).

- **`i18n.supported_languages()` fixed 7 → 12** — it was stale, omitting ja/ko/pl/pt/ru.
- **`effective_language()`** resolves the setting; for follow-Kodi it maps `xbmc.getLanguage()` → a bundled locale (en_gb fallback). The acceptance criterion "follow Kodi path tested with a stub" is covered.
- **`L()` consults a pinned locale's `strings.po` first**, else the existing Kodi/default path (unchanged for follow-Kodi, so the existing configurator-owner notifications behave exactly as before).

## Honest caveat (please read)

The 12 bundled non-en_gb `strings.po` files are currently **English placeholders** (msgstr == msgid), and Kodi renders `settings.xml` labels in its **own** GUI language. So pinning a locale changes the source file `L()` consults but does **not** yet change visible text — the mechanism is forward-compatible for when translations are populated. Today only the configurator-owner notifications (ids 30290–30293) route through `L()`. I kept the switcher because the issue + acceptance criteria call for it, but I'm flagging the limited current surface per the honest-signature norm.

## Tests

- `tests/test_v2914_build3_language_switcher.py` — 25 tests: supported-languages, options, `effective_language` (incl. follow-Kodi via stubbed `xbmc.getLanguage`, ISO/English-name/prefix/unknown/raises/missing/no-xbmc paths), `L()` pinned-vs-follow + fall-through, `.po` cache, menu persist + dispatch.
- `tests/test_all.py` — supported-languages 7→12, settings count 98→99.
- `tests/test_coverage_hardening.py` — menu-shape 12→13 choices.
- `docs/MANUAL_VERIFICATION_CHECKLIST.md` — Phase A + Phase C steps.

## Verification (software-verified only; hardware validation not claimed)

`pytest -n auto` **932 passed, 3 skipped**; serial coverage **99.10%** (`i18n.py` **100%**); `ruff check` + `ruff format --check resources default.py service.py` clean; `unittest discover` 551 OK; `audit_release` 578/578; doc/version/layout/i18n `--check` all green.

Run: `cd C:\Users\rigel\Documents\gitrepo\script.oppo203.iso.external; .venv\Scripts\python.exe -m pytest --basetemp=build\_pt -q tests\test_v2914_build3_language_switcher.py`

### #48 — Add in-add-on network settings menu (ENH-#42, IP editor) [1/2] [MERGED]
Part 1 of 2 for ENH-#42 (#42). This PR adds the in-add-on **network/IP viewer-editor**; the language switcher follows as PR 2.

## What

A new menu entry **"Network settings (TV / OPPO / AVR / Kodi)"** in `installer.main()` that lets a user view and override the configurator-managed connection fields without leaving Kodi — e.g. to nudge an IP after a router reboot or DHCP reassignment.

- **Backend-aware fields** — always OPPO IP/port + TV IP, then the active `tv_backend`'s host fields (ADB port + path / Sony PSK / Roku ECP port / SmartThings token + device id), plus AVR host/port when AVR is enabled or a backend is selected (+ Sony AVR PSK for `sony_audio_api`).
- **Enum normalization** — a backend stored as a numeric index (`"1"`) resolves to its value (`"sony_bravia"`) via `settings_reader.ENUM_VALUES`, matching how the reader normalizes.
- **Managed-by-configurator marker** — every editable key is in `service.CONFIGURATOR_MANAGED_KEYS`, so a top `[Managed by the configurator]` row explains overrides may be overwritten, and each successful edit repeats the note (consistent with the ENH-#41 Part C policy).
- **Safety** — empty/unchanged input is a no-op (won't clear a value); non-numeric port input is rejected.
- **Kodi box address** — shown **read-only**; there is no in-add-on setting for it (configurator-owned when the add-on is deployed remotely).

Per open question #2, this exposes per-backend host fields (operator's call), not only `tv_ip`.

## Tests

- `tests/test_v2914_build2_network_settings_menu.py` — 21 new tests: menu entry + dispatch, backend-aware field list incl. enum-index normalization, edit/write-back, invalid-port rejection, no-op, read-only Kodi row, managed marker.
- `tests/test_coverage_hardening.py` — menu-shape test updated 11→12 choices.
- `docs/MANUAL_VERIFICATION_CHECKLIST.md` — Phase A + Phase C steps added for the operator.

## Verification (software-verified only; hardware validation not claimed)

`pytest -n auto` **907 passed, 3 skipped**; serial coverage **99.08%** (≥99% floor; `installer.py` 99%, new code fully covered); `ruff check` + `ruff format --check resources default.py service.py` clean; `unittest discover` 526 OK; `audit_release` 578/578; doc/version/layout/i18n `--check` all green.

Run: `cd C:\Users\rigel\Documents\gitrepo\script.oppo203.iso.external; .venv\Scripts\python.exe -m pytest --basetemp=build\_pt -q tests\test_v2914_build2_network_settings_menu.py`

### #47 — refactor(addon): split resources/lib into tv/oppo/avr/kodi sub-packages (ENH-#43) [MERGED]
## ENH-#43 — split `resources/lib` into hardware-family sub-packages

Implements [ENH-#43](https://github.com/skull-01/script.oppo203.iso.external/issues/43).
Moves all 46 `resources/lib/*.py` modules into four sub-packages so the controlled family
is obvious from each diff path. **File moves + import rewiring only — no function or public
API renames.**

```
resources/lib/
  __init__.py        <- compat alias finder (the only new logic)
  tv/    (7)   adb_control, roku_ecp_control, smartthings_control, tv_backends, tv_control, tv_diagnostics, tv_presets
  oppo/  (14)  oppo_control, oppo_remote, oppo_tcp_client, command_map, constants, discovery, reconnect_backoff,
               hardware_capabilities, hardware_presets, hardware_profiles, hardware_validation_readiness,
               path_mapper, nas_playback_adapter, autoscript_helper
  avr/   (9)   avr_control, avr_denon_marantz, avr_onkyo_eiscp, avr_presets, avr_sequence, avr_sony_audio,
               avr_types, avr_yamaha, avr_diagnostics
  kodi/  (16)  installer, intercept, disc_classification, settings_reader, settings_schema, keymap_skin,
               playercorefactory_merge, i18n, diagnostic_logging, diagnostic_summary, logging_v116, diagnostics,
               arch_benchmark, preset_manager, external_player, version
```

`default.py` / `service.py` stay at the repo root (Kodi entry points). Git tracked all 46 as
renames (98–100% similarity).

## Backward-compatibility (the deprecation window)

The canonical name is now `resources.lib.<bucket>.<module>`. A lazy `sys.meta_path` finder in
[`resources/lib/__init__.py`](resources/lib/__init__.py) keeps **both** legacy forms working,
each resolving to the **same** module object:

- `from resources.lib.oppo_control import …` / `importlib.import_module("resources.lib.oppo_control")`
- bare `import oppo_control` (used by the conftest-pathed tests, `service.py`, `tools/audit_release.py`)

The finder imports nothing at package-import time — critical because `installer.py` runs
`xbmcaddon.Addon()` at module top, so importing `resources.lib` must stay cheap and must not
drag in Kodi. Aliasing happens only when a legacy name is actually imported. This means the
~20 test files and CI tooling that import `resources.lib.X` need **no changes**.

## Imports

- **Module-top cross-family imports are explicit:** e.g. `external_player` (kodi) now uses
  `from ..oppo.oppo_control import …`, `from ..tv.tv_control import …`, `from ..avr.avr_sequence import …`.
- **Lazy in-function imports stay bare** (`from oppo_control import …`) — they resolve through
  the finder at runtime and keep the existing test mocking (which patches by bare name) working.
- `command_map.py`'s data-file path bumps `parents[1]` → `parents[2]` (the module is one level
  deeper) so it still resolves `resources/data/oppo_command_map.json`.

## `version.py` → `kodi/`

Per the issue decision, `version.py` moved too. Updated every importer of its location:
`tools/sync_version.py` (project-root **sentinel** + import), `.github/workflows/package.yml`,
`scripts/package_release.sh`, `scripts/verify.sh` (py_compile list), `tools/audit_release.py`.
Frozen historical build records under `docs/release-history/` are intentionally left untouched.

## Test-harness changes

- New [`tests/__init__.py`](tests/__init__.py) installs the finder for the
  `python -m unittest discover` path (CI runs this; it does **not** load `conftest.py`).
  `conftest.py` does the same for pytest.
- The Kodi-stub context managers now purge the **canonical** bucket module alongside the legacy
  alias (via [`tests/_support/lib_buckets.py`](tests/_support/lib_buckets.py)) — otherwise the
  finder leaves a stale, stub-bound module (e.g. `installer` with a frozen `ADDON`) cached
  across tests.
- ~70 flat-path literals in tests (`spec_from_file_location("…","resources/lib/X.py")`,
  `.exists()`, ZIP-arcname asserts) updated to bucket paths. `test_all.py`'s "import every lib
  module" smoke test now recurses the buckets.
- 12 `# pragma: no cover` added to now-dead bare-name `except ImportError:` fallback branches —
  the finder gives bare imports canonical (package) context, so the relative `try` succeeds and
  those bare fallbacks are no longer exercised. They remain as defensive compat shims, excluded
  from coverage like the project's existing fallback shims.

## Gates (this session, Windows `.venv`)

| Gate | Result |
|---|---|
| `pytest -n auto` | **865 passed, 3 skipped** |
| serial coverage (99% floor) | **99.07%** (pre-push hook) / 99.04% local |
| `ruff check` + `ruff format --check` (resources, default.py, service.py) | clean |
| `python -m unittest discover -s tests` | **484 OK** |
| `sync_version` / `test_layout` / `i18n_extract` / `render_docs` --check | OK |
| `audit_release --expected-version 2.9.13` | **580/580 PASS** |
| runtime ZIP audit | 70 files, 50 under buckets, `version.py` in `kodi/`, no dev dirs |

## Honest signature

Software-verified only. The import-layout change is exercised by the full suite + the release
audit + a runtime-ZIP build, but the add-on was **not** run against real Kodi/OPPO/TV/AVR
hardware this session. Phase C on-device smoke steps are queued in
[`docs/MANUAL_VERIFICATION_CHECKLIST.md`](docs/MANUAL_VERIFICATION_CHECKLIST.md).

## Out of scope (clean follow-ups)

Function/class renames; splitting `tests/` into `tests/{tv,oppo,avr,kodi}/`; removing the
bare-name `except` fallbacks entirely.
