### #46 — feat(addon): in-add-on configurator-owner hint + overwrite warning (ENH-#41 Parts B+C) [MERGED]
# ENH-#41 Parts B + C — addon-side guidance hint and overwrite warning

Implements the addon-side of [ENH-#41](https://github.com/skull-01/script.oppo203.iso.external/issues/41) Parts B and C. Part A (policy doc) shipped in [#45](https://github.com/skull-01/script.oppo203.iso.external/pull/45); the configurator-side of Part C (writing the `<!-- generated by configurator vX.Y.Z YYYY-MM-DD -->` ownership marker into `settings.xml`) is a separate session in the configurator area.

## What changes

### Part B — guidance on settings open

- **Static lsep banner.** A new `<setting id="config_owner_hint" label="30290" type="lsep"/>` at the top of `<category id="connection">` (the default landing page when the user opens Kodi settings). The banner text is:

  > Most settings here are managed by the Windows configurator app. Changes you make in Kodi may be overwritten the next time the configurator runs. Use the configurator for persistent changes.

- **First-change notification.** `service.Monitor.onSettingsChanged` now shows a short hint notification once per Kodi session:

  > Most settings are managed by the configurator. Changes here may be overwritten.

  The once-per-session gate is the `oppo203_config_hint_shown` property on `xbmcgui.Window(10000)` (the Kodi home window). The property clears on Kodi restart.

### Part C — overwrite warning

- **`CONFIGURATOR_MANAGED_KEYS`** (new constant in `service.py`) — 42 protocol-level integration keys the configurator owns: IPs (`oppo_ip`, `tv_ip`, `avr_host`, `oppo_mac`), ports (`oppo_port`, `oppo_http_port`, `tv_adb_port`, `roku_ecp_port`, `avr_port`), hardware-model selectors (`oppo_hardware_model`, `tv_backend`, `avr_backend`, `selected_avr_preset_id`, `tv_adb_preset`), ADB (`adb_path`, `oppo_input_adb_shell`, `kodi_input_adb_shell`), TV command strings (LG / Samsung / custom / Roku), Sony TV (`sony_psk`, hdmi ports), SmartThings (`smartthings_token`, `smartthings_device_id`, oppo/kodi input ids), AVR sub-keys (`avr_player_input`, `avr_restore_input`, `avr_sound_mode`), Sony AVR (`sony_avr_psk`, api_path, player/restore input uris), and OPPO command sequences (`oppo_start_commands`, `oppo_stop_commands`, `oppo_remote_command_map`).

  Operator-tunable knobs — timeouts (`oppo_socket_timeout`, `kodi_startup_power_on_delay`), retries (`reconnect_max_retries`), bool toggles (`oppo_use_wol`, `tv_switching_enabled`, `avr_control_enabled`), playback timings (`fixed_timeout_minutes`, `http_poll_*`), broadcast addresses, mode enums (`oppo_start_mode`, `oppo_verbose_mode`) — are deliberately **excluded**.

- **Per-key warning.** `Monitor.__init__` snapshots managed-key values at service start. `Monitor.onSettingsChanged` compares current values against the baseline and, for each key that differs, logs at WARNING level:

  > `[OPPO203][SERVICE] Configurator-managed key 'oppo_ip' was overwritten via Kodi UI.`

  and shows a Kodi notification:

  > Setting 'oppo_ip' is managed by the configurator. Re-run the configurator to make this change permanent.

  After firing, the baseline refreshes so the warning is not re-emitted on subsequent unrelated settings changes.

## Kodi-API caveat (vs the ENH-#41 spec wording)

The ENH-#41 §21 Q&A says "first-open-per-session notification". Kodi exposes **no** "settings dialog opened" event — the only `xbmc.Monitor` hook for settings is `onSettingsChanged`, which fires *after* the user saves a change. So this PR implements Part B's notification as "first **change** per session"; the always-visible `lsep` banner is the on-open counterpart that fulfils the "on open" half of the spec. Calling out so the reviewer doesn't think the spec text was dropped.

## Consistency with #40

#40 stripped an earlier `onSettingsChanged` that mutated state (auto-applying compatibility presets on hardware-model change). The `onSettingsChanged` this PR re-introduces is **logging/notification only** — it never mutates add-on state. The class docstring on `Monitor` records this invariant.

## Files touched (17)

- `service.py` — `CONFIGURATOR_MANAGED_KEYS`, `_snapshot_managed_settings`, `_changed_managed_keys`, `_resolve_localized`, `_notify_config_hint_once_per_session`, `_warn_overwritten_managed_keys`, `Monitor.__init__`, `Monitor.onSettingsChanged`.
- `resources/settings.xml` — `<setting id="config_owner_hint" label="30290" type="lsep"/>` at top of `<category id="connection">`.
- 12 PO files — four new strings (`#30290` banner, `#30291` notification body, `#30292` per-key warning template with `{key}` placeholder, `#30293` notification title). Non-en_gb PO files use msgid=msgstr fallback per project convention; translators can update later.
- `tests/test_v2914_build1_config_owner_hint.py` — 21 new tests across `TManagedKeysContent`, `TSnapshotAndDiff`, `TNotificationHelpers`, `TMonitor`, `TSettingsXmlAndPo`.
- `tests/test_all.py` — settings-count assertion 97 → 98 (new lsep adds one row); comment updated.
- `docs/MANUAL_VERIFICATION_CHECKLIST.md` — Phase A entry with Phase C step-by-step on-device verification.

## Gates

- `pytest -n auto --basetemp=build\_pt` → **886 passed, 3 skipped** in ~9.5s (was 865 on `main`; the +21 are this PR's new tests).
- `ruff check service.py tests/test_v2914_build1_config_owner_hint.py` → clean. Repo-wide ruff still shows 257 pre-existing errors, covered by [ENH-#38](https://github.com/skull-01/script.oppo203.iso.external/issues/38) — out of scope here.
- Coverage gate is unchanged (this PR adds production code with tests, no exclusions).

## On-device verification

See the new Phase A entry in `docs/MANUAL_VERIFICATION_CHECKLIST.md` for the six-step on-device verification script (open settings → see banner → change non-managed → notification once → change another non-managed → no notification → change managed → per-key warning + Kodi log line → restart → banner re-fires once).

## Honest signature

Software-verified only. The Kodi-side notification UX, lsep banner rendering, and `xbmcgui.Window(10000)` property behaviour are exercised in tests with `mock.MagicMock` stand-ins for `xbmcgui` — they are **not** verified against a real Kodi instance in this session. Real-hardware Phase C verification is queued for the operator.

<details><summary>1 inline review comment(s)</summary>

**`chatgpt-codex-connector[bot]`** · 2026-05-29:

**<sub><sub>![P2 Badge](https://img.shields.io/badge/P2-yellow?style=flat)</sub></sub>  Avoid warning on add-on-initiated setting writes**

When a user accepts existing in-add-on helpers that persist settings, such as OPPO discovery applying `oppo_ip`/`oppo_port` or TCL presets applying ADB shell commands in `resources/lib/kodi/installer.py`, those `ADDON.setSetting(...)` calls can trigger this same `onSettingsChanged` path. Because the new hook unconditionally diffs every configurator-managed key, it will log/show the “overwritten via Kodi UI” / “Re-run the configurator” warning even though the change came from an existing add-on flow that just saved it permanently, which makes those helpers look broken or non-persistent. Consider suppressing this warning around known add-on writes or otherwise distinguishing settings-dialog edits from programmatic updates.

Useful? React with 👍 / 👎.

</details>

### #40 — Strip the in-Kodi setup wizard from the addon [MERGED]
## Theme

Strip the in-Kodi setup wizard from the add-on. The Windows configurator
(`configurator/`) now owns first-run setup — it writes
`playercorefactory.xml` and the remote-bridge keymap into Kodi userdata, seeds
add-on settings, and runs the player/TV/AVR probes that used to live in the
in-Kodi wizard dialog flow. Keeping a redundant wizard inside the add-on
confused users (which path to follow?) and was the source of the persistent
`No module named 'wizard'` launch bug (issue #22, referenced not closed per
norm).

## Scope (per operator decision: total strip)

**Production code removed:**
- `resources/lib/wizard.py` (807 lines — run_wizard / reset_wizard / run_avr_setup_wizard / WIZARD_TEXT)
- `resources/lib/wizard_polish.py` (pure-function nav model wrapped by wizard.py)
- `resources/lib/first_run_wizard.py` (the misleadingly-named v0.9.14 compatibility-preset helpers used by `service.py.Monitor.onSettingsChanged`)
- `autoscript_helper.run_autoscript_wizard` + its xbmcgui-bound `_yn`/`_ok`/`_in`/`_sel`/`_profile` helpers. `generate()` and `write_script()` remain as pure functions.

**Behavioural change (per total-strip choice):**
- `service.py.Monitor.onSettingsChanged` no longer auto-applies compatibility presets / warnings when the user changes the hardware model in Kodi settings. That responsibility moves to the configurator. The `Monitor` subclass is now a no-op shell; `abortRequested`/`waitForAbort` are inherited from `xbmc.Monitor`.

**`installer.main()` menu shrinks:**
- Lost: "Run first-run wizard", "Reset first-run wizard", "Generate Chinoppo AutoScript".
- Lost: the wizard auto-launch on first run.
- Kept: every non-wizard menu item (file generation, preview, discovery, TCL helper, file-list diagnostic, readiness/AVR exports). The architecture-choice first-run dialog still fires when `architecture_choice_made` is unset.

**Settings / strings:**
- `resources/settings.xml`: dropped the hidden `wizard_mode` setting; renamed `<category id="wizard">` → `<category id="playback">`.
- `resources/lib/i18n.py`: cleared the `_EN` fallback table (only held #31xxx wizard strings). `L()` itself is unchanged.
- 12 PO files: removed `#30910/#30920/#30930/#30940/#30950` wizard-setting labels, the full `#31000-#31061` v1.0.6 wizard block, retitled `#32103` → "Playback" and `#32113` → "Playback-architecture knobs."

**Tests:**
- Deleted 5 wizard-exclusive test files and 8 `test_superset_merge_build*.py` files (wizard + first_run_wizard + service watcher persistence merge slices).
- Surgical edits to `test_all.py`, `test_coverage_99.py`, `test_coverage_hardening.py`, `test_coverage_gate_99_restore.py`, `test_transfer_file_generation.py`, `test_v250_build5_diagnostic_logging.py`, `test_v253_build2_xml_option4.py`.
- Restored `test_v2910_build16_avr_wizard_diagnostics.py` with wizard.py-dependent halves stripped (`avr_diagnostics.wizard_capabilities` / `wizard_family_options` / `apply_wizard_selection` are kept as a pure-data API for the configurator).
- New `TStripWizard*` test classes lock the post-strip surface: `installer.main()` over each menu choice, discovery multi-result + exception, file-list 0/50+ entries, `settings_reader.save_settings` persistence + empty-dir refusal, `hardware_capabilities` player guidance per class, `autoscript` chmod-failure swallow, `write_script` line-ending normalisation.

**Docs:**
- `README.md` Installation step 4 directs users to the configurator. Historical-reconstruction section preserved verbatim.
- `docs/testing-strategy.md` drops the wizard/installer UI framing.
- `scripts/hooks/pre-push` and `.coveragerc` comments updated.
- `addon.xml` version and description **not** updated — that description is a multi-version historical release log; the operator will refresh at the next version bump.

## Verification (this commit, software-only — hardware not claimed)

|---|---|---|
| compile | `python -m py_compile service.py default.py` | OK |
| lint | `python -m ruff check service.py default.py resources/` | All checks passed |

Hardware validation not performed / not claimed.

## Fallout

### #39 — Wip/wizard ux [CLOSED]
# Pull Request Checklist

## Summary

Describe the change in a few sentences. Include the build name if this PR is part of a GitHub Readiness build.

## Scope

- [ ] Documentation only
- [ ] Tests/tooling only
- [ ] Runtime code change
- [ ] Packaging/release change
- [ ] Hardware-validation evidence update

## Protected behavior

- [ ] I did not change protected playback/routing behavior unless explicitly documented.
- [ ] I did not change OPPO command payload behavior unless explicitly documented.
- [ ] I did not change TV/AVR sequencing behavior unless explicitly documented.

**<sub><sub>![P2 Badge](https://img.shields.io/badge/P2-yellow?style=flat)</sub></sub>  Drop unsupported --sort from gh issue list**

When `resume` reaches these issue-list commands, `gh issue list` will reject `--sort` before returning any issues. I checked the GitHub CLI manual for `gh issue list`: its options include `--label`, `--limit`, `--search`, and `--state`, but no `--sort`; sorting is only available through search qualifiers like `--search "sort:created-asc"` or by post-processing the JSON. Because the same unsupported flag is repeated for both areas, the new per-area briefing path will fail in normal use.

Useful? React with 👍 / 👎.

### #35 — configurator: unblock first-time cargo build (icon + lockfile + winget docs) [MERGED]
## Summary

Fourth PR this session — pulls together the "first-time cargo on Windows" gaps that surfaced when the operator authorized installing the full Tauri 2 toolchain (Rust 1.95 + MSVC 14.44 BuildTools 2022), then promotes those installs to **auto** so the next agent's `resume` does the install end-to-end without re-asking.

Two commits:

1. **`configurator: unblock first-time cargo build (icon + lockfile + winget docs)`** — icon + Cargo.lock + .gitattributes + initial §2a winget command. Makes the build runnable but leaves the install as a manual step.
2. **`handoff: promote Rust + MSVC to auto-install in §2a (resume installs them)`** — flips Rust and MSVC to **auto** / **auto (UAC)**, so every future `resume` on a fresh Windows machine installs them silently (Rust) or with one UAC prompt (MSVC).

## Files

| File | Why |
|---|---|
| [`configurator/src-tauri/icons/icon.ico`](configurator/src-tauri/icons/icon.ico) | `tauri.conf.json`'s `bundle.icon` references it; without it `tauri-build` fails at the Windows-resource step **before** any Rust source compiles. 766-byte placeholder (32×32 terracotta "O") generated via PowerShell `System.Drawing`. **Not the real product icon** — that lands with §3 next-step #6 (icon + bundling). |
| [`configurator/src-tauri/Cargo.lock`](configurator/src-tauri/Cargo.lock) | Cargo's official guidance: commit Cargo.lock for binary crates so dep versions don't drift between dev machines. Never gitignored — just never produced. Locks 434 packages against `tauri 2.11.2`. |
| [`.gitattributes`](.gitattributes) | `Cargo.lock text eol=lf` — without it `autocrlf=true` on Windows checks out CRLF, cargo rewrites as LF on every invocation, and git shows a phantom diff forever. |
| [`AI_RESUME_HANDOFF.md`](AI_RESUME_HANDOFF.md) §2a | Row 10 (Rust) → **auto** with dual POSIX/Windows commands. Old combined row 11 split into row 11 (WebView2, manual check only — ships with Win 11) and row 12 (MSVC Build Tools 2022, **auto (UAC)**). Added a "Notes on auto-install behavior" block explaining plain auto vs auto (UAC), and a "what build the Windows binary needs end to end" line mapping rows 7-12 to dev + bundle paths. §1's environment-check branch list extended with the "auto (UAC)" case (warn the operator before triggering UAC). |

Hand-written diff is small (5 lines `.gitattributes` + 14/-4 in `AI_RESUME_HANDOFF.md`); the +4569 in Cargo.lock is auto-generated lockfile content.

## What gets auto-installed on `resume` after this lands

For a fresh Windows machine that has Node + git + gh + Python + WebView2 (i.e. Windows 11 + the existing §2a manual rows satisfied):

1. Rust toolchain (silent winget install, ~250 MB) — no UAC.
2. MSVC Build Tools 2022 with C++ workload (winget install via `Start-Process -Verb RunAs`, ~6 GB) — **one UAC dialog the first time**, operator clicks Yes. Subsequent resumes skip (idempotent — `Test-Path` returns true).

After both: `cd configurator\src-tauri; cargo build` works end to end, unblocking every form of Tauri verification.

## Verification

- [x] `cd configurator\src-tauri; cargo build` — `Finished 'dev' profile [unoptimized + debuginfo] target(s) in 36.62s` (rustc 1.95.0 + MSVC 14.44.35207). This was the work that proved the icon + lockfile combo unblocks the build.
- [x] Both auto-install commands (Rust + MSVC) verified end to end this session — see PR conversation for the exact `winget` invocations that succeeded.
- [x] All other gates already green on the three sibling PRs ([#32](https://github.com/skull-01/script.oppo203.iso.external/pull/32), [#33](https://github.com/skull-01/script.oppo203.iso.external/pull/33), [#34](https://github.com/skull-01/script.oppo203.iso.external/pull/34)) — none touch the files in this PR.

## Out of scope (intentionally)

- **Real product icon design + the other icon formats** (`32x32.png`, `128x128.png`, `icon.icns`) — needed for `tauri build` (full bundle) on Linux/macOS but not for `cargo build` / `tauri dev`. Fits the §6 icon + bundling theme.
- **`tauri/cargo` CI step** — would let GitHub Actions catch Rust regressions automatically; suggested if configurator iteration becomes frequent.
- **`package-lock.json` LF normalization** — scoped to Cargo.lock only here.
- **WebView2 auto-install** — left as manual check (Win 11 has it; older Windows users get an install pointer). Auto-installing a system-level browser component felt too invasive for a resume default; revisit if older-Windows operators ask.

## Session note

This is PR #4 of the session, at the AGENTS.md soft cap of 4/session. All four PRs are configurator-follow-up themed; this final one is the smallest-but-most-foundational, unblocking first-time Tauri verification for everyone and making the install part of resume's default behavior going forward.

### #34 — configurator: persist WizardState to %APPDATA% across restarts [MERGED]
## Summary

Per [`AI_RESUME_HANDOFF.md`](AI_RESUME_HANDOFF.md) §3 next-step #3 — third PR in the configurator-follow-up theme (paired with [#32](https://github.com/skull-01/script.oppo203.iso.external/pull/32) doc cleanup and [#33](https://github.com/skull-01/script.oppo203.iso.external/pull/33) window-control IPC; the three are independent and can merge in any order).

The wizard's [`WizardState`](configurator/src/state.ts) was held only in React `useState` — closing and reopening the configurator threw away every answer the user had entered. This PR persists it to a JSON file in the OS app-data dir so the wizard survives restart.

## Implementation

Three files, +70 / −3:

### [`configurator/src-tauri/src/lib.rs`](configurator/src-tauri/src/lib.rs)

Two `#[tauri::command]`s:

```rust
fn load_wizard_state(app: tauri::AppHandle) -> Result<Option<Value>, String>
fn save_wizard_state(app: tauri::AppHandle, state: Value) -> Result<(), String>
```

Both resolve the path via `tauri::Manager::path().app_data_dir()` and serialize via the already-vendored `serde_json` dep. Errors are stringified back to JS. The save path creates the parent directory if needed.

### [`configurator/src/state.ts`](configurator/src/state.ts)

Thin async wrappers around `invoke<T>` from `@tauri-apps/api/core`:

```ts
loadPersistedState(): Promise<WizardState | null>
savePersistedState(state: WizardState): Promise<void>
```

Both `try/catch` and swallow errors — persistence is best-effort and must never block the UI.

### [`configurator/src/App.tsx`](configurator/src/App.tsx)

Two `useEffect`s:

1. **Hydration** on mount: `loadPersistedState()` → if non-null, `setState(loaded)`; flips a `hydrated` flag either way.
2. **Save** on every state change, gated by the `hydrated` flag so the empty `INITIAL_STATE` doesn't clobber persisted data during the brief window before load resolves.

## Scope notes

- **No new deps.** `serde_json` was already in [`Cargo.toml`](configurator/src-tauri/Cargo.toml); `@tauri-apps/api ^2` was already in [`package.json`](configurator/package.json).
- **No capabilities change.** App-level commands defined with `#[tauri::command]` and registered via `generate_handler!` are auto-allowed in Tauri 2 — capabilities only gate *plugin* commands.
- **Persists wizard data only, not the current screen.** Restart re-orients the user at `step0_gate` with their answers intact. Persisting the screen too would require validating that the saved screen id is still defined in the current code version; out of scope for this PR.
- **Actual on-disk path.** Tauri 2's `app_data_dir()` resolves to `%APPDATA%\com.script-oppo203-iso-external.configurator\state.json` (uses the bundle identifier from [`tauri.conf.json`](configurator/src-tauri/tauri.conf.json)). §3 mentioned the prettier `OppoKodiAddonConfigurator/` name — adjustable in a follow-up by joining `data_dir().join("OppoKodiAddonConfigurator")` instead, if you prefer the human-readable name.

## Test plan

- [x] `cd configurator; npx tsc --noEmit` — clean (exit 0)
- [x] `cd configurator; npm run build` — clean (49 modules / 25.39 KB CSS / 215.38 KB JS / 329ms; +2 modules and +0.4 KB JS vs. pre-PR for the `invoke` import chain)
- [x] `pytest -n auto --basetemp=build\_pt` — 987 passed, 3 skipped in 8.66s (unaffected)
- [x] **`cargo check` (Rust typecheck)** — clean, finished in 6.00s against tauri 2.11.2.
- [x] **`cargo build` (full Rust compile + MSVC link)** — clean, dev profile, finished in 36.62s on rustc 1.95.0 + MSVC 14.44.35207. Required adding a *local-only* placeholder `configurator/src-tauri/icons/icon.ico` to unblock tauri-build's Windows-resource step — see "Verification caveat" below.
- [ ] **End-to-end on Windows.** Not yet run. With Rust now in place I can do `npm run tauri dev` and click min/max/close + change a wizard field + close-reopen to confirm restore. Will do on request — kept out of this update so the PR doesn't drift.

## Verification caveat — pre-existing missing icon

[`configurator/src-tauri/tauri.conf.json`](configurator/src-tauri/tauri.conf.json) declares `icons/icon.ico` (and three other icon files) but the icons directory ships with **only a `README.md`** — the actual icon files were never committed (gap from PR #30; see its body's "real app icon (placeholder)" note). Without `icon.ico`, `cargo build`/`tauri-build` fails at the Windows-resource generation step before ever compiling our crate's `lib.rs`.

To verify the Rust in this PR I generated a 766-byte placeholder `icon.ico` (32×32 terracotta "O") via PowerShell `System.Drawing` and put it in `configurator/src-tauri/icons/` **locally**. It is NOT in this PR. The Rust verification above is therefore "true in any tree that has *some* `icon.ico` present" — which is anyone who unblocks the same icon gap.

A separate small PR (or fold into the §3 next-step #6 "app icon + bundling" theme) should commit a placeholder icon so the build is unblocked for every subsequent agent / operator without local fixup.

### #33 — configurator: wire window-control IPC on custom title bar [MERGED]
## Summary

Per [`AI_RESUME_HANDOFF.md`](AI_RESUME_HANDOFF.md) §3 next-step #2 — picked up now that PR #30 has merged.

The custom Windows-style title bar in [`WinShell.tsx`](configurator/src/shell/WinShell.tsx) had:

- Three buttons (min / max / close) with **no `onClick` handlers** — pure decoration.
- No drag region anywhere — the window opened where Tauri put it and couldn't be moved.
- Stale `-webkit-app-region: no-drag` CSS in [`styles.css`](configurator/src/styles.css) that does nothing in Tauri (Electron-era idiom).

PR #30 already declared the matching window-control capabilities in [`capabilities/default.json`](configurator/src-tauri/capabilities/default.json):

```
core:window:allow-minimize
core:window:allow-maximize
core:window:allow-unmaximize
core:window:allow-toggle-maximize
core:window:allow-close
core:window:allow-start-dragging
```

So this PR is **JS-only** — no Rust, no `tauri.conf.json`, no capabilities. Single file: [`WinShell.tsx`](configurator/src/shell/WinShell.tsx), +26 / −4.

## Change

Three things:

1. **Import** `getCurrentWindow` from `@tauri-apps/api/window` (already a dep — `^2`).
2. **Wire onClick handlers** on the three buttons → `minimize()` / `toggleMaximize()` / `close()`. The handlers `void` the returned `Promise` to satisfy `no-floating-promises` style without requiring `await` in event handlers.
3. **Add `data-tauri-drag-region=""`** on the outer `.titlebar` div. Tauri 2 checks `event.target` and walks ancestors looking for the attribute — interactive children (the three `<button>`s) still receive their own clicks, but mousedown on the empty title-area and spacer initiates a drag-to-move.

`tabIndex={-1}` kept on the buttons (Windows-native title bars aren't Tab-focusable).

## Out of scope (intentionally)

- **Removing the stale `-webkit-app-region: no-drag` CSS.** It's harmless dead code — a separate small CSS-cleanup PR if you care.
- **State persistence** (handoff §3 next-step #3) — coming next as its own PR.
- **App icon** (next-step #6) — also separate.

## Test plan

- [x] `cd configurator; npx tsc --noEmit` — clean (exit 0)
- [x] `cd configurator; npm run build` — clean (53 modules / 25.39 KB CSS / 230.32 KB JS / 380ms; +6 modules and +15 KB JS vs. pre-PR, all from the `@tauri-apps/api/window` chain)
- [x] `pytest -n auto --basetemp=build\_pt` — 987 passed, 3 skipped in 7.88s (unaffected, as expected)
- [ ] **Native click-through on Windows** — needs `cargo` (Rust 1.77+) installed; not present in this environment per §2a row 10. The functional verification (clicking min/max/close, dragging the title bar) is gated on the operator running `cd configurator; npm run tauri dev` on their Windows host. Software-verified; hardware validation not claimed.

The commits look like real wizard-module work (player presets, install paths, PO header fix) — not obviously stale. Pruning needs operator judgment, not a doc cleanup. Flagging here for separate triage.
- **`ruff format --check resources default.py service.py`.** CI runs both `check` and `format --check`; AGENTS.md only mentions `check`. Adding `format` to the local gate list would be an enhancement to the contract, not a fix; left for a future PR if wanted.

## Test plan

### #30 — Scaffold OppoKodiAddon Configurator (Tauri 2 + React) under configurator/ [MERGED]
## Summary

Stands up the directory and build chain for the **OppoKodiAddon Configurator** — a Windows app that *configures* the already-installed `script.oppo203.iso.external` Kodi add-on. The product is built from the design in [`docs/installuidraft/design_handoff_oppo_installer/`](../tree/claude/windows-installer-ui-gfv4m/docs/installuidraft/design_handoff_oppo_installer).

### Naming note

The Kodi add-on is installed via Kodi's normal add-on mechanism (the `script.oppo203.iso.external-*.zip` artifact). This Windows app does **not** install the add-on — it sets it up: writes `playercorefactory.xml` + the remote-bridge keymap into Kodi's `userdata/`, probes the user's TV/player, and captures HDMI input topology. "Installer" was the legacy word from the design handoff; this PR uses "configurator" throughout.

### What's in

- **Stack:** Tauri 2 (Rust core) + Vite + React 18 + TypeScript, picked because the React component structure in `prototype/screens-1.jsx` and `screens-2.jsx` lifts over with minimal rework.
- **Aesthetic:** Direction A (Warm Paper) only — terracotta `#C2410C`, DM Sans, light + dark mode. The other two aesthetic directions and the design-time tweaks panel are intentionally dropped.
- **Shell is fully functional:** custom Windows-11-style title bar, persistent chain diagram (`Media → Kodi → TV ⇄ Player`), stepper / sidebar / minimal progress variants, screen-entry animation.
- **Router walks all 23 screens:** Step 0 (gate + media-source exit branch) is ported faithfully from the prototype. The other 21 screens are TODO-marked stubs with `back`/`next` wired through `FooterNav` so the entire flow is testable end to end before each one is filled in.
- **Reusable building blocks ready:** `WinShell`, `Chain`, `Progress`, `Sidebar`, `AppHeader`, `FooterNav`, `DiagLog`, `Icon` (30+ inline SVGs), `WizardState` type + `computeCompleted` derivation.

## Layout

```
configurator/
├── README.md                 ← dev/build instructions + next milestones
├── package.json              ← oppokodiaddon-configurator; React 18, Vite 5, @tauri-apps/api ^2
├── tsconfig*.json, vite.config.ts
├── index.html                ← loads DM Sans + JetBrains Mono from Google Fonts
├── src/
│   ├── App.tsx               ← router + state, 23-screen registry
│   ├── styles.css            ← Direction A tokens + component CSS
│   ├── state.ts, steps.ts    ← WizardState, screen↔step↔chain maps
│   ├── icons.tsx             ← the prototype's full icon set, typed
│   ├── shell/                ← WinShell, Chain, Progress, Sidebar, AppHeader, FooterNav, DiagLog
│   └── screens/              ← Step0Gate, Step0Exit (ported); stubs.tsx (21 placeholders)
└── src-tauri/
    ├── Cargo.toml            ← oppokodiaddon-configurator / oppokodiaddon_configurator_lib
    ├── build.rs
    ├── tauri.conf.json       ← 1180×820 default, 1000×720 min, decorations off
    │                           identifier com.script-oppo203-iso-external.configurator
    ├── capabilities/default.json
    └── src/{main,lib}.rs
```

## Packaging boundary

The Kodi add-on's installable zip is allowlist-driven — only `addon.xml`, `default.py`, `service.py`, and `resources/` ship. `configurator/` is excluded by default; verified with `test_g8_runtime_packaging_excludes_publication_and_readiness_docs`. Defensive updates also landed in root `.gitignore` (node_modules, target/, dist/) and `ruff.toml` (excludes `configurator/`).

Note: `resources/lib/installer.py` is a pre-existing module — it's the *add-on's* internal config-file writer. The Windows configurator will eventually drive it over SSH/SMB. Unrelated to the directory rename; left alone.

## Test plan

- [x] `npx tsc --noEmit` — clean
- [x] `npm run build` — vite production build succeeds (25 KB CSS, 160 KB JS)
- [x] `pytest -q` — all 990 add-on tests pass (after the rename too)
- [ ] Open the wizard on Windows and click through all 23 screens (`cd configurator && npm install && npm run tauri dev`) — needs a Windows host with the Tauri 2 prerequisites; not runnable from this CI/cloud env
- [ ] Visual diff against the prototype HTML (`docs/installuidraft/.../prototype/OPPO Installer Wizard.html`) — should be pixel-close for Step 0 and the shell, stubs are deliberately marked

## Not in this PR

- Porting the remaining 21 screens (each is < 120 lines in the prototype)
- Real side effects behind the diag logs (SFTP / SMB / TCP probes / ADB / Roku ECP / Sony / `#EJT`+`#QPW` for OPPO clones)
- State persistence to `%APPDATA%/OppoKodiAddonConfigurator/state.json`
- Real `playercorefactory.xml` + keymap file generation
- Real app icon (placeholder `O`-on-gradient title bar icon)
- Branch name still says `windows-installer-ui-` — not worth re-pushing

### #29 — Fix broken claude-review CI: allow dependabot-initiated runs [MERGED]
## What

Adds `allowed_bots: 'dependabot'` to `.github/workflows/claude-code-review.yml`.

## Why

Every claude-review run on our dependabot PRs (#23–#28) has been failing with:

```
Action failed with error: Workflow initiated by non-human actor:
dependabot (type: Bot). Add bot to allowed_bots list or use '*' to
allow all bots.
```

The `anthropics/claude-code-action@v1` refuses bot-initiated runs by default — that's the documented mitigation against an attacker turning code review into a prompt-injection vehicle. We need it allowed for dependabot specifically because dependabot is what opens our dependency PRs.

Verified against the failing log on PR #28 (run `26529340316`).

## Choice of `'dependabot'` over `'*'`

Narrow on purpose — `'*'` would also allow any future bot integration (Renovate, custom bots, etc.) without re-review. If we add another trusted bot later, extend the list explicitly.

## Doc follow-up

`AI_RESUME_HANDOFF.md` §14 currently says "Fix the broken claude-review CI workflow (bot/secret)". That's not quite right — the OAuth secret is fine, this was just a config gap. Will refresh the handoff after this lands.

---

### #28 — Update pytest-cov requirement from <8,>=5 to >=7.1.0,<8 [MERGED]
> [!WARNING]
> Dependabot will stop supporting `python v3.9`!
> 
> Please upgrade to one of the following versions: `v3.9`, `v3.10`, `v3.11`, `v3.12`, `v3.13`, or `v3.14`.
>

Updates the requirements on [pytest-cov](https://github.com/pytest-dev/pytest-cov) to permit the latest version.
<details>
<summary>Changelog</summary>
<p><em>Sourced from <a href="https://github.com/pytest-dev/pytest-cov/blob/master/CHANGELOG.rst">pytest-cov's changelog</a>.</em></p>
<blockquote>
<h2>7.1.0 (2026-03-21)</h2>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Fixed total coverage computation to always be consistent, regardless of reporting settings.
Previously some reports could produce different total counts, and consequently can make --cov-fail-under behave different depending on
reporting options.
See <code>[#641](https://github.com/pytest-dev/pytest-cov/issues/641) &lt;https://github.com/pytest-dev/pytest-cov/issues/641&gt;</code>_.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Improve handling of ResourceWarning from sqlite3.</p>
<p>The plugin adds warning filter for sqlite3 <code>ResourceWarning</code> unclosed database (since 6.2.0).
It checks if there is already existing plugin for this message by comparing filter regular expression.
When filter is specified on command line the message is escaped and does not match an expected message.
A check for an escaped regular expression is added to handle this case.</p>
<p>With this fix one can suppress <code>ResourceWarning</code> from sqlite3 from command line::</p>
<p>pytest -W &quot;ignore:unclosed database in &lt;sqlite3.Connection object at:ResourceWarning&quot; ...</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Various improvements to documentation.
Contributed by Art Pelling in <code>[#718](https://github.com/pytest-dev/pytest-cov/issues/718) &lt;https://github.com/pytest-dev/pytest-cov/pull/718&gt;</code>_ and
&quot;vivodi&quot; in <code>[#738](https://github.com/pytest-dev/pytest-cov/issues/738) &lt;https://github.com/pytest-dev/pytest-cov/pull/738&gt;</code><em>.
Also closed <code>[#736](https://github.com/pytest-dev/pytest-cov/issues/736) &lt;https://github.com/pytest-dev/pytest-cov/issues/736&gt;</code></em>.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Fixed some assertions in tests.
Contributed by in Markéta Machová in <code>[#722](https://github.com/pytest-dev/pytest-cov/issues/722) &lt;https://github.com/pytest-dev/pytest-cov/pull/722&gt;</code>_.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Removed unnecessary coverage configuration copying (meant as a backup because reporting commands had configuration side-effects before coverage 5.0).</p>
</li>
</ul>
<h2>7.0.0 (2025-09-09)</h2>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Dropped support for subprocesses measurement.</p>
<p>It was a feature added long time ago when coverage lacked a nice way to measure subprocesses created in tests.
It relied on a <code>.pth</code> file, there was no way to opt-out and it created bad interations
with <code>coverage's new patch system &lt;https://coverage.readthedocs.io/en/latest/config.html#run-patch&gt;</code>_ added
in <code>7.10 &lt;https://coverage.readthedocs.io/en/7.10.6/changes.html#version-7-10-0-2025-07-24&gt;</code>_.</p>
<p>To migrate to this release you might need to enable the suprocess patch, example for <code>.coveragerc</code>:</p>
<p>.. code-block:: ini</p>
<p>[run]
patch = subprocess</p>
<p>This release also requires at least coverage 7.10.6.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Switched packaging to have metadata completely in <code>pyproject.toml</code> and use <code>hatchling &lt;https://pypi.org/project/hatchling/&gt;</code>_ for
building.
Contributed by Ofek Lev in <code>[#551](https://github.com/pytest-dev/pytest-cov/issues/551) &lt;https://github.com/pytest-dev/pytest-cov/pull/551&gt;</code>_
with some extras in <code>[#716](https://github.com/pytest-dev/pytest-cov/issues/716) &lt;https://github.com/pytest-dev/pytest-cov/pull/716&gt;</code>_.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Removed some not really necessary testing deps like <code>six</code>.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<!-- raw HTML omitted -->
</blockquote>
<p>... (truncated)</p>
</details>

### #27 — Update pytest-xdist requirement from <4,>=3 to >=3.8.0,<4 [MERGED]
> [!WARNING]
> Dependabot will stop supporting `python v3.9`!
> 
> Please upgrade to one of the following versions: `v3.9`, `v3.10`, `v3.11`, `v3.12`, `v3.13`, or `v3.14`.
>

Updates the requirements on [pytest-xdist](https://github.com/pytest-dev/pytest-xdist) to permit the latest version.
<details>
<summary>Changelog</summary>
<p><em>Sourced from <a href="https://github.com/pytest-dev/pytest-xdist/blob/master/CHANGELOG.rst">pytest-xdist's changelog</a>.</em></p>
<blockquote>
<h1>pytest-xdist 3.8.0 (2025-06-30)</h1>
<h2>Features</h2>
<ul>
<li>
<p><code>[#1083](https://github.com/pytest-dev/pytest-xdist/issues/1083) &lt;https://github.com/pytest-dev/pytest-xdist/issues/1083&gt;</code>_: Add <code>--no-loadscope-reorder</code> and <code>--loadscope-reorder</code> option to control whether to automatically reorder tests in loadscope for tests where relative ordering matters. This only applies when using <code>loadscope</code>.</p>
<p>For example, [test_file_1, test_file_2, ..., test_file_n] are given as input test files, if <code>--no-loadscope-reorder</code> is used, for either worker, the <code>test_file_a</code> will be executed before <code>test_file_b</code> only if <code>a &lt; b</code>.</p>
<p>The default behavior is to reorder the tests to maximize the number of tests that can be executed in parallel.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<h1>pytest-xdist 3.7.0 (2025-05-26)</h1>
<h2>Features</h2>
<ul>
<li>
<p><code>[#1142](https://github.com/pytest-dev/pytest-xdist/issues/1142) &lt;https://github.com/pytest-dev/pytest-xdist/issues/1142&gt;</code>_: Added support for Python 3.13.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>[#1144](https://github.com/pytest-dev/pytest-xdist/issues/1144) &lt;https://github.com/pytest-dev/pytest-xdist/issues/1144&gt;</code>_: The internal <code>steal</code> command is now atomic - it unschedules either all requested tests or none.</p>
<p>This is a prerequisite for group/scope support in the <code>worksteal</code> scheduler, so test groups won't be broken up incorrectly.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>[#1170](https://github.com/pytest-dev/pytest-xdist/issues/1170) &lt;https://github.com/pytest-dev/pytest-xdist/issues/1170&gt;</code>_: Add the <code>--px</code> arg to create proxy gateways.</p>
<p>Proxy gateways are passed to additional gateways using the <code>via</code> keyword.
They can serve as a way to run multiple workers on remote machines.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>[#1200](https://github.com/pytest-dev/pytest-xdist/issues/1200) &lt;https://github.com/pytest-dev/pytest-xdist/issues/1200&gt;</code>_: Now multiple <code>xdist_group</code> markers are considered when assigning tests to groups (order does not matter).</p>
<p>Previously, only the last marker would assign a test to a group, but now if a test has multiple <code>xdist_group</code> marks applied (for example via parametrization or via fixtures), they are merged to make a new group.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<h2>Removals</h2>
<ul>
<li><code>[#1162](https://github.com/pytest-dev/pytest-xdist/issues/1162) &lt;https://github.com/pytest-dev/pytest-xdist/issues/1162&gt;</code>_: Dropped support for EOL Python 3.8.</li>
</ul>
<h2>Trivial Changes</h2>
<ul>
<li>
<p><code>[#1092](https://github.com/pytest-dev/pytest-xdist/issues/1092) &lt;https://github.com/pytest-dev/pytest-xdist/issues/1092&gt;</code>_: Update an error message to better indicate where users should go for more information.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>[#1190](https://github.com/pytest-dev/pytest-xdist/issues/1190) &lt;https://github.com/pytest-dev/pytest-xdist/issues/1190&gt;</code>_: Switched to using a SPDX license identifier introduced in PEP 639.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<h1>pytest-xdist 3.6.1 (2024-04-28)</h1>
<!-- raw HTML omitted -->
</blockquote>
<p>... (truncated)</p>
</details>

### #25 — Bump actions/download-artifact from 4 to 8 [MERGED]
Bumps [actions/download-artifact](https://github.com/actions/download-artifact) from 4 to 8.
<details>
<summary>Release notes</summary>
<p><em>Sourced from <a href="https://github.com/actions/download-artifact/releases">actions/download-artifact's releases</a>.</em></p>
<blockquote>
<h2>v8.0.0</h2>
<h2>v8 - What's new</h2>
<blockquote>
<p>[!IMPORTANT]
actions/download-artifact@v8 has been migrated to an ESM module. This should be transparent to the caller but forks might need to make significant changes.</p>
</blockquote>
<blockquote>
<p>[!IMPORTANT]
Hash mismatches will now error by default. Users can override this behavior with a setting change (see below).</p>
</blockquote>
<h3>Direct downloads</h3>
<p>To support direct uploads in <code>actions/upload-artifact</code>, the action will no longer attempt to unzip all downloaded files. Instead, the action checks the <code>Content-Type</code> header ahead of unzipping and skips non-zipped files. Callers wishing to download a zipped file as-is can also set the new <code>skip-decompress</code> parameter to <code>true</code>.</p>
<h3>Enforced checks (breaking)</h3>
<p>A previous release introduced digest checks on the download. If a download hash didn't match the expected hash from the server, the action would log a warning. Callers can now configure the behavior on mismatch with the <code>digest-mismatch</code> parameter. To be secure by default, we are now defaulting the behavior to <code>error</code> which will fail the workflow run.</p>
<h3>ESM</h3>
<p>To support new versions of the @actions/* packages, we've upgraded the package to ESM.</p>
<h2>What's Changed</h2>
<ul>
<li>Don't attempt to un-zip non-zipped downloads by <a href="https://github.com/danwkennedy"><code>@​danwkennedy</code></a> in <a href="https://redirect.github.com/actions/download-artifact/pull/460">actions/download-artifact#460</a></li>
<li>Add a setting to specify what to do on hash mismatch and default it to <code>error</code> by <a href="https://github.com/danwkennedy"><code>@​danwkennedy</code></a> in <a href="https://redirect.github.com/actions/download-artifact/pull/461">actions/download-artifact#461</a></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Full Changelog</strong>: <a href="https://github.com/actions/download-artifact/compare/v7...v8.0.0">https://github.com/actions/download-artifact/compare/v7...v8.0.0</a></p>
<h2>v7.0.0</h2>
<h2>v7 - What's new</h2>
<blockquote>
<p>[!IMPORTANT]
actions/download-artifact@v7 now runs on Node.js 24 (<code>runs.using: node24</code>) and requires a minimum Actions Runner version of 2.327.1. If you are using self-hosted runners, ensure they are updated before upgrading.</p>
</blockquote>
<h3>Node.js 24</h3>
<p>This release updates the runtime to Node.js 24. v6 had preliminary support for Node 24, however this action was by default still running on Node.js 20. Now this action by default will run on Node.js 24.</p>
<h2>What's Changed</h2>
<ul>
<li>Update GHES guidance to include reference to Node 20 version by <a href="https://github.com/patrikpolyak"><code>@​patrikpolyak</code></a> in <a href="https://redirect.github.com/actions/download-artifact/pull/440">actions/download-artifact#440</a></li>
<li>Download Artifact Node24 support by <a href="https://github.com/salmanmkc"><code>@​salmanmkc</code></a> in <a href="https://redirect.github.com/actions/download-artifact/pull/415">actions/download-artifact#415</a></li>
<li>fix: update <code>@​actions/artifact</code> to fix Node.js 24 punycode deprecation by <a href="https://github.com/salmanmkc"><code>@​salmanmkc</code></a> in <a href="https://redirect.github.com/actions/download-artifact/pull/451">actions/download-artifact#451</a></li>
<li>prepare release v7.0.0 for Node.js 24 support by <a href="https://github.com/salmanmkc"><code>@​salmanmkc</code></a> in <a href="https://redirect.github.com/actions/download-artifact/pull/452">actions/download-artifact#452</a></li>
</ul>
<h2>New Contributors</h2>
<ul>
<li><a href="https://github.com/patrikpolyak"><code>@​patrikpolyak</code></a> made their first contribution in <a href="https://redirect.github.com/actions/download-artifact/pull/440">actions/download-artifact#440</a></li>
<li><a href="https://github.com/salmanmkc"><code>@​salmanmkc</code></a> made their first contribution in <a href="https://redirect.github.com/actions/download-artifact/pull/415">actions/download-artifact#415</a></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Full Changelog</strong>: <a href="https://github.com/actions/download-artifact/compare/v6.0.0...v7.0.0">https://github.com/actions/download-artifact/compare/v6.0.0...v7.0.0</a></p>
<h2>v6.0.0</h2>
<!-- raw HTML omitted -->
</blockquote>
<p>... (truncated)</p>
</details>

<ul>

### #24 — Bump actions/upload-artifact from 4 to 7 [MERGED]
Bumps [actions/upload-artifact](https://github.com/actions/upload-artifact) from 4 to 7.
<details>
<summary>Release notes</summary>
<p><em>Sourced from <a href="https://github.com/actions/upload-artifact/releases">actions/upload-artifact's releases</a>.</em></p>
<blockquote>
<h2>v7.0.0</h2>
<h2>v7 What's new</h2>
<h3>Direct Uploads</h3>
<p>Adds support for uploading single files directly (unzipped). Callers can set the new <code>archive</code> parameter to <code>false</code> to skip zipping the file during upload. Right now, we only support single files. The action will fail if the glob passed resolves to multiple files. The <code>name</code> parameter is also ignored with this setting. Instead, the name of the artifact will be the name of the uploaded file.</p>
<h3>ESM</h3>
<p>To support new versions of the <code>@actions/*</code> packages, we've upgraded the package to ESM.</p>
<h2>What's Changed</h2>
<ul>
<li>Add proxy integration test by <a href="https://github.com/Link"><code>@​Link</code></a>- in <a href="https://redirect.github.com/actions/upload-artifact/pull/754">actions/upload-artifact#754</a></li>
<li>Upgrade the module to ESM and bump dependencies by <a href="https://github.com/danwkennedy"><code>@​danwkennedy</code></a> in <a href="https://redirect.github.com/actions/upload-artifact/pull/762">actions/upload-artifact#762</a></li>
<li>Support direct file uploads by <a href="https://github.com/danwkennedy"><code>@​danwkennedy</code></a> in <a href="https://redirect.github.com/actions/upload-artifact/pull/764">actions/upload-artifact#764</a></li>

<h2>New Contributors</h2>
<ul>

</ul>
<p><strong>Full Changelog</strong>: <a href="https://github.com/actions/upload-artifact/compare/v6...v7.0.0">https://github.com/actions/upload-artifact/compare/v6...v7.0.0</a></p>
<h2>v6.0.0</h2>
<h2>v6 - What's new</h2>
<blockquote>
<p>[!IMPORTANT]
actions/upload-artifact@v6 now runs on Node.js 24 (<code>runs.using: node24</code>) and requires a minimum Actions Runner version of 2.327.1. If you are using self-hosted runners, ensure they are updated before upgrading.</p>
</blockquote>
<h3>Node.js 24</h3>
<p>This release updates the runtime to Node.js 24. v5 had preliminary support for Node.js 24, however this action was by default still running on Node.js 20. Now this action by default will run on Node.js 24.</p>
<h2>What's Changed</h2>
<ul>
<li>Upload Artifact Node 24 support by <a href="https://github.com/salmanmkc"><code>@​salmanmkc</code></a> in <a href="https://redirect.github.com/actions/upload-artifact/pull/719">actions/upload-artifact#719</a></li>
<li>fix: update <code>@​actions/artifact</code> for Node.js 24 punycode deprecation by <a href="https://github.com/salmanmkc"><code>@​salmanmkc</code></a> in <a href="https://redirect.github.com/actions/upload-artifact/pull/744">actions/upload-artifact#744</a></li>
<li>prepare release v6.0.0 for Node.js 24 support by <a href="https://github.com/salmanmkc"><code>@​salmanmkc</code></a> in <a href="https://redirect.github.com/actions/upload-artifact/pull/745">actions/upload-artifact#745</a></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Full Changelog</strong>: <a href="https://github.com/actions/upload-artifact/compare/v5.0.0...v6.0.0">https://github.com/actions/upload-artifact/compare/v5.0.0...v6.0.0</a></p>
<h2>v5.0.0</h2>
<h2>What's Changed</h2>
<p><strong>BREAKING CHANGE:</strong> this update supports Node <code>v24.x</code>. This is not a breaking change per-se but we're treating it as such.</p>
<ul>
<li>Update README.md by <a href="https://github.com/GhadimiR"><code>@​GhadimiR</code></a> in <a href="https://redirect.github.com/actions/upload-artifact/pull/681">actions/upload-artifact#681</a></li>
<li>Update README.md by <a href="https://github.com/nebuk89"><code>@​nebuk89</code></a> in <a href="https://redirect.github.com/actions/upload-artifact/pull/712">actions/upload-artifact#712</a></li>
<li>Readme: spell out the first use of GHES by <a href="https://github.com/danwkennedy"><code>@​danwkennedy</code></a> in <a href="https://redirect.github.com/actions/upload-artifact/pull/727">actions/upload-artifact#727</a></li>

- `@dependabot ignore this minor version` will close this PR and stop Dependabot creating any more for this minor version (unless you reopen the PR or upgrade to it yourself)

<blockquote>
<h2>v6.0.0</h2>
<h2>What's Changed</h2>
<ul>
<li>Update README to include Node.js 24 support details and requirements by <a href="https://github.com/salmanmkc"><code>@​salmanmkc</code></a> in <a href="https://redirect.github.com/actions/checkout/pull/2248">actions/checkout#2248</a></li>

<p><strong>Full Changelog</strong>: <a href="https://github.com/actions/checkout/compare/v5.0.0...v6.0.0">https://github.com/actions/checkout/compare/v5.0.0...v6.0.0</a></p>
<h2>v6-beta</h2>
<h2>What's Changed</h2>
<p>Updated persist-credentials to store the credentials under <code>$RUNNER_TEMP</code> instead of directly in the local git config.</p>
<p>This requires a minimum Actions Runner version of <a href="https://github.com/actions/runner/releases/tag/v2.329.0">v2.329.0</a> to access the persisted credentials for <a href="https://docs.github.com/en/actions/tutorials/use-containerized-services/create-a-docker-container-action">Docker container action</a> scenarios.</p>
<h2>v5.0.1</h2>
<h2>What's Changed</h2>
<ul>
<li>Port v6 cleanup to v5 by <a href="https://github.com/ericsciple"><code>@​ericsciple</code></a> in <a href="https://redirect.github.com/actions/checkout/pull/2301">actions/checkout#2301</a></li>

### #21 — Add pre-push hook enforcing the 99% coverage gate locally [MERGED]
## Why
The fast loop (`pytest -n auto`) doesn't measure coverage, so a coverage drop — e.g. new wizard/installer code during iteration without matching tests — would only surface in CI. This wires the coverage gate into a **pre-push hook** so it's caught locally first.

Chosen over integrating into `dev_build.py` so the **on-device deploy loop stays fast** (no 13s tax per deploy); the gate runs only when you push.

## What
- **`scripts/hooks/pre-push`** — runs the same parallel pytest-cov gate (Windows temp workaround baked in) and exits nonzero if tests fail or coverage < `.coveragerc` floor (99%). Bypass with `git push --no-verify`.
- **`.gitattributes`** — `scripts/hooks/* text eol=lf` so a CRLF checkout doesn't break the shebang on Windows.
- **Enable per clone:** `git config core.hooksPath scripts/hooks` — added as **auto-row 7** of the resume readiness checklist, so the resume preflight sets it automatically on any machine.
- **`AI_RESUME_HANDOFF.md`** — documents the hook (§2 + §3) and fixes a stale "floor 50%" note left from the gate-99 PR.

## Verified end-to-end
The hook fired on this branch's own push: **987 passed, 3 skipped, 99.08%, ~13s**, push allowed. The failure path is standard — pytest-cov returns nonzero when coverage < floor, so the push is blocked.

Does **not** touch `dev_build.py` (on-device iteration stays fast).

### #20 — Restore 99% coverage gate (un-omit UI modules) [MERGED]
## Why this was cheap
Coverage never actually dropped — only the **floor policy** did (98→50). The four UI/glue modules omitted from measurement (`wizard.py`, `first_run_wizard.py`, `wizard_polish.py`, `installer.py`) were already **94–100% covered** because the suite's `tests/_stubs` fakes drive them for real. With nothing omitted the suite was already ~98%; closing a small enumerated gap brings the whole `resources/lib` package to **99.08%**.

## Phase 1 — close the gaps
New `tests/test_coverage_gate_99_restore.py` (10 tests, local fakes only):
- `installer.export_avr_diagnostic_report` — success / None / getSetting-except paths (was the biggest single gap, ~18 lines)
- `avr_sony_audio` — `build_sony_audio_url` ValueError, `_parse_response` fallback, `_default_post` (mocked urlopen)
- `avr_diagnostics` — `_settings_dict`/`_truthy` fallbacks, controller-unavailable query/action
- `wizard._probe` success/failure, `wizard.avr_wizard_support_metadata` flat import fallback
- `first_run_wizard._ui_call` edge paths
- `hardware_capabilities` class predicates; `avr_sequence`/`tv_diagnostics` `_settings_dict`

## Phase 2 — flip the policy to 99 (kept in sync)
- `.coveragerc`: remove `omit` block, `fail_under` 50→99
- `pyproject.toml [tool.coverage]`: drop `omit`, `fail_under`→99 (was dead config; now aligned)
- `resources/lib/constants.py` `MIN_COVERAGE_PERCENT` 50→99; `tools/audit_release.py` default 50→99
- test assertions updated: `test_all.py` (×2), `g5_tooling_config`, `build2_disc_classification`
- docs reframed: `testing-strategy.md`, `AI_RESUME_HANDOFF.md`, `AI_RESUME_GUIDE.md`
- **untouched:** historical `fail_under=98` in `test_all.py` (reads frozen evidence)

## Pragmas (1 line, justified)
- `tv_control.py:13` `except ImportError:` — the relative-import fallback only runs on-device (top-level import always resolves in the flat test env), so it can't be exercised in CI. The remaining handful of uncovered lines are the same flat-vs-package import shims, left visible.

## Coverage: before → after
| | Before (omit) | After (no omit) |
|---|---|---|
| Measured stmts | 4628 | 5593 |
| Coverage | 98.70% (gate 50) | **99.08% (gate 99)** |

## Validation
- **987 passed, 3 skipped**; coverage **99.08%**, `fail_under=99` enforced.
- Release audit **PASS (580/580)** — `coverage_gate - fail_under=99`.
- `render_docs --check`, `sync_version --check` green.
- Runtime unchanged (~14s gate; the gate value has zero runtime cost).

### #19 — Speed up the test loop: stop walking .venv in make_pot, fix avr network-timeout test [MERGED]
## Result
Fast-loop wall: **~17.9s → ~9.8s** (−45%). Coverage gate also dropped (**~25s → ~15s**) since the slow tests it runs are now fast.

## Root cause (not what the task assumed)
The task framed these as cold-subprocess-spawn costs. The real bottleneck was an **unbounded `os.walk` into `.venv`**:
- `tools/make_pot.py:collect_ids` walked the whole tree, skipping only `__pycache__/.git/tests/tools/output` — **not `.venv` or `build`**. On this machine the walk visited 1650 `.py` files, **1603 of them inside `.venv`**, tokenizing each.
- `i18n_extract.check_extraction` calls `collect_ids` several times, so `test_i18n_extract_preserves_make_pot_fallback_contract` took **~9.2s**.

Fix: prune vendored/generated/cache dirs in the walk. **Output is identical** (those trees contain no add-on localization ids): `collect_ids` **1.86s → 0.044s**, the 9.2s test **→ 0.19s**, and the subprocess `i18n_extract --check` test (which paid the same walk) **4.13s → 0.15s**.

## Changes
| File | Change |
|---|---|
| `tools/make_pot.py` | Add `_SKIP_DIRS` (.venv, venv, build, dist, node_modules, .mypy_cache, .pytest_cache, .ruff_cache, .tox) and prune them in `_iter_python_files`. Also speeds CI's `i18n_extract --check`. |
| `tests/test_all.py` | Regression test: `.venv`/`build`/etc. are skipped by `collect_ids`. |
| `tests/test_v2910_build16_avr_wizard_diagnostics.py` | The `controller=None` path made a **real TCP connection to a dead host** (~3s SYN timeout). Patch `socket.create_connection` to refuse instantly — same failure-handling path covered, no network I/O. |
| `tests/test_v291_build10_audit_reporter_refactor.py` | Split the CLI test: keep the **text path as the real subprocess smoke**, run the **JSON path in-process via `main()`**. |

## Per-test before → after
| Test | Before | After |
|---|---|---|
| `...build15...preserves_make_pot_fallback_contract` | 9.16s | 0.19s |
| `...build16...reports_build16_alias_policy` | 4.85s | 0.09s |
| `...build15...cli_check_is_non_writing_and_safe` (subprocess smoke, kept) | 4.13s | 0.15s |
| `...build16_query_and_explicit_action_edge_paths` (avr) | 3.01s | ~0s |
| `...build10...audit_cli...` | 2.76s | text 0.48s + json 0.41s |

## Validation
- **977 passed, 3 skipped** (+2: new regression test + audit CLI split).
- Coverage **unchanged at 98.70%** (4628 stmts / 34 missed; floor 50 enforced).
- Release audit **PASS (580/580)**; `render_docs --check` and `sync_version --check` green.

## Note / follow-up
The new floor (~9.8s) is dominated by the many `test_release_audit_*` tests (~1.5s each under xdist contention; `run_audit` is ~0.46s solo). Lowering that further would mean speeding up the release-audit's `compileall` or memoizing it — a broader, gate-sensitive change, out of scope here.

### #18 — Speed up local coverage gate ~3x (parallel via pytest-cov) + worksteal default [MERGED]
## Why
On this machine (Ryzen 7 9800X3D, 8 cores) the local coverage gate ran **serial ~75s** — the machine sat mostly idle — because plain `coverage run -m pytest` can't measure pytest-xdist workers.

## What
- **`requirements-dev.txt`**: add `pytest-cov`.
- Document a **parallel coverage gate** via pytest-cov (starts coverage inside each xdist worker, combines results) in `AI_RESUME_HANDOFF.md` §3 + cheat sheet, `docs/ai-handoff/AI_RESUME_GUIDE.md` §6.4 + §10, and `docs/developer-guide/testing.md`.
- Add **`--dist worksteal`** to the fast test loop (free ~10%; rebalances the few subprocess-spawning tests).

## Results (measured)
| Stage | Before | After |
|---|---|---|
| Coverage gate | ~75s serial | **~25-28s** parallel |
| Fast loop | ~20s (load) | ~17.7s (worksteal) |

Coverage totals are **identical** to serial (4628 stmts / 34 missed / **98.7%**) and the 50% floor is still enforced — so it's correct, not approximate.

## Scope / safety
- **CI is intentionally unchanged** — it runs on 2-core runners and its serial `coverage run` command is pinned by `test_github_readiness_g6_ci_hardening.py`. This PR speeds up the **local** developer workflow only.
- Note in docs: worker count above 8 doesn't help (subprocess-spawning tests oversubscribe the cores); ~17s is the practical fast-loop floor until those tests are refactored to call tool `main()` in-process (queued separately).
- SMT is currently **off** on this CPU (8 logical); enabling it in BIOS would give 16 threads — noted in the guide.

## Validation
- Parallel gate: **975 passed, 3 skipped, 98.70%**, floor enforced.
- `render_docs --check`, `sync_version --check`, and `g5`+`g6` readiness tests all green.

### #17 — Norm: always purge branches once merged [MERGED]
Adds a working norm: **always purge a branch once its PR merges** — merge with `gh pr merge --merge --delete-branch`, then prune any leftover merged local branches (`git branch -d <name>`, `git fetch --prune`). Never leave merged branches lying around.

Captured in all three AI instruction files so the rule stays in sync:
- **AGENTS.md** — Working norms (branch + PR bullet)
- **CLAUDE.md** — the contributor one-liner
- **AI_RESUME_HANDOFF.md** §4 — Build norms

Docs-only; full suite green (975 passed, 3 skipped).

### #16 — Fix parallel test command: load xdist explicitly when autoload is disabled [MERGED]
## Bug
The documented parallel test command set `PYTEST_DISABLE_PLUGIN_AUTOLOAD=1` (matching CI's deterministic plugin set) **and** passed `-n auto`. With autoload off, pytest-xdist never loads, so pytest errors:

```
__main__.py: error: unrecognized arguments: -n
```

## Fix
Add `-p xdist` to load the plugin explicitly, in both:
- `AI_RESUME_HANDOFF.md` §3 (parallel test command)
- `docs/ai-handoff/AI_RESUME_GUIDE.md` §6.2 (deep companion)

Each gets a one-line note explaining why `-p xdist` is required. No version strings touched.

## Validation
`975 passed, 3 skipped` with the corrected command:
```
$env:PYTEST_DISABLE_PLUGIN_AUTOLOAD = "1"; pytest -q -n auto -p xdist --basetemp=build\_pt
```

### #10 — Speed up tests: scope release-audit compile to project, add pytest-xdist [MERGED]
Enables fast parallel local test runs and fixes a latent release-audit bug.

## Problem
`audit_release.audit_compile()` ran `compileall.compile_dir(root, force=True)` over the
**entire** tree — including the in-repo `.venv`. On a dev machine that force-recompiles
all of site-packages on every audit call (slow), and under `pytest-xdist` the parallel
audit subprocesses race writing the same `.pyc` files, failing with `WinError 5`. CI never
hit this (no in-repo `.venv`).

## Fix
- `audit_compile` now skips `.venv`/`venv`/`build`/`dist`/`output`/`.git`/`.pytest_cache`/
  `__pycache__`/`node_modules` via `compile_dir(rx=...)`, and writes throwaway bytecode to
  a private temp dir (`sys.pycache_prefix`) so concurrent runs do not collide. It still
  validates all *project* sources.
- Added `pytest-xdist` to `requirements-dev.txt` for local `pytest -n auto`.

## Results (local, Windows, 8 cores)

| Run | Before | After |
|---|---|---|
| Full suite, `pytest -n auto` | 229s | 16s (~14x) |
| Coverage gate (serial) | 229s | 70s (~3.3x) |

Audit outcome unchanged: `python_compile` still passes, 571/571 PASS. Coverage still 99%.

Note: the coverage gate stays serial (xdist + plain `coverage run` would undercount);
CI is unaffected (no in-repo `.venv`, no `-n` in CI invocations).

---

- First-run wizard and add-on menu now generate complete, ready-to-transfer files instead of XML snippets to merge by hand:
  - a drop-in `playercorefactory.xml`, and
  - a drop-in remote-bridge keymap.
- Files are written to the add-on-data `generated/` folder (mirrors Kodi `userdata` layout) — copy into place and restart Kodi.
- External-player mode writes `playercorefactory.xml` + keymap; service-interception mode writes only the keymap. Generation is non-fatal and never blocks the wizard.
- Add-on now ships a 256x256 icon, so it is no longer blank when installed.

### What did not change
Additive setup-tooling change only. OPPO command semantics, service interception, XML routing, NAS behavior, startup auto-power, TV switching, and AVR sequencing are preserved. No new hardware features.

This is a software-verified release. Hardware validation was not performed or claimed.

### Verification (local, pre-push)
- `sync_version --check`, `render_docs --check` — OK
- `audit_release --expected-version 2.9.12` — PASS (571/571)
- ruff + black (CI scope) — clean
- Full suite: 975 passed, 3 skipped (POSIX-only); coverage 98% (gate 98)
@

---

### #7 — Add-on icon + generate ready-to-transfer setup files [MERGED]
## Summary

Two add-on setup UX improvements:

1. **Add-on icon** — Kodi (Krypton 17+) shows a blank placeholder unless an icon asset is declared. Adds a 256×256 `icon.png` at the add-on root and references it via `<assets><icon>` in `addon.xml`. The installable-ZIP allowlist already reserved `icon.png`, so it ships automatically.

2. **Ready-to-transfer setup files** — the wizard and add-on menu now write complete, drop-in `playercorefactory.xml` and remote-bridge keymap files to `addon_data/<id>/generated/` (mirroring Kodi's `userdata` layout), so the user just copies them across instead of hand-merging snippets.

## Details

`installer.py`
- New `build_playercorefactory_file_xml()` / `build_keymap_file_xml()` emit complete documents without the "add this inside your existing element" merge comments. Factored out `_player_element_xml()`, `_keymap_document_xml()`, and `build_rule_xml(include_merge_comment=...)` so the legacy snippet output is byte-for-byte unchanged.
- New `_generated_paths()`, `write_playercorefactory_file()`, `write_keymap_file()`, and `generate_transfer_files()`; writers take `announce=` so they are chatty from the menu and silent from the wizard.
- Menu items relabelled to write/preview ready-to-copy files; menu indices unchanged. Legacy snippet helpers kept for backward compatibility.

`wizard.py`
- `run_wizard()` generates the files on completion (playercorefactory only in external-player mode; keymap always) and appends the saved paths to the completion dialog. Generation is non-fatal.

## Verification
- Full suite: **975 passed, 3 skipped** (pre-existing POSIX-only release-script skips).
- Coverage gate: **98% TOTAL** (new code fully covered).
- `black --check`, `ruff check`, and `tools/type_check.py` all green.

🤖 Generated with [Claude Code](https://claude.com/claude-code)

### #5 — Make the 8 Windows-only test failures cross-platform [MERGED]
## Summary

The repo's test suite was green on CI (Linux/UTC) but had 8 failures on Windows from latent non-portable behavior. This fixes the **runtime** to be portable and makes the **POSIX-only dev-tooling tests** skip cleanly off-Linux.

## Runtime portability (the Kodi add-on)

- **Path separators** — `diagnostics.default_path` and `preset_manager.save_submission` built addon-data paths with `os.path.join`, which emits `\` on Windows. Switched to `posixpath.join` so paths use `/` on every platform (Kodi's convention).
- **Timezone** — diagnostic/submission export filenames used `time.localtime`, making them depend on the machine's timezone (`…-080000` on UTC+8 vs `…-000000` expected). Switched `diagnostics`, `preset_manager`, `tv_diagnostics`, and `avr_diagnostics` to `time.gmtime` (UTC) so exported support-artifact filenames are deterministic.

## Dev-tooling tests (POSIX release scripts)

`scripts/package_release.sh` is bash + `python3` + `sha256sum` tooling that CI runs on Linux and that can't run on vanilla Windows.

- Skip the three script-dependent tests when POSIX shell tooling is unavailable (`os.name == "nt"` or no `bash`), rather than failing.
- **Fixed a latent bug**: those tests replaced the *entire* subprocess environment (dropping `PATH`/`SystemRoot`), which is fragile even on POSIX. They now merge with `os.environ`.

## Verification (local, Windows, Python 3.12)

- Full suite: **961 passed, 3 skipped, 0 failed** (was 8 failed). The 3 skips are the POSIX scripts; they run and pass on CI's Linux.
- `coverage` — 98% (passes the gate)
- `ruff check` / `black --check` — clean
- `tools/audit_release.py --expected-version 2.9.10` — PASS 553/553

No change to shipped runtime logic beyond path/timestamp formatting.

🤖 Generated with [Claude Code](https://claude.com/claude-code)

<details><summary>1 inline review comment(s)</summary>

**`chatgpt-codex-connector[bot]`** · 2026-05-22:

**<sub><sub>![P2 Badge](https://img.shields.io/badge/P2-yellow?style=flat)</sub></sub>  Detect all required shell tools before unskipping script tests**

The new skip gate only checks `os.name != "nt"` and `bash` presence, but `scripts/package_release.sh` also hard-depends on `python3` and `sha256sum` (see its invocations at lines 6, 16, 23, and 26). On environments like macOS or minimal POSIX images where `bash` exists but `sha256sum` does not, these tests will run and fail instead of being skipped, which contradicts the stated goal of skipping when required POSIX tooling is unavailable. Please include checks for all required executables (or skip on non-Linux) in the gating condition.

Useful? React with 👍 / 👎.

</details>

### #4 — Fix red CI: lint, formatting, and flaky time-mock tests [MERGED]
## Summary

`main`'s CI was failing on **both** the `lint` job (ruff + black) and the `Release gate` job (full pytest). This restores CI to green **without changing runtime behavior** — the release audit stays at 553/553.

## Root causes fixed

1. **Ruff (171 errors)** — the lint config had drifted ahead of the code. Fixes: `%`-format → f-strings, `lambda` → `def`, `raise ... from None`, `capture_output=True`, `getattr(x, "const")` → attribute access, dropped a dead `import re`, and `# noqa: F401` on the **intentional constant re-exports** that tests assert (e.g. `installer.XML_DISC_FILETYPES == dc.XML_DISC_FILETYPES`).
2. **Black (50 files unformatted)** — applied `black` across `resources/`, `default.py`, `service.py` to satisfy the existing `black --check` gate. This is the bulk of the diff and is purely mechanical.
3. **5 `external_player` hold-loop tests → `StopIteration`** — the tests patch `time.time` globally, but `log()` falls back to the stdlib `logging` module (which calls `time.time()`) when `xbmc` is absent — the CI condition — draining the iterator. Suppressed `log()` in those tests so the patched time sequence reaches only the code under test.
4. **`.sh` scripts not executable** — `scripts/verify.sh` / `scripts/package_release.sh` were committed `100644`; the packaging test checks `st_mode & 0o111`. Marked executable.

## Notes

- `service.py` keeps `player = InterceptionPlayer(...)` (with a `# noqa: F841` + comment): Kodi garbage-collects `xbmc.Player` subclasses that aren't referenced, which would silently stop playback callbacks.
- Diff is large (~54 files) but ~50 files are pure `black` reformatting.

## Verification (local, Python 3.12)

- `ruff check` — clean
- `black --check` — clean
- `pytest` — the only remaining failures are Windows-only (path separators, local-timezone filenames, exec-bit reporting, bash subprocess); all pass on CI's Linux/UTC.
- `tools/audit_release.py --expected-version 2.9.10` — PASS 553/553

🤖 Generated with [Claude Code](https://claude.com/claude-code)

<details><summary>2 inline review comment(s)</summary>

**`chatgpt-codex-connector[bot]`** · 2026-05-22:

**<sub><sub>![P1 Badge](https://img.shields.io/badge/P1-orange?style=flat)</sub></sub>  Grant write scopes required for @claude responses**

This workflow only grants `read` on `contents`, `pull-requests`, and `issues`, but the Claude action is expected to post tracking/reply comments and potentially open/update PR artifacts when invoked via `@claude`. In that scenario, GitHub API calls that write to issues/PRs will be rejected (`Resource not accessible by integration`), so the assistant can be triggered but cannot complete its core interaction loop.

Useful? React with 👍 / 👎.

**`chatgpt-codex-connector[bot]`** · 2026-05-22:

**<sub><sub>![P1 Badge](https://img.shields.io/badge/P1-orange?style=flat)</sub></sub>  Permit PR/issue writes for automated code review output**

The review job is configured with read-only PR/issue permissions, but automated review mode needs to publish findings back to the pull request (inline comments/summary or tracking comment). With `pull-requests: read` and `issues: read`, the review can run but cannot post results to the PR, which breaks the purpose of this workflow.

Useful? React with 👍 / 👎.

</details>

### #1 — Bump actions/setup-python from 5 to 6 [MERGED]
Bumps [actions/setup-python](https://github.com/actions/setup-python) from 5 to 6.
<details>
<summary>Release notes</summary>
<p><em>Sourced from <a href="https://github.com/actions/setup-python/releases">actions/setup-python's releases</a>.</em></p>
<blockquote>
<h2>v6.0.0</h2>
<h2>What's Changed</h2>
<h3>Breaking Changes</h3>
<ul>
<li>Upgrade to node 24 by <a href="https://github.com/salmanmkc"><code>@​salmanmkc</code></a> in <a href="https://redirect.github.com/actions/setup-python/pull/1164">actions/setup-python#1164</a></li>
</ul>
<p>Make sure your runner is on version v2.327.1 or later to ensure compatibility with this release. <a href="https://github.com/actions/runner/releases/tag/v2.327.1">See Release Notes</a></p>
<h3>Enhancements:</h3>
<ul>
<li>Add support for <code>pip-version</code>  by <a href="https://github.com/priyagupta108"><code>@​priyagupta108</code></a> in <a href="https://redirect.github.com/actions/setup-python/pull/1129">actions/setup-python#1129</a></li>
<li>Enhance reading from .python-version by <a href="https://github.com/krystof-k"><code>@​krystof-k</code></a> in <a href="https://redirect.github.com/actions/setup-python/pull/787">actions/setup-python#787</a></li>
<li>Add version parsing from Pipfile by <a href="https://github.com/aradkdj"><code>@​aradkdj</code></a> in <a href="https://redirect.github.com/actions/setup-python/pull/1067">actions/setup-python#1067</a></li>
</ul>
<h3>Bug fixes:</h3>
<ul>
<li>Clarify pythonLocation behaviour for PyPy and GraalPy in environment variables by <a href="https://github.com/aparnajyothi-y"><code>@​aparnajyothi-y</code></a> in <a href="https://redirect.github.com/actions/setup-python/pull/1183">actions/setup-python#1183</a></li>
<li>Change missing cache directory error to warning  by <a href="https://github.com/aparnajyothi-y"><code>@​aparnajyothi-y</code></a> in <a href="https://redirect.github.com/actions/setup-python/pull/1182">actions/setup-python#1182</a></li>
<li>Add Architecture-Specific PATH Management for Python with --user Flag on Windows by <a href="https://github.com/aparnajyothi-y"><code>@​aparnajyothi-y</code></a> in <a href="https://redirect.github.com/actions/setup-python/pull/1122">actions/setup-python#1122</a></li>
<li>Include python version in PyPy python-version output by <a href="https://github.com/cdce8p"><code>@​cdce8p</code></a> in <a href="https://redirect.github.com/actions/setup-python/pull/1110">actions/setup-python#1110</a></li>

</ul>

<li>Upgrade setuptools to 78.1.1 to fix path traversal vulnerability in PackageIndex.download by <a href="https://github.com/aparnajyothi-y"><code>@​aparnajyothi-y</code></a> in <a href="https://redirect.github.com/actions/setup-python/pull/1165">actions/setup-python#1165</a></li>
<li>Upgrade actions/checkout from 4 to 5 by <a href="https://github.com/dependabot"><code>@​dependabot</code></a>[bot] in <a href="https://redirect.github.com/actions/setup-python/pull/1181">actions/setup-python#1181</a></li>
<li>Upgrade <code>@​actions/tool-cache</code> from 2.0.1 to 2.0.2 by <a href="https://github.com/dependabot"><code>@​dependabot</code></a>[bot] in <a href="https://redirect.github.com/actions/setup-python/pull/1095">actions/setup-python#1095</a></li>
